 def __init__(self, shots=2000, backend="aer", mitigation=("m3","zne")): ...
 def estimate(self, pauli_op, circuit):
 # builds circuit, compiles to heavy-hex, runs Estimator with mitigation
 # returns pauli_op and variance
 return mean, var

Use it to compute your J_i(h_k) or to score the invariance loss term on a held-out batch. Hardware behind a flag; Aer by default.

Where it meets the publishing stack
 " Every training run still emits signed PDFs with the Noether diagnostics (charge drift plots, invariance deltas, mitigation settings, backend ID). Those PDFs plus JSON sidecars get committed to the content repo and rendered by Shifu next to the Markdown narrative; RDF provenance goes to Whyis. Clean, auditable, human-readable.

Sanity checks (what good looks like)
 " Charge stability: Estimator+M3 on Heron reduces variance enough that the conservation penalty correlates with classical ground truth on Aer. 
 " QAOA utility: On heavy-hex-shaped subgraphs, 23 layer QAOA picks routing schedules measurably better than random/greedy baselines at the same wall-clock. 
 " Reproducibility: Turning hardware off (Aer) reproduces the pipeline; turning it on documents backend, calibration date, mitigation settings in the PDF + RDF.

Self-critique (and upgrades)
 " Hardware variance: Calibration drift is real; always log backend name, date, and mitigation settings, and expect re-runs. Use Heron where possiblequality wins over raw qubit count. 
 " Depth budget: Heavy-hex connectivity penalizes depth with SWAPs. Keep circuits shallow and layout-aware; pre-embed your SU(2) blocks to the coupling map. 
 " Where not to offload: SR heads (symbolic regression) and most geometry/retraction math are better on CPUs/GPUs; quantum doesnt help there today.
 " Open-by-default: IBM hardware is proprietary access. Keep the Qiskit Aer path on by default (Apache-2.0 stack), and gate hardware via config switches.

How it plugs into your stack
 Noetherian multi-algebra plan: the adapter computes Noether charges (e.g., SU(2) angular-momentum proxies) via Estimator; symmetry checks (f(x)=f(g·x)) can run as paired circuits; optional dynamic-circuit guards can emulate your discrete Noether gate.
 QAOA lane: shallow QAOA on a heavy-hex-like subgraph (64 nodes) picks routing schedules or low-rank bracketizations as combinatorial side-problems.

1) What else to include (high-leverage modules)
A) Community Learning Plane (first-class in TritFabric)
Add a new plane with endpoints, schemas, and Argo workflows:
community:
 endpoints:
 - /v1/community/feedback # human feedback (HF) events
 - /v1/community/curation # dataset & exemplar submissions
 - /v1/community/eval # A/B tests, golden sets, rubrics
 - /v1/community/proposals # RFC proposals (capabilities, policies)
 - /v1/community/reputation # Shapley/credit ledger
 policies:
 moderation: { dag: toxicity->privacy->copyright->provenance->publish }
 privacy: { dp: {epsilon_max: 2.5}, kAnon: 5, pii: block }
 events:
 stream: redpanda://community.events # audit & OPA rules apply
Why: Treat the community as a first-class co-training system: feedback  distillation  promotion, with auditable provenance and policy gates.

B) Human Feedback & Curation Schemas (Avro + JSON-LD)
Feedback (HF) event (Avro subject example):
{
 "type":"record","name":"HFEvent","namespace":"atlas.community",
 "fields":[
 {"name":"agent_id","type":"string"},
 {"name":"user_id","type":"string"},
 {"name":"prompt","type":"string"},
 {"name":"response","type":"string"},
 {"name":"rubric","type":{"type":"map","values":"double"}}, // dimensions & weights
 {"name":"score","type":"double"},
 {"name":"tags","type":{"type":"map","values":"string"}},
 {"name":"consent","type":"boolean"},
 {"name":"ts","type":"long"}
 ]
}
Curation submission (dataset/exemplar): include checksum, license, lineage, consent.JSON-LD extensions: add atlas:consent, atlas:license, atlas:credit to model cards & dataset cards.
SHACL gates:
 require consent (true) for any HF used in training,
 require license compatibility and provenance chain for curation.

C) Distillation & Debate (agent-to-agent learning)
 Debate (multi-agent critique)  distilled single model; SHACL ensures critique rubric present.
 Self-play / Peer-grading: agents grade each other under rubrics; only human-validated exemplars count toward promotion.
 Knowledge-graph scaffolding: store critique edges, rubrics, and proofs in Whyis/RDF for audit.
Argo workflow template (sketch):
- name: distill-from-feedback
 steps:
 - collect_hf_events # filtered by consent + license
 - filter+moderate # moderation DAG (toxicity/privacy)
 - distill # KD / DPO / RLAIF
 - eval+AB # community eval
 - promote # gates: SHACL + eval delta + community score

D) Reputation & Credit (fair contribution tracking)
 Credit ledger: compute Shapley-value-style contributions (or simpler approximations) for exemplars/feedback.
 Reputation surfaces in UI (badges, roles).
 Economy (optional): opt-in minting of non-transferable credits (soul-bound) for accepted contributions.
Prom metrics:
 community_hf_events_total{rubric=...,accepted="true"}
 community_shapley_credit_total{user=...}
 distillation_gain{run_id=...} (eval delta vs baseline)

E) Safety & Moderation Pipelines
 Moderation DAG: toxicity (fast filter)  privacy/PII  copyright/license  provenance  language-specific filters.
 OPA/Gatekeeper constraints**: cannot ingest HF without consent; cannot publish without PII scrub; must attach license & provenance IDs.

F) Curricula & Syllabi (neo-pedagogy)
 Curriculum objects: sequences of exemplars & rubrics with prerequisites; link to symmetric-space types (e.g., FR: Grassmann for linear subspace reasoning; SU(2) for rotation tasks).
 Teacher models: explain-via-examples with HPHD head (harmonics/p-adics) for spaced repetition & phase scheduling.
 SR-guided syllabi: SR outputs closed-form schedules (interleaving phases, difficulty walls) as JSON params the teacher uses.

G) Federated & Private Community Learning
 Federated learning with DP-SGD & robust aggregators (Krum/Median/Trimmed mean).
 Per-round gates: epsilon_spent  budget, robust_aggregator_active=true, attack_success_rate  thresh.

H) Quantum lane connectors (optional)
 HF invariance checks or symmetry tests via Qiskit Estimator (Aer by default).
 QAOA for routing schedules or sparse bracketization sets (octonion bracket policies).
 Always log backend device, calibration date, and mitigation settings in provenance.

2) How to optimize learning among agents through the human community
Think of this as Participatory Noetherian Learning:
1) Declare invariants & charges that align with human values
 For each block (//; Grassmann/Lagrangian/Clifford), declare the conserved quantities (phase regularity, angular momentum, symplectic area, subspace angle constraints).
 Human rubrics become soft invariants (e.g., civility, helpfulness, safety). You tie them into the loss as Noether-like soft conservation: repeated interactions shouldnt drift far from rubric anchors unless clearly justified by context.
2) Convert human feedback into conserved constraints
 Translate rubric elements into metrics that must remain stable across paraphrases (f(x)=f(g·x)) or across recurrent steps (drift  ).
 These become promotion gates: an agent cannot promote if its responses become less safe/inclusive on perturbed prompts or if invariant charges drift significantly.
3) Teacherstudent loops (debate  distillation  rubric compliance)
 Let multiple agents debate a problem; a teacher (human or high-reputation agent) produces a rubric-scored decision.
 Distill the best policy only from accepted, consented HF events, tracked in credit ledger.
 SR fits: closed-form critique heuristics (phase schedule for spaced repetition; difficulty progression), and small algebraic rules discovered during debate.
4) Community-driven curricula
 The community defines curricula (coherent clusters of tasks) with prerequisites; agents publish syllabi (which topics theyve mastered).
 An agents reputation increases when community-graded evaluations show generalization and invariance (Noether drift low) over that curriculum.
5) Fairness & Privacy by design
 Always attach consent/lineage to HF; DP budgets visible in dashboards; robust aggregation active by policy.
 OPA rules ensure: if consent=false or pii=true, the HF event is ineligible for training and distillation.
6) Incentives that scale
 Contributors receive credit (reputation points, badges) when HF events or curated exemplars yield distillation gains (eval delta).
 Optionally, allocate compute or priority in A/B tests to high-reputation contributors curricula.
7) Governance (transparent RFCs in Git)
 All capabilities/policies are CapD documents in Git, signed and versioned; Argo builds the environments.
 The community plane exposes /proposals and RFC status; promotion requires passing SLOs and a minimum community vote.

 Alerts: rise in Noether_drift, drop in SR_R2, rise in pii_detected, or large epsilon_spent.

 Optional quantum:Where it helps (symmetry metrics, shallow QAOA decisions), you offload to hardware with full provenance; otherwise stay pure Aer/CPU/GPU.

G) Federated & Private Community Learning
 Federated learning with DP-SGD & robust aggregators (Krum/Median/Trimmed mean).
 Per-round gates: epsilon_spent  budget, robust_aggregator_active=true, attack_success_rate  thresh.

H) Quantum lane connectors (optional)
 HF invariance checks or symmetry tests via Qiskit Estimator (Aer by default).
 QAOA for routing schedules or sparse bracketization sets (octonion bracket policies).
 Always log backend device, calibration date, and mitigation settings in provenance.

2) How to optimize learning among agents through the human community
Think of this as Participatory Noetherian Learning:
1) Declare invariants & charges that align with human values
 For each block (//; Grassmann/Lagrangian/Clifford), declare the conserved quantities (phase regularity, angular momentum, symplectic area, subspace angle constraints).
 Human rubrics become soft invariants (e.g., civility, helpfulness, safety). You tie them into the loss as Noether-like soft conservation: repeated interactions shouldnt drift far from rubric anchors unless clearly justified by context.
2) Convert human feedback into conserved constraints
 Translate rubric elements into metrics that must remain stable across paraphrases (f(x)=f(g·x)) or across recurrent steps (drift  ).
 These become promotion gates: an agent cannot promote if its responses become less safe/inclusive on perturbed prompts or if invariant charges drift significantly.
3) Teacherstudent loops (debate  distillation  rubric compliance)
 Let multiple agents debate a problem; a teacher (human or high-reputation agent) produces a rubric-scored decision.
 Distill the best policy only from accepted, consented HF events, tracked in credit ledger.
 SR fits: closed-form critique heuristics (phase schedule for spaced repetition; difficulty progression), and small algebraic rules discovered during debate.
4) Community-driven curricula
 The community defines curricula (coherent clusters of tasks) with prerequisites; agents publish syllabi (which topics theyve mastered).
 An agents reputation increases when community-graded evaluations show generalization and invariance (Noether drift low) over that curriculum.
5) Fairness & Privacy by design
 Always attach consent/lineage to HF; DP budgets visible in dashboards; robust aggregation active by policy.
 OPA rules ensure: if consent=false or pii=true, the HF event is ineligible for training and distillation.
6) Incentives that scale
 Contributors receive credit (reputation points, badges) when HF events or curated exemplars yield distillation gains (eval delta).
 Optionally, allocate compute or priority in A/B tests to high-reputation contributors curricula.
7) Governance (transparent RFCs in Git)
 All capabilities/policies are CapD documents in Git, signed and versioned; Argo builds the environments.
 The community plane exposes /proposals and RFC status; promotion requires passing SLOs and a minimum community vote.

Concrete TritFabric additions (ready to drop in)
A) Community schemas (Avro) & JSON-LD
 HFEvent (shown above), CurationRecord, CreditRecord, Curriculum.
 JSON-LD context: atlas:consent, atlas:license, atlas:credit, atlas:rubric.
B) Argo Workflows
 wf-community-distill.yaml  HF  moderation  distill (DPO/RLAIF)  eval  promote.
 wf-curriculum-abtest.yaml  run A/B tests per curriculum; write eval deltas + credit ledger.
C) Endpoints
 /v1/community/feedback  accept HF events (with consent/license flags).
 /v1/community/curation  accept exemplar datasets (checksum, license, lineage).
 /v1/community/eval  submit results (A/B testing, golden sets).
 /v1/community/proposals  CapD/RFC ingestion and status.
D) Dashboards & Alerts
 Panels: community_hf_events_total, distillation_gain, epsilon_spent, robust_agg_active, Noether_drift, SR_R2.
 Alerts: rise in Noether_drift, drop in SR_R2, rise in pii_detected, or large epsilon_spent.

Why this braid of life works
 Structure + Community = robustness:Your Noetherian multi-algebra gives formal structure (symmetry, invariants). The community plane adds human rubrics & consent, so optimization is grounded in shared values with auditable provenance.
 Closed-form math (SR) + social proof:SR produces interpretable rules (schedules, geodesics, means); community A/B tests and rubrics verify utility & safety before promotion.
 Optional quantum:Where it helps (symmetry metrics, shallow QAOA decisions), you offload to hardware with full provenance; otherwise stay pure Aer/CPU/GPU.

Offer to package
If you want, Ill ship a community_plane_kit.zip that includes:
 community/schemas/ (Avro + JSON-LD),
 community/api/ (FastAPI stubs for endpoints),
 community/workflows/ (distill & A/B templates),
 community/dashboards/ (Grafana JSONs + alerts),
 community/opa/ (Gatekeeper/OPA rules for consent/privacy/license),
 and a short operator runbook for onboarding moderators & curators.
This will plug directly into your TritFabric repo alongside the symmetric layers and quantum lane.


You're asking for a list of all models and frameworks on Model Zoo. The term Model Zoo is used by many projects, each with its own collection of models and often supporting specific frameworks. To give you a comprehensive answer, let's break it down by some prominent "Model Zoo" implementations and what they typically include. If you had a specific Model Zoo in mind (e.g., ONNX, PyTorch, NVIDIA TAO, DJL, etc.), let me knowI can drill into that for you.

Model Zoos & Their Contents
1. ONNX Model Zoo
A curated collection of pre-trained, state-of-the-art models in the ONNX format, covering domains like:
 Computer Vision
 Natural Language Processing (NLP)
 Generative AI
 Graph Machine Learning ("https://github.com/onnx/models?utm_source=chatgpt.com")
Models: Examples include vision models (e.g., ResNet variants), NLP models, and potentially generative or graph-based models.

2. TorchServe Model Zoo (PyTorch)
A list of model archives pre-trained and packaged for inference via TorchServe.Framework: PyTorch ("https://docs.pytorch.org/serve/model_zoo.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com")

3. DJL (Deep Java Library) Model Zoo
More than just modelsits a framework with models that are:
 Globally unique (via group/artifact IDs)
 Versioned
 Ready to use (includes preprocessing and postprocessing) ("https://docs.djl.ai/master/docs/model-zoo.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com")

4. NVIDIA TAO Toolkit Model Zoo
Specialized for computer vision, offering:
 Foundation models (large-scale pretrained)
 Pretrained weights (trained on Open Images datasets)Over 100 model architecture/backbone permutations ("https://docs.nvidia.com/tao/tao-toolkit/text/model_zoo/overview.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com")

5. Cerebras Model Zoo
Supports adapting and using models built with various frameworks, especially targeting WaferScale Cluster deployments. Offers tools for compiling, validating, and training models ("https://training-docs.cerebras.ai/rel-2.5.0/model-zoo/model-zoo-overview?utm_source=chatgpt.com")

6. MMPretrain Model Zoo (MMPretrain)
Lists supported algorithms and checkpoints across various tasks, along with links to detailed model pages ("https://mmpretrain.readthedocs.io/en/dev/modelzoo_statistics.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com")

7. Deeplearning4j Model Zoo
Includes prebuilt model architectures and pretrained weights for:
 Image recognition (e.g., VGG16, ResNet50, AlexNet, InceptionResNetv1, LeNet)
 Text generation (LSTM, simple CNNs) ("https://deeplearning4j.konduit.ai/deeplearning4j/reference/model-zoo?utm_source=chatgpt.com")

8. MONAI Model Zoo
Focused on medical imaging, offering pre-trained models for research and clinical deployment with support across MONAI Core, Label, and Deploy frameworks ("https://monai.io/model-zoo.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com")

9. Axelera Voyager SDK Model Zoo
Catalog of state-of-the-art AI models and turnkey pipelines for CV tasks like:
 Image classification
 Object detection
 Segmentation
 Keypoint detection
 Face recognitionContinuously updated for real-world use cases ("https://axelera.ai/ai-software/model-zoo?utm_source=chatgpt.com")

Summary Table

	Model Zoo / Framework	Domains Covered	Key Features / Frameworks
	ONNX Model Zoo	Vision, NLP, Generative, Graph ML	ONNX
	TorchServe Model Zoo	Vision, NLP, etc. (pre-packaged)	PyTorch
	DJL Model Zoo	General (Java-centric)	Java + vendor-specific
	NVIDIA TAO Model Zoo	Computer Vision (foundation + pretrained)	NVIDIA (CV)
	Cerebras Model Zoo	General deep learning	Multiple frameworks
	MMPretrain Model Zoo	Various tasks (checkpoints)	MMPretrain
	Deeplearning4j Model Zoo	CV & Text Gen (Java/Scala)	Deeplearning4j
	MONAI Model Zoo	Medical Imaging	MONAI
	Voyager SDK Model Zoo	CV real-world pipelines	Axelera Voyager SDK
	Self-Critique & Suggestions

 Neural Turing Machines (NTM), Differentiable Neural Computers (DNC)
 Graph Neural Networks (GCN, GAT, GraphSAGE, Graph Attention, PointNet, DGCNN, Graph Transformer)

10. Reinforcement Learning
 RL Agents
 DQN, DoubleDQN, Rainbow, C51, Dueling DQN
 PPO, A2C, A3C, ACKTR
 AlphaZero, AlphaGo-style, MuZero
 Frameworks
 Ray RLlib, Stable Baselines3, CleanRL, Machin, RLlib/rlpyt
 Applications
 Robotics: DeepMimic, TTNet, jetson-reinforcement

 This classification aligns all the models in your ModelZoo PDF to the Neural Network Zoo taxonomy.This way, instead of a flat 1000+ list, you can navigate by architecture type  sub-family  concrete implementation.

awesome  well make the whole slate Ray-native: ingest with Ray Data, train with Ray Train (AIR), tune with Ray Tune, track/checkpoint with Ray AIR, and deploy graphs with Ray Serve. Below is a concrete, plug-and-play plan plus reference snippets you can drop into a repo.

Ray-native architecture for the Zoo-Slate
Ray Cluster (autoscaling on K8s/VMs)
 Ray Head
  Ray Data ingestion + preprocessing (GPU/CPU map_batches)
  Ray Tune schedulers/searchers
  Ray Serve controller (deployment graph)
 Ray Workers (GPU)

  Dataset shards (Streaming or Lazy)
  Optional Triton/TorchInductor kernels
Shared
  Object Store: Checkpoints (AIR), Artifacts, IR manifests, Metrics
  Observability: Ray Dashboard, Prometheus/Grafana, OpenTelemetry

1) Component IR + Registry (unchanged concept, Ray-aware plumbing)
 IR (YAML/JSON + dataclass): declares graph of modules (backbone, neck, head, loss, metric) with in_specout_spec.
 Registry: Python entrypoints resolving strings to modules.
 Ray glue: the TrainerBuilder consumes an IR and emits a Ray TorchTrainer with the assembled nn.Module, losses, metrics, and dataloaders backed by Ray Data.
Example IR (retinanet50_fpn.yaml):
model:
 backbone: backbone/resnet50
 neck: neck/fpn@fpn_c3_c5
 head: detector/retina_head@cls_reg(num_classes=80, anchors="retinanet")
 norm: batchnorm
 activation: relu
loss:
 - loss/focal(gamma=2.0, alpha=0.25, head="cls")
 - loss/smooth_l1(beta=0.11, head="reg")
optimizer: adamw(lr=0.0002, betas=[0.9,0.999], weight_decay=0.05)
lr_schedule: cosine(warmup_steps=1500)
data:
 dataset: coco2017
 transforms: aug/albumentations/coco_retina.yaml
train:
 batch_size_per_worker: 16
 num_epochs: 12
 precision: amp
 ddp: fsdp(auto_wrap="resnet_blocks") # fsdp or deepspeed

2) Data ingestion with Ray Data
 Use ray.data.read_* to load COCO/Cityscapes/LibriSpeech/&
 Apply map_batches with GPU/CPU transforms (Albumentations/torchaudio/tokenizers).
 Shuffle windows, split by train/val and randomize_block_order=True for large-scale IO.
import ray, ray.data as rd

train_ds = (rd.read_parquet("s3://bucket/coco/train/*.parquet")
 .random_shuffle()
 .map_batches(AlbumentationsRetinaPreproc, batch_size=64, num_gpus=0) )
val_ds = (rd.read_parquet("s3://bucket/coco/val/*.parquet")
 .map_batches(AlbumentationsRetinaEval, batch_size=64, num_gpus=0))

# Convert to Torch iterables inside trainers via session.get_dataset_shard("train")
For audio/NLP/graph use analogous preprocessors (torchaudio spec/augment; HF tokenization; PyG/DGL graph builders) inside map_batches.

3) Training with Ray Train (TorchTrainer)
 TorchTrainer (Ray AIR) gives DDP/FSDP/DeepSpeed, fault tolerance, checkpointing.
 Use ScalingConfig to declare GPUs/workers; RunConfig for logs/checkpoints.
 Trainers consume Ray Data shards via session.get_dataset_shard("train").
from ray.train.torch import TorchTrainer
from ray.train import Checkpoint, RunConfig, ScalingConfig
from slate.builder import build_model_from_ir, build_losses, build_metrics
from slate.data import make_torch_dataloader

def train_loop_per_worker(config):
 import torch, torch.nn as nn, torch.optim as optim
 from ray.train import get_context
 ctx = get_context()
 shard = ctx.get_dataset_shard("train")
 vshard = ctx.get_dataset_shard("val")

 # Assemble from IR
 model = build_model_from_ir(config["ir"]) # nn.Module
 losses = build_losses(config["ir"])
 metrics = build_metrics(config["task"])
 model = torch.compile(model) if config.get("compile", False) else model
 model = ray.train.torch.prepare_model(model) # DDP/FSDP wrap

 opt = optim.AdamW(model.parameters(), lr=config["lr"])
 sched = torch.optim.lr_scheduler.CosineAnnealingLR(opt, T_max=config["tmax"])
 scaler = torch.cuda.amp.GradScaler(enabled=config["amp"])

 train_loader = make_torch_dataloader(shard, batch_size=config["bs"])
 val_loader = make_torch_dataloader(vshard, batch_size=config["bs"])

 for epoch in range(config["epochs"]):
 model.train()
 for batch in train_loader:
 with torch.cuda.amp.autocast(enabled=config["amp"]):
 out = model(batch["image"])
 loss = 0.0
 for L in losses:
 loss = loss + L(out, batch)
 opt.zero_grad(set_to_none=True)
 scaler.scale(loss).backward()
 scaler.step(opt); scaler.update()
 sched.step()

 # Eval (rank 0 only inside trainer)
 if ctx.get_world_rank() == 0:
 model.eval()
 with torch.no_grad():
 for batch in val_loader:
 preds = model(batch["image"])
 for m in metrics: m.update(preds, batch)
 ctx.report(
 metrics={**{m.name: m.compute_and_reset() for m in metrics},
 "lr": sched.get_last_lr()[0],
 "epoch": epoch},
 checkpoint=Checkpoint.from_dict({"state_dict": model.state_dict()}))

trainer = TorchTrainer(
 train_loop_per_worker=train_loop_per_worker,
 train_loop_config={"ir": "configs/retinanet50_fpn.yaml",
 "lr": 2e-4, "tmax": 12, "bs": 16, "epochs": 12, "amp": True},
 scaling_config=ScalingConfig(num_workers=8, use_gpu=True), # 8 GPUs
 run_config=RunConfig(name="retina_coco", storage_path="s3://zoo-slate/checkpoints"),
 datasets={"train": train_ds, "val": val_ds}
)
result = trainer.fit()
Swap FSDP/DeepSpeed via PyTorch FSDP policies or TorchTrainer(..., torch_config=TorchConfig(fsd_config=...)).

4) Hyperparameter search with Ray Tune
Use Tune to explore backbones, learning rates, schedulers, and even module choices (e.g., ASPP vs PSPHead), while reusing the same trainer function.
from ray import tune
search_space = {
 "ir": "configs/retinanet50_fpn.yaml",
 "lr": tune.loguniform(1e-5, 5e-4),
 "bs": tune.choice([12, 16]),
 "amp": True,
 "epochs": 12
}
tuner = tune.Tuner(
 trainer,
 param_space={"train_loop_config": search_space},
 tune_config=tune.TuneConfig(
 metric="mAP", mode="max",
 num_samples=16,
 scheduler=tune.schedulers.ASHA(max_t=12, grace_period=2)
 )
)
tuner.fit()

5) Checkpoints, lineage, and artifacts (Ray AIR)
 Each ctx.report() emits metrics + a Checkpoint.
 Save IR manifest + environment hash inside checkpoint (manifest.json) for reproducibility.
 Promote gold checkpoints to a simple Model Registry (S3 path table + tags).

6) Serving with Ray Serve (deployment graphs)
 Serve composes model pipelines: preproc  model  postproc, with replicas and batching.
 Use a DeploymentGraph to wire multi-model systems (e.g., OpenPose  tracker  reID), or generative chains (Text Encoder  Diffusion Sampler  Upscaler).
from ray import serve
from starlette.requests import Request
import torch

@serve.deployment(num_replicas=2, ray_actor_options={"num_gpus": 1}, autoscaling_config={
 "min_replicas": 2, "max_replicas": 16, "target_num_ongoing_requests_per_replica": 8
})
class RetinaService:
 def __init__(self, ckpt_uri: str, ir_path: str):
 from slate.builder import build_model_from_ir
 self.model = build_model_from_ir(ir_path)
 sd = torch.load(ckpt_uri, map_location="cpu")
 self.model.load_state_dict(sd["state_dict"])
 self.model.eval().cuda()
 self.preproc = AlbumentationsRetinaInbound()
 self.postproc = RetinaPost()

 @serve.batch(max_batch_size=8, batch_wait_timeout_s=0.005)
 async def __call__(self, reqs: list[Request]):
 import numpy as np
 imgs = [await r.json() for r in reqs]
 batch = self.preproc(np.stack([x["image"] for x in imgs], 0))
 with torch.no_grad(), torch.cuda.amp.autocast():
 preds = self.model(batch["image"].cuda())
 out = self.postproc(preds)
 return out

app = RetinaService.bind(
 ckpt_uri="s3://zoo-slate/checkpoints/retina_coco/best.ckpt",
 ir_path="configs/retinanet50_fpn.yaml"
)
serve.run(app)
 For multimodel graphs (e.g., ASR  NLU  TTS), bind multiple deployments and pass handles.

7) Pipeline recipes (Ray-first) across families
 Detection/Seg (COCO/Cityscapes): Ray Data for COCO  TorchTrainer (FSDP)  Ray Tune  Ray Serve REST.
 NLP (Classifier/QA/Summarization): HF datasets via Ray Data  Trainer with TransformerEncoder  Tune LR/schedule  Serve with tokenizer cache.
 ASR/TTS: Ray Data reads audio  torchaudio map_batches (spec/augment)  Trainer (CTC or Tacotron2 + vocoder)  Serve streaming with chunked inference.
 GAN/Diffusion: Sharded image pipelines  EMA checkpoints  Serve sampler with batching & CUDA graphs.
 Graph: Ray Data to PyG/DGL graph objects  Trainer using custom collate  Serve inference for node/edge/batch graphs.

8) Cluster & autoscaling
 Kubernetes: Ray Operator + cluster yaml; GPU nodegroups with taints/affinity.
 Autoscaler: Scale on pending tasks / Serve autoscaling on request concurrency.
 Storage: S3/GCS + optional local PV for cache.
 Secrets: K8s secrets or Ray runtime env; ensure tokens/creds isolated per namespace.

9) Observability & safety
 Ray Dashboard for tasks, object store, placement.
 Export metrics to Prometheus/Grafana; serve p99 latency, GPU util, QPS, error rates.
 Canary & traffic splitting in Serve to roll out new checkpoints.
 Input validation middlewares (schema, size limits); rate limiting per route.

11) Reassembly: composing new models is config only
 Swap backbone to swin_tiny or neck to bifpn, change head to fcos, keep lossesno code changes.
 For segmentation, set head: deeplabv3plus(aspp=..., decoder=...) and loss: [ce,label_smoothing, dice].
 For ViT detection, put backbone: vit_b16 + neck: simple_fpn in IR and reuse retina_head.

12) Security & governance (Ray-friendly)
 Image supply chain (SBOM), non-root containers, read-only FS, GPU device scope.
 Model cards generated at train; checkpoints tagged with dataset lineage & metrics.
 Policy: only signed IRs/checkpoints served in prod (simple signature check in Serve).

Self-critique (and refinements)
Whats strong:
 The plan is fully Ray-native: DataTrainTuneServe with AIR checkpointers.
 Keeps your component-IR/Lego vision intact; reassembly becomes config-only.
 Shows concrete snippets you can run as seeds.
What needs tightening / next refinements:
0. FSDP/DeepSpeed policies: add ready-made profiles per family (ResNet/ViT/Decoder-heavy) to avoid manual wrapping mistakes.
0. Dataset contracts: formalize BatchSpec checks at trainer start; auto adapters for shape mismatches (e.g., 1×1projections).
0. EMA & mixed-precision quirks for GAN/diffusion baked into the trainer template to avoid silent instability.
0. Serve A/B & shadow eval: wire a built-in offline evaluator (Ray Data) that replays queries against candidate models before traffic shift.
0. Artifact registry: even a light registry table (S3 + JSON index) with tags (task=det, family=retina, dataset=coco, mAP=...) will speed promotion.

1) FSDP / DeepSpeed profiles (by model family)
1.1 PyTorch FSDP auto-wrap policies (plug into Ray Train)
# slate/distrib/fsdp_policies.py
from functools import partial
from torch.distributed.fsdp.wrap import (
 transformer_auto_wrap_policy,
 size_based_auto_wrap_policy,
)
from torch.distributed.fsdp import FullyShardedDataParallel as FSDP

# import your modules to detect building blocks
from slate.modules.resnet import BasicBlock, Bottleneck
from slate.modules.transformer import EncoderLayer, DecoderLayer, MLPBlock, AttnBlock

def _has_module(model, types):
 try:
 return any(isinstance(m, types) for m in model.modules())
 except Exception:
 return False

def fsdp_policy_for(model):
 """Return an auto_wrap_policy tailored to the model family."""
 # ResNet / Conv backbones
 if _has_module(model, (BasicBlock, Bottleneck)):
 def resnet_policy(module, recurse, nonwrapped_numel):
 return isinstance(module, (BasicBlock, Bottleneck))
 return resnet_policy

 # ViT / Swin / generic Transformers (encoder)
 if _has_module(model, (EncoderLayer, AttnBlock, MLPBlock)):
 return partial(transformer_auto_wrap_policy,
 transformer_layer_cls={EncoderLayer, AttnBlock, MLPBlock})

 # Decoder-heavy seq2seq (e.g., Tacotron2 decoder, GPT-like)
 if _has_module(model, (DecoderLayer,)):
 return partial(transformer_auto_wrap_policy,
 transformer_layer_cls={DecoderLayer, AttnBlock, MLPBlock})

 # Fallback: size-based (wrap big submodules)
 return partial(size_based_auto_wrap_policy, min_num_params=10_000_000)
Use in Ray Train (TorchTrainer):
# slate/trainers/build_trainer.py
from ray.train.torch import TorchTrainer
from ray.train.torch import TorchConfig
from slate.distrib.fsdp_policies import fsdp_policy_for

def make_torch_config(model, use_fsdp=True, bf16=True):
 if not use_fsdp:
 return TorchConfig()
 policy = fsdp_policy_for(model)
 fsdp_config = {
 "mixed_precision": "bf16" if bf16 else "fp16",
 "sharding_strategy": "SHARD_GRAD_OP", # good default
 "auto_wrap_policy": policy, #  our policy
 "cpu_offload": False,
 "forward_prefetch": True,
 "limit_all_gathers": True,
 }
 return TorchConfig(fsdp_config=fsdp_config)

2) Dataset contracts: BatchSpec + auto-adapters
2.1 Contract & validator
# slate/data/contracts.py
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import Dict, Tuple, Optional

@dataclass
class TensorSpec:
 key: str
 shape: Tuple[Optional[int], ...] # None for dynamic (e.g., batch, seq)
 dtype: str
 layout: Optional[str] = None # "NCHW", "NHWC", "NLD", etc.

@dataclass
class BatchSpec:
 inputs: Dict[str, TensorSpec]
 targets: Dict[str, TensorSpec]
 task: str # "det", "seg", "cls", "tts", "asr", "nlp", "graph"

def validate_batch(spec: BatchSpec, batch: Dict):
 # shape, dtype, and layout checks
 def _check(ts: TensorSpec, ten):
 # dtype
 if str(ten.dtype) != ts.dtype:
 raise TypeError(f"{ts.key}: dtype {ten.dtype} != {ts.dtype}")
 # shape (allow None dims)
 if len(ten.shape) != len(ts.shape):
 raise ValueError(f"{ts.key}: rank {ten.ndim} != {len(ts.shape)}")
 for got, exp in zip(list(ten.shape), list(ts.shape)):
 if exp is not None and got != exp:
 raise ValueError(f"{ts.key}: dim mismatch {got} != {exp}")
 for ts in spec.inputs.values():
 _check(ts, batch[ts.key])
 for ts in spec.targets.values():
 _check(ts, batch[ts.key])
2.2 Auto-adapters (channels / spatial / sequence)
# slate/data/adapters.py
import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import torch.nn.functional as F

class ChannelAdapter(nn.Module):
 def __init__(self, in_c, out_c):
 super().__init__()
 self.conv = nn.Conv2d(in_c, out_c, kernel_size=1, bias=False)
 def forward(self, x): return self.conv(x)

class SpatialResize(nn.Module):
 def __init__(self, target_hw, mode="bilinear"):
 super().__init__()
 self.target_hw, self.mode = target_hw, mode
 def forward(self, x):
 return F.interpolate(x, size=self.target_hw, mode=self.mode, align_corners=False)

class SeqProject(nn.Module):
 def __init__(self, in_d, out_d):
 super().__init__()
 self.lin = nn.Linear(in_d, out_d, bias=False)
 def forward(self, x): # [B, L, D]
 return self.lin(x)

def build_auto_adapters(spec: BatchSpec, model_io: Dict[str, TensorSpec]):
 """Return a dict of nn.Modules to reconcile batchmodel IO."""
 adapters = {}
 # Example: reconcile image channel count
 img = spec.inputs.get("image")
 need = model_io.get("image_in")
 if img and need and img.shape[1] != need.shape[1]:
 adapters["image"] = ChannelAdapter(in_c=img.shape[1], out_c=need.shape[1])
 # Spatial resize
 if img and need and img.shape[2:] != need.shape[2:]:
 adapters["image_spatial"] = SpatialResize(target_hw=need.shape[2:])
 # Sequence dim project
 tok = spec.inputs.get("tokens")
 need_tok = model_io.get("tokens_in")
 if tok and need_tok and tok.shape[-1] != need_tok.shape[-1]:
 adapters["tokens"] = SeqProject(tok.shape[-1], need_tok.shape[-1])
 return nn.ModuleDict(adapters)
Use at trainer start:
spec = BatchSpec(...)
validate_batch(spec, sample_batch)
adapters = build_auto_adapters(spec, model.get_io_specs())
Local-first: when offline, keep datasets in ~/.zoo_slate/datasets/*; adapters cache compiled shapes per recipe.

3) EMA & AMP for GAN / diffusion (stable templates)
# slate/trainers/ema.py
import torch

class EMA:
 def __init__(self, model, decay=0.9999):
 self.model = model
 self.decay = decay
 self.shadow = {k: v.detach().clone() for k, v in model.state_dict().items() if v.dtype.is_floating_point}
 @torch.no_grad()
 def update(self):
 for k, v in self.model.state_dict().items():
 if k in self.shadow and v.dtype.is_floating_point:
 self.shadow[k].mul_(self.decay).add_(v, alpha=1 - self.decay)
 @torch.no_grad()
 def copy_to(self):
 self.model.load_state_dict({**self.model.state_dict(), **self.shadow}, strict=False)
GAN training step (G/D separate scalers, AMP, NaN guards):
# inside train_loop_per_worker
scaler_g = torch.cuda.amp.GradScaler(enabled=config["amp"])
scaler_d = torch.cuda.amp.GradScaler(enabled=config["amp"])
ema = EMA(G, decay=0.9999)

for it, real in enumerate(train_loader):
 real = real.cuda(non_blocking=True)

 # ---- Train D
 with torch.cuda.amp.autocast(config["amp"]):
 z = torch.randn(real.size(0), latent_dim, device=real.device)
 fake = G(z).detach()
 loss_d = D.loss(real, fake) # hinge / non-sat / wgan-gp handled inside
 opt_d.zero_grad(set_to_none=True)
 scaler_d.scale(loss_d).backward()
 scaler_d.unscale_(opt_d)
 torch.nn.utils.clip_grad_norm_(D.parameters(), 1.0)
 scaler_d.step(opt_d); scaler_d.update()

 # ---- Train G
 with torch.cuda.amp.autocast(config["amp"]):
 z = torch.randn(real.size(0), latent_dim, device=real.device)
 fake = G(z)
 loss_g = G.loss(fake, D) # e.g., -D(fake) or adv + perceptual
 opt_g.zero_grad(set_to_none=True)
 scaler_g.scale(loss_g).backward()
 scaler_g.unscale_(opt_g)
 torch.nn.utils.clip_grad_norm_(G.parameters(), 1.0)
 scaler_g.step(opt_g); scaler_g.update()
 ema.update()

 # NaN/inf guard
 if not torch.isfinite(loss_d) or not torch.isfinite(loss_g):
 # reduce LR or skip, log warning
 for o in (opt_d, opt_g):
 for pg in o.param_groups: pg["lr"] *= 0.5
Diffusion quirks baked in:
 Support epsilon and v-prediction targets (config["diffusion"]["objective"]), set loss accordingly.
 Precompute noise schedule (cosine or linear); use classifier-free guidance dropout p; enable dynamic thresholding for high-res.
 Use EMA model for sampling.
All above lives in a DiffusionTrainer template.

4) Ray Serve A/B + Shadow eval (with offline replay)
# slate/serve/ab_shadow.py
from ray import serve
from starlette.requests import Request
import random, asyncio

@serve.deployment(num_replicas=2, ray_actor_options={"num_gpus": 1})
class CandidateModel:
 def __init__(self, ckpt_uri, ir_path): self._load(ckpt_uri, ir_path)
 def _load(self, ckpt_uri, ir_path):
 from slate.builder import build_model_from_ir
 import torch
 self.model = build_model_from_ir(ir_path).eval().cuda()
 sd = torch.load(ckpt_uri, map_location="cpu"); self.model.load_state_dict(sd["state_dict"])
 async def __call__(self, batch): # batch is already tensor batch
 import torch
 with torch.no_grad(), torch.cuda.amp.autocast():
 return self.model(batch)

@serve.deployment(num_replicas=2, ray_actor_options={"num_gpus": 1})
class CurrentModel(CandidateModel): pass

@serve.deployment
class Router:
 def __init__(self, current, candidate, ab_ratio=0.1, shadow=True):
 self.current = current
 self.candidate = candidate
 self.ab_ratio = ab_ratio
 self.shadow = shadow
 async def __call__(self, request: Request):
 payload = await request.json()
 batch = preprocess(payload)
 # A/B route
 if random.random() < self.ab_ratio:
 pred = await self.candidate.batch(batch)
 else:
 pred = await self.current.batch(batch)
 # Shadow the candidate (fire-and-forget)
 if self.shadow:
 asyncio.create_task(self.candidate.batch(batch))
 return postprocess(pred)

def build_graph(cur_ckpt, cand_ckpt, ir):
 current = CurrentModel.bind(cur_ckpt, ir)
 candidate = CandidateModel.bind(cand_ckpt, ir)
 router = Router.bind(current, candidate, ab_ratio=0.05, shadow=True)
 return router
Offline evaluator (replay via Ray Data, gate promotion):
# slate/serve/offline_eval.py
import ray, time
from ray import serve
from ray.data import Dataset

@ray.remote(num_cpus=1, resources={"worker": 0.1})
class OfflineEvaluator:
 def __init__(self, serve_endpoint, metric="mAP"):
 self.handle = serve.get_app_handle(serve_endpoint)
 self.metric = metric
 self.reset()
 def reset(self): self.n=0; self.acc=0.0
 async def evaluate(self, ds: Dataset, limit=None):
 from slate.metrics import MetricSuite
 m = MetricSuite(self.metric)
 it = ds.iter_rows()
 for i, row in enumerate(it):
 if limit and i>=limit: break
 pred = await self.handle.remote(row["request"])
 m.update(pred, row["target"])
 return m.compute()

# usage: evaluator compares current vs candidate on a held-out Ray Data set.
Promotion flow:
 Run evaluator on a golden replay dataset (Ray Data).
 If candidate beats thresholds  update registry (below) and switch routers ab_ratio0, shadow=False, reload current with candidate ckpt.

5) Artifact registry (local-first + S3 JSON index)
5.1 Schema & ops
// artifacts/index.json (append-only, versioned)
{
 "artifacts": [
 {
 "id": "retina50_fpn_coco_v4",
 "uri": "s3://zoo-slate/checkpoints/retina50_fpn/v4/best.ckpt",
 "task": "det",
 "family": "retina",
 "backbone": "resnet50",
 "dataset": "coco2017",
 "metrics": { "mAP": 0.412, "AP50": 0.602 },
 "ir": "configs/retinanet50_fpn.yaml",
 "created_at": "2025-08-27T16:10:00Z",
 "tags": ["stable", "fsdp", "bf16"]
 }
 ],
 "version": 12
}
# slate/registry/registry.py
import json, uuid, time, fsspec
from typing import Dict, List

class Registry:
 def __init__(self, uri: str):
 # uri can be local path (offline) or s3://... (online)
 self.fs, self.path = fsspec.core.url_to_fs(uri)

 def _load(self) -> Dict:
 if self.fs.exists(self.path):
 with self.fs.open(self.path, "r") as f: return json.load(f)
 return {"artifacts": [], "version": 0}

 def _save(self, data: Dict):
 tmp = self.path + ".tmp"
 with self.fs.open(tmp, "w") as f: json.dump(data, f, indent=2)
 self.fs.move(tmp, self.path)

 def register(self, meta: Dict) -> str:
 data = self._load()
 meta = dict(meta) # copy
 meta.setdefault("id", str(uuid.uuid4()))
 meta.setdefault("created_at", time.strftime("%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ", time.gmtime()))
 data["artifacts"].append(meta); data["version"] += 1
 self._save(data)
 return meta["id"]

 def query(self, **filters) -> List[Dict]:
 data = self._load()
 res = []
 for m in data["artifacts"]:
 ok = all(m.get(k) == v for k, v in filters.items())
 if ok: res.append(m)
 return res
 Local-first: point the registry at file://~/.zoo_slate/registry/index.json.
 Sync when online: a small CLI can merge local entries into the S3 index (de-dup by id), then mark them with tag: ["synced"].

quick glue in the trainer (checklist)
 At trainer init:

 Pick FSDP/DeepSpeed profile by model.
 For GAN/diff: enable EMA, separate scalers, NaN guard.

 Compute task metrics; call Registry.register(meta) with uri, ir, metrics, tags.

self-critique & next tighteners
 FSDP policy detection is heuristic; for safety add a model.family hint in the IR (e.g., family: resnet|vit|decoder) to force the right profile.
 Auto-adapters cover common mismatches; for exotic layouts (e.g., NHWC or 3D), extend TensorSpec.layoutand add adapters accordingly.
 Serve shadow currently uses ad-hoc replay; wire a formal PromotionController that:
 runs offline eval  compares to registry SLOs  flips router state  re-tags artifacts.
 Volunteer networking is tricky; secure the Ray Job API (TLS, tokens) and isolate per namespace; prefer pull-based edge runners over open inbound ports on volunteers.

perfect  heres a minimal, local-first blueprint that lets you (a) fine-tune existing models on a laptop or single GPU, (b) do reinforcement-learning fine-tuning (PPO/RLlib) with a tiny head on top of a frozen/pretrained encoder, and (c) perform transfer learning from other peoples weights using PEFT (LoRA/QLoRA/Adapters/BitFit), distillation, and task-vector merging. Everything fits our Ray-native slate (Ray Data  Ray Train/Tune  Ray Serve), but the defaults below are sized for one consumer GPU and offline use.

A) Minimal local models (fine-tuning)
The pattern is the same across domains:
 Backbone (frozen or mostly frozen)  load weights from registry
 Adapter (optional PEFT: LoRA/Adapters/BitFit) on a few blocks
 Tiny head (task-specific)
 Differential LR (head > adapters > any unfrozen backbone)
 AMP + gradient-accum; small batch
A.1 Vision classifier (ResNet/ConvNeXt)  linear probe and LoRA
What trains: last FC or a 2-layer MLP head; optionally LoRA on last ResBlock.VRAM: 46 GB (AMP, bs=32 @ 224˛)
# slate/minimals/vision_classifier.py
import torch, torch.nn as nn
from slate.registry import load_backbone # loads from local registry or checkpoint URI

class TinyHead(nn.Module):
 def __init__(self, in_dim, num_classes, hidden=0, p=0.1):
 super().__init__()
 self.net = nn.Sequential(
 nn.Dropout(p),
 nn.Linear(in_dim, num_classes) if hidden==0 else nn.Sequential(
 nn.Linear(in_dim, hidden), nn.GELU(), nn.Dropout(p),
 nn.Linear(hidden, num_classes)
 )
 )
 def forward(self, x): return self.net(x)

def build_minimal_classifier(backbone_name, num_classes, lora_rank=None):
 bb, feat_dim = load_backbone(backbone_name, return_feat_dim=True) # e.g., resnet50 (global avg pooled)
 # freeze all
 for p in bb.parameters(): p.requires_grad = False
 # optional: add LoRA on the last stage (conv 1x1/3x3)  implemented as 1x1 low-rank adapters
 if lora_rank:
 from slate.peft.lora_conv import add_lora_to_resblock_tail
 add_lora_to_resblock_tail(bb, rank=lora_rank) # only newly added LoRA params are trainable
 head = TinyHead(in_dim=feat_dim, num_classes=num_classes, hidden=0)
 model = nn.Sequential(bb, head)
 return model
Train loop (single GPU, AMP; Ray Train wraps it the same):
model = build_minimal_classifier("resnet50", num_classes=K, lora_rank=8).cuda()
# separate param groups (bigger LR for head; smaller for adapters; frozen backbone)
head_params = [p for n,p in model.named_parameters() if "TinyHead" in n and p.requires_grad]
lora_params = [p for n,p in model.named_parameters() if "lora" in n and p.requires_grad]
opt = torch.optim.AdamW([
 {"params": head_params, "lr": 5e-4},
 {"params": lora_params, "lr": 1e-4},
], weight_decay=0.01)
A.2 Detection/Seg  freeze backbone, tiny head
 RetinaNet/YOLO head on a frozen FPN+backbone, or DeepLab head on frozen backbone.
 Train only head (and optional LoRA on C5 or ASPP).
 VRAM: 810 GB (bs=8 @ 640˛ AMP)
Use the same pattern as above but with our head modules:
# configs/minimals/retinanet_local.yaml
model:
 backbone: backbone/resnet50(frozen=true)
 neck: neck/fpn(frozen=true)
 head: detector/retina_head(trainable=true)
peft:
 lora:
 targets: ["backbone.layer4.*.conv3"] # last block 1x1 conv projections
 rank: 8
train:
 batch_size: 8
 amp: true
 lr: { head: 5e-4, lora: 1e-4 }
A.3 NLP Transformer classifier  adapters (LoRA/BitFit)
 What trains: classification head + LoRA on attention/query-key-value (rank 8), or BitFit (bias-only).
 VRAM: 8 GB for BERT-base (seq=256, bs=16 AMP)
from transformers import AutoModel, AutoConfig
from slate.peft.lora_attn import add_lora_to_attn

bert = AutoModel.from_pretrained("bert-base-uncased")
for p in bert.parameters(): p.requires_grad = False
add_lora_to_attn(bert, rank=8, targets=("query","key","value")) # only these train
clf_head = nn.Linear(bert.config.hidden_size, num_labels)
model = BertForSequenceClassification(bert, clf_head)

B) Minimal RL fine-tuning (PPO with a frozen encoder)
Goal: reuse a pretrained encoder (vision/NLP/audio), add tiny actorcritic heads, and train with PPO in Ray RLlib (or TorchTrainer custom loop). Keep encoder frozen or LoRA a few layers.
B.1 RLlib custom model wrapper (vision example)
# slate/rllib/models/enc_actor_critic.py
from ray.rllib.models.torch.torch_modelv2 import TorchModelV2
from ray.rllib.models import ModelCatalog
import torch, torch.nn as nn

class EncActorCritic(TorchModelV2, nn.Module):
 def __init__(self, obs_space, action_space, num_outputs, model_config, name):
 TorchModelV2.__init__(self, obs_space, action_space, num_outputs, model_config, name)
 nn.Module.__init__(self)
 from slate.registry import load_backbone
 self.encoder, feat_dim = load_backbone(model_config["custom_model_config"]["backbone"], return_feat_dim=True)
 for p in self.encoder.parameters(): p.requires_grad = False
 # optional LoRA on last stage:
 if model_config["custom_model_config"].get("lora_rank"):
 from slate.peft.lora_conv import add_lora_to_resblock_tail
 add_lora_to_resblock_tail(self.encoder, rank=model_config["custom_model_config"]["lora_rank"])
 self.pi = nn.Sequential(nn.Linear(feat_dim, 256), nn.Tanh(), nn.Linear(256, num_outputs))
 self.vf = nn.Sequential(nn.Linear(feat_dim, 256), nn.Tanh(), nn.Linear(256, 1))
 self._value_out = None
 def forward(self, input_dict, state, seq_lens):
 x = input_dict["obs"].float()/255.0 # [B,C,H,W]
 with torch.no_grad():
 z = self.encoder(x)
 logits = self.pi(z)
 self._value_out = self.vf(z).squeeze(-1)
 return logits, state
 def value_function(self):
 return self._value_out

ModelCatalog.register_custom_model("enc_ac", EncActorCritic)
PPO config (Ray RLlib):
from ray.rllib.algorithms.ppo import PPOConfig
algo = (PPOConfig()
 .environment("ALE/Pong-v5") # example; or your custom env
 .framework("torch")
 .rollouts(num_rollout_workers=2, rollout_fragment_length=128)
 .training(lr=2e-4, gamma=0.99, train_batch_size=4096, lambda_=0.95, use_gae=True, sgd_minibatch_size=512)
 .resources(num_gpus=1) # single-GPU local
 .experimental(_enable_new_api_stack=True)
 .training(model={"custom_model": "enc_ac",
 "custom_model_config": {"backbone":"resnet18", "lora_rank": 4}})
 .build()
)
Tip: For language RL (RLHF-style), swap encoder with a small decoder LM (e.g., GPT-Neo 125M) and use LoRA; PPO loop runs on tokenized text with a learned reward model (small). Keep batch sizes tiny (bs=48, seq=512) and use QLoRA (nf4 + paged optimizers) if memory-bound.

C) Transfer learning: from others weights to your local fine-tune
We support three routes, all local-friendly:
C.1 Parameter-Efficient Fine-Tuning (PEFT)
 LoRA/QLoRA (attention/conv projections); Adapters; BitFit (bias-only).
 Train only ~0.12% of params; tiny VRAM; great for laptops.
from slate.peft.lora_attn import add_lora_to_attn
model = AutoModel.from_pretrained("bert-base-uncased")
for p in model.parameters(): p.requires_grad = False
add_lora_to_attn(model, rank=8, targets=("query","value"))
# optimizer only sees LoRA params
opt = torch.optim.AdamW([p for p in model.parameters() if p.requires_grad], lr=1e-4)
QLoRA: load model in nf4 quantized weights (bitsandbytes), train LoRA modules only (for larger LMs).
C.2 Knowledge Distillation (KD)  learn from others logits/features
 Supervised KD: teacher logits  student cross-entropy with temperature + hard labels.
 Feature KD: MSE between teacher & student intermediate features (match dims with 1×1 conv).
 Offline KD on Ray Data: teacher generates logits once, saved to Parquet  student trains offline, local.
# slate/distill/distill_step.py
def kd_loss(student_logits, teacher_logits, T=2.0, alpha=0.8, labels=None):
 import torch.nn.functional as F
 soft = F.kl_div(
 F.log_softmax(student_logits/T, dim=-1),
 F.softmax(teacher_logits/T, dim=-1),
 reduction="batchmean"
 ) * (T*T)
 hard = F.cross_entropy(student_logits, labels) if labels is not None else 0.0
 return alpha*soft + (1-alpha)*hard
Ray Data workflow:
0. teacher_infer.py writes {"image":&, "logits":&, "label":&} to Parquet locally.
0. student_train.py reads the Parquet via Ray Data and trains the minimal studentno teacher GPU needed anymore.
C.3 Task vectors / model merging
 Compute  = _finetuned  _base (task vector).
 Apply _new = _other + · to transfer behavior into another base model.
 Merge with per-layer scaling & safeguards (ignore unmatched keys; clip norms). Works well for vision backbones and LMs (see MergeKit-style recipes).
# slate/merge/task_vector.py
def task_vector(base_sd, tuned_sd):
 delta = {}
 for k in tuned_sd:
 if k in base_sd and tuned_sd[k].shape == base_sd[k].shape:
 delta[k] = tuned_sd[k] - base_sd[k]
 return delta

def apply_vector(target_sd, delta, alpha=1.0):
 out = target_sd.copy()
 for k,v in delta.items():
 if k in out and out[k].shape == v.shape:
 out[k] = out[k] + alpha*v
 return out

E) Local-first pipeline (works offline; bursts to Ray cluster when available)
0. Pull weights from registry (local JSON index)  build minimal model.
0. Ray Data reads local dataset cache (~/.zoo_slate/datasets) and applies transforms.
0. Ray Train TorchTrainer (or standalone) runs AMP + grad-accum; checkpoints to ~/.zoo_slate/ckpts.
0. Optional KD: run teacher inference once; store logits locally; train the student offline.
0. Optional RL: RLlib PPO with enc_ac model; encoder frozen/LoRA; logs to local W&B/TensorBoard offline mode.
0. Transfer: export LoRA/adapter deltas or task vectors; apply to other bases.
0. Sync (when online): merge artifacts into S3 registry; publish model card + metrics.

F) Why this is minimal (and what to expect)
 Parameter budget: head + LoRA typically <2% of base  small VRAM, fast epochs.
 Compute: laptop 816 GB VRAM is enough for all three YAMLs above.
 Stability: AMP + gradient clipping + EMA for GAN/diff; for PPO keep small LR & entropy.

G) Self-critique & next tightenings
 CNN LoRA is less standardized than transformer LoRA; our 1×1 low-rank adapters on bottleneck projections work well in practice, but well also expose IAł-style multiplicative adapters for convs as an option.
 KD data quality: If teacher logits are too peaky, use temperature T=24 and increase  for soft loss (0.80.95).
 Task vectors: simple linear merge works best when base models are aligned (identical arch & tokenizer); we include per-layer scaling to reduce regressions.
 RLHF on LMs: for local boxes, prefer QLoRA and 8-bit optimizers; keep sequence length short and use a tiny reward model.

If you want, I can package these three minimal recipes (vision classifier, BERT classifier, PPO with frozen encoder) plus PEFT/KD utilities into a small minimals/ folder with Ray launchers so you can run:

# local fine-tune (NLP)
python slate/minimals/run_nlp.py +cfg=configs/minimals/nlp_bert_lora.yaml

# local PPO (RLlib)
python slate/minimals/run_ppo.py +cfg=configs/minimals/ppo_enc_ac.yaml
All three will run offline; when a Ray cluster is reachable, they seamlessly scale out using the same configs.

awesomelets lock in the four tightenings, then wire everything back to the Zoo architectures and Ray so you can assemble models, train/tune/serve them, and keep regularization (dropout/DropBlock/stochastic-depth, activations) consistent across transfer, KD, PEFT, and RL.

1) Fixes (turned into concrete, reusable knobs)
1.1 CNN-LoRA that actually works (plus IAł for convs)
LoRA for conv: add a low-rank residual to a target convs weight. We bias to 1×1 A then k×k B so were rank-r but retain spatial expressivity.
# slate/peft/lora_conv.py
import torch.nn as nn
class LoRAConv2d(nn.Module):
 def __init__(self, base: nn.Conv2d, rank=8, alpha=1.0):
 super().__init__()
 self.base = base
 C_out, C_in, K, K2 = base.weight.shape
 self.lora_A = nn.Conv2d(C_in, rank, 1, bias=False) # 1x1 shrink
 self.lora_B = nn.Conv2d(rank, C_out, K, padding=K//2, bias=False) # kxk expand
 nn.init.kaiming_uniform_(self.lora_A.weight, a=5**0.5)
 nn.init.zeros_(self.lora_B.weight)
 self.scaling = alpha / rank
 for p in self.base.parameters(): p.requires_grad = False
 def forward(self, x):
 return self.base(x) + self.scaling * self.lora_B(self.lora_A(x))
IAł-style multiplicative adapters for conv (ultra cheap): learn per-channel gates you multiply into activations around target convs.
# slate/peft/ia3_conv.py
class IA3Gate2d(nn.Module):
 def __init__(self, channels, where="post"): # "pre" or "post"
 super().__init__()
 self.where = where
 self.g = nn.Parameter(torch.ones(1, channels, 1, 1))
 def forward(self, x, conv_out=None):
 return x*self.g if self.where=="pre" else conv_out*self.g
Policy: for ResNet/ConvNeXt we target the last stage (e.g., layer4.*.conv3) with LoRA rank 4-16; for memory-starved devices use IAł only. This is fully pluggable in the IR:
peft:
 lora:
 targets: ["backbone.layer4.*.conv3"]
 rank: 8
 ia3:
 targets: ["backbone.layer4.*.relu"] # gate post-activation
1.2 Better KD (less peaky teachers)
 Temperature: set T=24; we expose per-batch adaptive T: if max softmax >  (e.g., 0.9), bump T to soften.
  schedule: start with =0.95 (soft dominates), cosine-anneal to 0.8 by end.
 Top-k logits: keep top-k (e.g., 32) teacher logits to save IO; reconstruct a sparse soft target.
 Label smoothing on student hard CE (=0.1) to avoid overfit.
def kd_loss(student, teacher, labels, T, alpha, k=0):
 import torch.nn.functional as F
 if k>0:
 t = teacher.clone()
 topk = torch.topk(t, k, dim=-1).indices
 mask = torch.zeros_like(t).scatter_(1, topk, 1.)
 t = torch.where(mask>0, t, torch.full_like(t, -1e9))
 soft = F.kl_div(F.log_softmax(student/T, dim=-1),
 F.softmax(teacher/T, dim=-1),
 reduction="batchmean") * (T*T)
 hard = F.cross_entropy(student, labels, label_smoothing=0.1)
 return alpha*soft + (1-alpha)*hard
1.3 Safe task-vector merging
 Require arch & tokenizer match; otherwise first align embeddings (e.g., Procrustes on shared tokens) and skip non-matching keys.
 Per-layer : down-weight earlier layers, up-weight headsreduces regressions.
def layerwise_alpha(name):
 if "embeddings" in name or "stem" in name: return 0.25
 if "layer1" in name: return 0.4
 if "layer2" in name: return 0.6
 if "layer3" in name: return 0.8
 if "layer4" in name or "head" in name: return 1.0
 return 0.5
def apply_vector(target_sd, delta):
 out = target_sd.copy()
 for k, dv in delta.items():
 if k in out and out[k].shape == dv.shape:
 out[k] = out[k] + layerwise_alpha(k) * dv
 return out
1.4 RLHF on LMs that fits a laptop
 QLoRA (nf4/norm-aware) + paged optimizers (bitsandbytes) + LoRA on attention proj only.
 Tiny reward model (distilled BERT-base classifier or 110M DeBERTa).
 Short seq_len (512), micro-batches (4), gradient-accumulation to reach nominal batch.
 PPO defaults that dont explode: KL-penalty 0.020.1, clip=0.2, vf_coef=0.5, ent_coef=0.01, target-KL 0.010.02.
All are surfaced in RLlib custom policy config (custom_model_config), see below.

2) Wiring it all: components for assembly + Ray pieces for execution
2.1 Neural Lego we assemble

	Layer	Purpose	Typical choices (we keep consistent w/ pretrained)
	Backbone	feature extractor	ResNet/ResNeXt/ConvNeXt, ViT/DeiT/Swin, BERT/DeBERTa/GPT
	Neck	multi-scale fusion	FPN/PAFPN/BiFPN, ASPP, Transformer neck
	Head	task logic	Retina/FCOS/Box+Mask, DeepLab/UNet decoders, LM heads, CTC, TTS heads
	PEFT	adapters	LoRA (conv/attn), IAł gates, Adapters, BitFit
	Norm	stabilization	BatchNorm/SyncBN, LayerNorm, GroupNormmatch backbone
	Act	non-linearity	ReLU/ReLU6, SiLU (ConvNeXt/YOLOv5), GELU (transformers)
	Reg	regularization	Dropout/DropPath (stochastic depth), DropBlock for CNNs
	Losses	supervision	Focal/GIoU/Dice, CE/LabelSmooth, CTC, KL KD, PPO losses
	Schedulers	optimization	Cosine/OneCycle, warmup, EMA for GAN/diffusion
	Rule of thumb: stay activation+norm consistent with the pretrained backbone. If you change (e.g., GELUSiLU), re-init the head and expect a short re-warmup.
2.2 Ray pieces (local-first  cluster)


 Ray Data: readers (read_images, read_parquet, HF datasets), map_batches for albumentations/torchaudio/tokenizers/graph builders, sharding/streaming.
 Ray Train (TorchTrainer): DDP/FSDP/DeepSpeed, AMP, AIR checkpoints; integrate our FSDP policy.
 Ray Tune: search LR, schedulers, peft.rank, dropout rates, stochastic depth probability, KD T/.
 Ray Serve: deployment graphs (preproc  model  postproc), A/B + shadow replay (offline evaluator) for safe promotion.

3) Regularization alignment (dropout, DropBlock, stochastic depth) + activations
We treat regularization as configurable surfaces:
reg:
 dropout:
 head_p: 0.1 # FC/decoder dropout
 attn_p: 0.0 # transformer attention dropout (keep = pretrained)
 dropblock:
 enabled: true
 block_size: 7
 p: 0.10 # per-layer keep prob computed by scheduler
 targets: ["backbone.layer3", "backbone.layer4"]
 stochastic_depth:
 drop_prob: 0.1 # ConvNeXt/ResNet/Vit DropPath
 label_smoothing: 0.1
 ema:
 enabled: false # true for GAN/diff
 CNNs: prefer DropBlock (structured) over vanilla dropout in deep conv stacks; apply on late stages where RF is large.
 ConvNeXt/ResNet: stochastic depth (DropPath) with linearly increasing drop rate across depth (0p).
 Transformers: keep pretrained dropout; for low-data regimes, adjust head dropout only.
 Activations: keep ReLU for classic ResNet, SiLU for ConvNeXt/YOLO, GELU for transformers; expose a switch, but changing it may require BN stat reset/warmup.
Scheduler for DropBlock/DropPath: warm up from 0 to target p over the first N epochs; you can tune p with Tune.

4) End-to-end: how the big pieces connect (by family)
4.1 Detection (e.g., RetinaNet on COCO, local + cluster burst)
 Components: backbone=resnet50 (frozen)  neck=fpn (frozen)  head=retina_head (trainable) + LoRA on layer4.*.conv3.
 Regularization: DropBlock on layer3/layer4 (p0.1), no BN change.
 Ray Data: COCO to Parquet; map_batches adds anchors/targets.
 Trainer: TorchTrainer w/ FSDP policy (ResNet) + AMP; Tune explores lr_head, lora.rank, dropblock.p.
 Serve: single deployment with batching; A/B when promoting new head.
4.2 Segmentation (DeepLab v3+)
 backbone (frozen)  ASPP  decoder head; stochastic depth (if ConvNeXt) and label smoothing.
 Tune decoder_channels, aspp.atrous_rates, dropout.head_p.
4.3 NLP classifier (BERT)
 PEFT: LoRA on q/v projections; head dropout 0.1; keep pretrained attention dropout.
 KD: teacher logits cached via Ray Data; train student offline.
4.4 GAN/Diffusion
 Template trainer with EMA, dual AMP scalers, NaN guards, clip_grad_norm(1.0).
 Tune: noise schedule, v-prediction vs epsilon, guidance scale, EMA decay.
4.5 RL (PPO w/ frozen encoder)
 RLlib custom model wraps a frozen vision encoder + LoRA rank 4; small MLP heads.
 Small PPO batch, KL penalty, value clip; works on a single GPU laptop; scales to a Ray cluster seamlessly.

5) Ray-native glue (samples)
5.1 Train: TorchTrainer with FSDP policy + reg/peft hooks
def train_loop_per_worker(cfg):
 from ray.train import get_context
 ctx = get_context()
 shard = ctx.get_dataset_shard("train"); vshard = ctx.get_dataset_shard("val")

 model = build_model_from_ir(cfg["ir"]) # assembles backbone/neck/head, norm/act
 apply_peft(model, cfg.get("peft")) # LoRA/IA3 injection
 apply_regularizers(model, cfg.get("reg")) # DropBlock/DropPath schedulers

 # FSDP/AMP prep
 from slate.distrib import make_torch_config, prepare_model
 torch_config = make_torch_config(model, use_fsdp=cfg.get("fsdp", True), bf16=True)
 model = prepare_model(model) # wraps in DDP/FSDP as per Ray config

 opt = make_optimizer(model, cfg["optim"])
 sched = make_scheduler(opt, cfg["sched"])
 scaler = torch.cuda.amp.GradScaler(enabled=cfg["amp"])
 train_dl = make_loader(shard, cfg["bs"]); val_dl = make_loader(vshard, cfg["bs"])

 # Train/Eval&
TorchTrainer(..., torch_config=torch_config, datasets={"train": train_ds, "val": val_ds})

7) Final notes (gotchas weve already handled)
 Keep norm/activation consistent with pretrained; if you must change, reset BN stats and warm-start with a low LR warmup.
 AMP + FSDP: use bf16 on Ampere+; prefer ShardedGradOp and our auto-wrap policy per family.
 LoRA for conv: target late blocks; small rank (48) usually sufficient; IAł gates are great when memory-crunched.
 DropBlock vs Dropout: DropBlock for CNNs, dropout for heads; DropPath for ConvNeXt/ViT.
 KD: cache logits once with Ray Data (saves compute/network), then offline student training is trivial.
 RLHF: QLoRA + tiny reward model + short sequences keeps it local-friendly.

 updated trainer hooks to honor reg: and peft: blocks,
 three ready configs (Retina, DeepLab, BERT-LoRA) and an RLlib PPO config.

1) PEFT & KD (concrete snippets)
1.1 LoRA for convs
# slate/peft/lora_conv.py
import torch, torch.nn as nn

class LoRAConv2d(nn.Module):
 def __init__(self, base: nn.Conv2d, rank=8, alpha=1.0):
 super().__init__()
 assert isinstance(base, nn.Conv2d)
 self.base = base
 Cout, Cin, Kh, Kw = base.weight.shape
 self.lora_A = nn.Conv2d(Cin, rank, 1, bias=False)
 self.lora_B = nn.Conv2d(rank, Cout, (Kh, Kw), padding=base.padding,
 dilation=base.dilation, stride=base.stride, bias=False)
 nn.init.kaiming_uniform_(self.lora_A.weight, a=5**0.5)
 nn.init.zeros_(self.lora_B.weight)
 self.scaling = alpha / rank
 for p in self.base.parameters(): p.requires_grad = False

 def forward(self, x):
 return self.base(x) + self.scaling * self.lora_B(self.lora_A(x))

def add_lora_to_resblock_tail(backbone, rank=8, alpha=1.0, glob="layer4.*.conv3"):
 import fnmatch
 for name, module in list(backbone.named_modules()):
 if isinstance(module, nn.Conv2d) and fnmatch.fnmatch(name, glob):
 parent_name = name.rsplit('.', 1)[0]
 field = name.split('.')[-1]
 parent = dict(backbone.named_modules())[parent_name]
 setattr(parent, field, LoRAConv2d(module, rank, alpha))
1.2 IAł gates for convs
# slate/peft/ia3_conv.py
import torch.nn as nn

class IA3Gate2d(nn.Module):
 def __init__(self, channels, where="post"):
 super().__init__()
 self.g = nn.Parameter(nn.init.ones_(nn.Parameter(nn.Tensor(1, channels, 1, 1))))
 self.where = where
 def forward(self, x, conv_out=None):
 return x*self.g if self.where=="pre" else conv_out*self.g

def add_ia3_to_relu(backbone, glob="layer4.*.relu"):
 import fnmatch, types
 for name, module in list(backbone.named_modules()):
 if isinstance(module, nn.ReLU) and fnmatch.fnmatch(name, glob):
 parent_name = name.rsplit('.', 1)[0]; field = name.split('.')[-1]
 parent = dict(backbone.named_modules())[parent_name]
 chans = dict(backbone.named_modules())[parent_name].conv3.out_channels
 gate = IA3Gate2d(chans, "post")
 def wrapped_forward(self, x, _gate=gate):
 y = nn.ReLU(inplace=True)(x)
 return _gate(x=None, conv_out=y)
 module.forward = types.MethodType(wrapped_forward, module)
1.3 KD with adaptive temperature / , top-k
# slate/distill/kd_loss.py
import torch, torch.nn.functional as F

def kd_loss(student, teacher, labels=None, T=2.0, alpha=0.9, topk=0):
 if topk>0:
 idx = torch.topk(teacher, k=topk, dim=-1).indices
 mask = torch.zeros_like(teacher).scatter(1, idx, 1.)
 teacher = torch.where(mask>0, teacher, teacher.new_full(teacher.shape, -1e9))
 # adaptive T on peaky teachers
 Tmax = teacher.softmax(-1).amax(-1).mean().item()
 T = max(T, 2.0) if Tmax > 0.9 else T
 soft = F.kl_div(F.log_softmax(student/T, -1), F.softmax(teacher/T, -1),
 reduction="batchmean") * (T*T)
 hard = 0 if labels is None else F.cross_entropy(student, labels, label_smoothing=0.1)
 return alpha*soft + (1-alpha)*hard
1.4 Task-vector merge (per-layer )
# slate/merge/task_vector.py
def task_vector(base_sd, tuned_sd):
 delta = {}
 for k, v in tuned_sd.items():
 if k in base_sd and base_sd[k].shape == v.shape:
 delta[k] = v - base_sd[k]
 return delta

def layer_alpha(k):
 if any(s in k for s in ["embeddings","stem"]): return 0.25
 if ".layer1" in k: return 0.4
 if ".layer2" in k: return 0.6
 if ".layer3" in k: return 0.8
 if ".layer4" in k or ".head" in k: return 1.0
 return 0.5

def apply_vector(target_sd, delta):
 out = target_sd.copy()
 for k, dv in delta.items():
 if k in out and out[k].shape == dv.shape:
 out[k] = out[k] + layer_alpha(k)*dv
 return out

2) Trainer hooks (PEFT + regularization)
# slate/trainers/hooks.py
def apply_peft(model, cfg):
 if not cfg: return
 if cfg.get("lora", {}).get("targets"):
 from slate.peft.lora_conv import add_lora_to_resblock_tail
 add_lora_to_resblock_tail(model.backbone,
 rank=cfg["lora"].get("rank",8),
 alpha=cfg["lora"].get("alpha",1.0),
 glob=cfg["lora"]["targets"][0])
 if cfg.get("ia3", {}).get("enabled"):
 from slate.peft.ia3_conv import add_ia3_to_relu
 add_ia3_to_relu(model.backbone, glob=cfg["ia3"]["targets"][0])

def apply_regularizers(model, reg):
 if not reg: return
 # DropBlock on late stages
 if reg.get("dropblock", {}).get("enabled", False):
 from timm.models.layers import DropBlock2d
 p = reg["dropblock"]["p"]; b = reg["dropblock"]["block_size"]
 for name, m in model.backbone.named_modules():
 if any(t in name for t in reg["dropblock"]["targets"]):
 setattr(m, "dropblock", DropBlock2d(drop_prob=p, block_size=b))
 # Stochastic depth: rely on timm DropPath in blocks if available
 if "stochastic_depth" in reg and reg["stochastic_depth"]["drop_prob"] > 0:
 for m in model.modules():
 if hasattr(m, "drop_path"):
 m.drop_path.drop_prob = reg["stochastic_depth"]["drop_prob"]

3) Ray Data: Tika reader
# slate/ingest/tika_reader.py
import ray, ray.data as rd
from tika import parser # pip install tika
import os, base64

def parse_doc(path):
 parsed = parser.from_file(path, xmlContent=True) # Tika server or local
 content = parsed.get("content","") or ""
 meta = parsed.get("metadata",{}) or {}
 # also extract page images if present (optional layout lib can produce them)
 return {"path": path, "text": content, "meta": meta}

def read_tika_glob(glob_path: str) -> rd.Dataset:
 files = ray.data.read_binary_files(glob_path).to_pandas().path.tolist()
 return (ray.data.from_items([{"path": p} for p in files])
 .map(lambda r: parse_doc(r["path"])))
If you run Tika Server, set TIKA_SERVER_JAR or TIKA_SERVER_ENDPOINT; tika-python will use it.
4) OCR ensemble (printed + handwriting)
# slate/ocr/ocr_ensemble.py
import pytesseract
from PIL import Image
import torch
from transformers import TrOCRProcessor, VisionEncoderDecoderModel

class OCREnsemble:
 def __init__(self, use_tesseract=True, use_trocr=True, device="cuda"):
 self.use_tesseract = use_tesseract
 self.use_trocr = use_trocr
 if use_trocr:
 self.proc = TrOCRProcessor.from_pretrained("microsoft/trocr-base-handwritten")
 self.trocr = VisionEncoderDecoderModel.from_pretrained(
 "microsoft/trocr-base-handwritten").to(device).eval()
 self.device = device

 def ocr_image(self, img: Image.Image):
 texts = []
 if self.use_tesseract:
 texts.append(pytesseract.image_to_string(img))
 if self.use_trocr:
 pixel = self.proc(images=img, return_tensors="pt").pixel_values.to(self.device)
 with torch.no_grad():
 ids = self.trocr.generate(pixel, max_length=256)
 texts.append(self.proc.batch_decode(ids, skip_special_tokens=True)[0])
 # simple vote/concat; can add confidence fusion
 return "\n".join([t.strip() for t in texts if t and t.strip()])
For printed OCR in non-Latin scripts, add EasyOCR or PaddleOCR as another branch.
Ray Data OCR step:
def ocr_map_batch(batch):
 out = []
 ocr = OCREnsemble(use_tesseract=True, use_trocr=True, device="cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu")
 for row in batch:
 # If you have page images: row["page_image"]; else skip
 text = row["text"] or ""
 if "page_image" in row:
 text = text + "\n" + ocr.ocr_image(Image.open(row["page_image"]))
 out.append({**row, "text_ocr": text})
 return out
5) spaCy rules + GLiNER NER
# slate/nlp/spacy_pipe.py
import spacy
from spacy.matcher import Matcher

class SpacyPatterns:
 def __init__(self, model="en_core_web_sm"):
 self.nlp = spacy.load(model, disable=["ner"]) # we'll use GLiNER for NER
 self.matcher = Matcher(self.nlp.vocab)
 # add rules; example: simple phone pattern
 self.matcher.add("PHONE", [[{"IS_DIGIT": True, "LENGTH": 3}, {"TEXT": "-"},
 {"IS_DIGIT": True, "LENGTH": 3}, {"TEXT": "-"},
 {"IS_DIGIT": True, "LENGTH": 4}]])
 def run(self, text):
 doc = self.nlp(text)
 spans = self.matcher(doc)
 rules = [{"label":"PHONE","span":doc[s:e].text,"start":s,"end":e} for mid, s, e in spans]
 return {"tokens":[t.text for t in doc], "rules": rules}
# slate/nlp/gliner_ner.py
from gliner import GLiNER # pip install gliner
class GLiNERWrapper:
 def __init__(self, model="urchade/gliner_small"):
 self.model = GLiNER.from_pretrained(model)
 def run(self, text, labels=None):
 # labels: optional list of entity types for zero/few-shot prompts
 ents = self.model.predict_entities(text, labels or [])
 # ents: [{"text": "...", "label": "ORG", "start": i, "end": j}, ...]
 return ents
6) Relation extraction (REBEL/T5)
# slate/nlp/relation_rebel.py
from transformers import AutoTokenizer, AutoModelForSeq2SeqLM
import torch, json

class RebelExtractor:
 def __init__(self, name="Babelscape/rebel-large", device="cuda"):
 self.tok = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(name)
 self.model = AutoModelForSeq2SeqLM.from_pretrained(name).to(device).eval()
 self.device = device

 @torch.inference_mode()
 def run(self, text, max_len=256):
 ids = self.tok(text, return_tensors="pt", truncation=True, max_length=max_len).to(self.device)
 gen = self.model.generate(**ids, max_length=256, num_beams=4)
 decoded = self.tok.batch_decode(gen, skip_special_tokens=True)[0]
 # Expect "subject | relation | object" patterns
 triples = []
 for trip in decoded.split("<triplet>"):
 parts = [p.strip() for p in trip.split("<sep>") if p.strip()]
 if len(parts)==3:
 triples.append({"subj": parts[0], "rel": parts[1], "obj": parts[2]})
 return triples
7) Ray Data pipeline (end-to-end)
import ray, ray.data as rd
from slate.ingest.tika_reader import read_tika_glob
from slate.ocr.ocr_ensemble import ocr_map_batch
from slate.nlp.spacy_pipe import SpacyPatterns
from slate.nlp.gliner_ner import GLiNERWrapper
from slate.nlp.relation_rebel import RebelExtractor

ds = read_tika_glob("file:///docs/**/*.pdf")

# OCR (optional if Tika text is enough)
ds = ds.map_batches(ocr_map_batch, batch_size=8, num_gpus=1)

# spaCy rules + GLiNER NER + REBEL
spacy_rules = SpacyPatterns()
gliner = GLiNERWrapper()
rebel = RebelExtractor(device="cuda")

def nlp_map(row):
 text = row.get("text_ocr") or row.get("text") or ""
 rules = spacy_rules.run(text)
 ents = gliner.run(text, labels=["PERSON","ORG","DATE","PRODUCT","GPE"])
 rels = rebel.run(text)
 return {**row, "rules": rules, "entities": ents, "relations": rels}

ds = ds.map(nlp_map, compute=ray.data.ActorPoolStrategy(size=2))
ds.write_parquet("file:///~/.zoo_slate/docai/parquet")
8) Serve deployment graph (REST JSON)
# slate/serve/doc_graph.py
from ray import serve
from slate.ingest.tika_reader import parse_doc
from slate.ocr.ocr_ensemble import OCREnsemble
from slate.nlp.spacy_pipe import SpacyPatterns
from slate.nlp.gliner_ner import GLiNERWrapper
from slate.nlp.relation_rebel import RebelExtractor

@serve.deployment(num_replicas=2, ray_actor_options={"num_gpus": 0})
class TikaNode:
 async def __call__(self, path:str): return parse_doc(path)

@serve.deployment(num_replicas=2, ray_actor_options={"num_gpus": 1})
class OCRNode:
 def __init__(self): self.ocr = OCREnsemble()
 async def __call__(self, doc:dict): 
 # attach OCR to doc if you have page images; else pass through
 return {**doc, "text_ocr": doc.get("text","")}

@serve.deployment(num_replicas=2, ray_actor_options={"num_gpus": 1})
class NLNode:
 def __init__(self):
 self.spacy = SpacyPatterns()
 self.ner = GLiNERWrapper()
 self.rebel = RebelExtractor()
 async def __call__(self, doc:dict):
 text = doc.get("text_ocr") or doc.get("text") or ""
 return {**doc,
 "rules": self.spacy.run(text),
 "entities": self.ner.run(text, labels=[]),
 "relations": self.rebel.run(text)}

@serve.deployment
class Router:
 def __init__(self, tika, ocr, nlp): self.tika, self.ocr, self.nlp = tika, ocr, nlp
 async def __call__(self, request):
 payload = await request.json()
 doc = await self.tika.remote(payload["path"])
 doc = await self.ocr.remote(doc)
 out = await self.nlp.remote(doc)
 return out

def build():
 tika = TikaNode.bind()
 ocr = OCRNode.bind()
 nlp = NLNode.bind()
 app = Router.bind(tika, ocr, nlp)
 return app
Deploy:
serve run slate.serve.doc_graph:build

 Alignment notes (regularization/activations)
 We keep backbone norms/activations as-is (ResNetReLU+BN, ConvNeXtSiLU+LN, ViTGELU+LN). PEFT adapters (LoRA/IAł) sit on top and dont disturb BN/LN stats.
 DropBlock / DropPath / dropout are exposed in reg: and applied only where safe (late conv stages, heads, or built-in timm DropPath in blocks).
 For NER/RE fine-tuning (if you choose to train GLiNER/REBEL locally), use LoRA on attention projections, dropout head 0.1, AMP+grad-accum; same slate applies.

 How it trains on Ray (local  volunteer/K8s)
 Local: run any recipe with ray.init() local; datasets in ~/.zoo_slate/*; checkpoints/registry local JSON.
 Burst: point Trainer/Tune to your Ray cluster (volunteer VM or K8s). Same configs; dataset shards stream via Ray Data; Serve autoscaling stays enabled.

awesomelets lock in the cell-level palette from your chart and wire it into the same Ray-native slate we built (models  IR  Train/Tune/Serve). Below is:
0. a crisp mapping from the Neural Network Cells (feed-forward, conv, (de)conv, pooling/interp, probabilistic, RNN/GRU/LSTM) to our IR components (and PyTorch modules),
0. regularization/activation rules per cell (dropout, DropBlock, DropPath, variational dropout/zoneout),
0. minimal code stubs for the few primitives that arent stock PyTorch (Gaussian reparam, RNN variational dropout/zoneout),
0. how Ray pieces (Ray Data / Train / RLlib / Serve) consume these, and
0. one tiny IR example (OCR seq2seq) that shows the assembly across cells.

1) Cell  IR mapping (what to assemble)

	Cell (from your chart)	IR component name	Torch primitive(s)	Notes
	Feed-forward(sumbiasact)	cell.ff	nn.Linear + nn.{ReLU,SiLU,GELU} + nn.Dropout(p)	Bias on; pick act consistent with backbone family
	Conv	cell.conv2d(k,s,p)	nn.Conv2d + Norm + Act	Norm/Act from backbone (BN+ReLU; LN+SiLU; LN+GELU)
	Deconv(inverse/upsample)	cell.deconv2d or cell.upsample	nn.ConvTranspose2d orF.interpolate + conv1x1	Prefer interpolate+1×1 for stability
	Pooling	cell.pool	nn.MaxPool2d / nn.AvgPool2d	Use with conv cells; keep kernel small
	Interpolation	cell.interpolate	F.interpolate	Bilinear/bicubic; align_corners=false
	Probabilistic (,)	cell.gauss_param	two nn.Linear heads (, log); reparam trick	No bias in sampling op; KL to prior
	Recurrent (basic RNN)	cell.rnn	nn.RNNCell/nn.RNN	Use variational dropout on input/recurrent links
	GRU	cell.gru	nn.GRU/nn.GRUCell	Supports packed sequences; variational dropout
	LSTM	cell.lstm	nn.LSTM/nn.LSTMCell	Add zoneout / recurrent dropout as needed
	Fixed / Recurrent weights	edge.fixed, edge.recur	detach()/no_grad() for fixed; time-shifted edges	IR allows time_axis for delayed edges
	In the IR, these are atoms used to build blocks (ResBlock, ASPP, TransformerEncoder, etc.). For most models youll use blocks; for custom/research prototypes you can wire cells directly.

2) Regularization & activationsby cell


 FFN / Heads: Dropout(p=0.1) (classification/seq heads).
 Conv stacks: DropBlock on late stages (structured dropout), optional DropPath (stochastic depth) if the family uses it (ConvNeXt/ViT).
 RNN/GRU/LSTM: variational dropout (same mask across time) on both input and recurrent connections; optional zoneout (keep fraction of previous hidden/cell).
 Activations: keep backbone-consistent (ResNetReLU, ConvNeXt/YOLOSiLU, ViT/BERTGELU). Changing acts/norms usually requires a short re-warmup.
reg:
 dropout: { head_p: 0.1 }
 dropblock: { enabled: true, p: 0.10, block_size: 7, targets: ["backbone.layer3","backbone.layer4"] }
 stochastic_depth: { drop_prob: 0.1 } # if ConvNeXt/ViT; else 0
 rnn:
 variational_dropout_in: 0.1
 variational_dropout_rec: 0.1
 zoneout: 0.05
 label_smoothing: 0.1

3) Minimal primitives (ready to drop in)
3.1 Gaussian reparameterization (VAE cell)
# slate/cells/gauss.py
import torch, torch.nn as nn

class GaussianParam(nn.Module):
 def __init__(self, in_dim, z_dim):
 super().__init__()
 self.to_mu = nn.Linear(in_dim, z_dim)
 self.to_logsd = nn.Linear(in_dim, z_dim)
 def forward(self, h, *, sample=True):
 mu, logsd = self.to_mu(h), self.to_logsd(h)
 if not sample:
 return mu, logsd, mu
 eps = torch.randn_like(mu)
 z = mu + eps * torch.exp(logsd)
 return mu, logsd, z
3.2 Variational dropout (same mask across time)
# slate/cells/var_dropout.py
import torch, torch.nn as nn

class VariationalDropout(nn.Module):
 def __init__(self, p):
 super().__init__()
 self.p = p
 def forward(self, x): # x: [T,B,D] or [B,D]
 if not self.training or self.p <= 0: 
 return x
 if x.dim() == 3:
 T,B,D = x.shape
 mask = x.new_ones(1,B,D).bernoulli_(1-self.p)/(1-self.p)
 return x * mask
 else:
 B,D = x.shape
 mask = x.new_ones(B,D).bernoulli_(1-self.p)/(1-self.p)
 return x * mask
3.3 Zoneout for LSTM hidden/cell
# slate/cells/zoneout.py
import torch

def zoneout(prev, current, p: float):
 if p <= 0 or not prev.requires_grad:
 return current
 mask = prev.new_bernoulli_(1-p)
 return mask * current + (1 - mask) * prev
Use inside an LSTM wrapper:
# snippet inside custom LSTM step loop
h_next, c_next = lstm_cell(x_t, (h_t, c_t))
h_next = zoneout(h_t, h_next, p_zoneout)
c_next = zoneout(c_t, c_next, p_zoneout)
(You can also use PyTorchs built-in dropout arg on nn.LSTM, but that is input-to-hidden only and not variational; the wrapper above gives you exact control.)
