4.1 Ray Data (sequences & images)
 Sequences: store {"tokens": LongTensor, "length": int}; map_batches packs into padded tensors and length masks.
 Images: {"image": C×H×W, "label": &}; augment in map_batches (Albumentations).
 Docs (OCR): produce "text" from Tika/OCR; tokenize in map_batches (spaCy/HF tokenizers).
def pack_sequences(batch, pad_id=0):
 # returns padded [B,L], lengths for RNN/LSTM cells
4.2 Ray Train (TorchTrainer)
 FFN/CNN: exactly as before; FSDP/DeepSpeed profiles auto-select.
 RNN/GRU/LSTM: trainer sets torch.backends.cudnn.enabled=False for deterministic RNNS if needed; supports TBPTT with cfg["tbptt_len"].
 VAE: add KL term (KL(N(,) || N(0,1))) to loss; use our GaussianParam.
train_loop_config:
 ir: configs/seq2seq_ocr.yaml
 tbptt_len: 64
 reg:
 rnn: { variational_dropout_in: 0.1, variational_dropout_rec: 0.1, zoneout: 0.05 }
4.3 RLlib (recurrent policies)
 Wrap cell.lstm or cell.gru in a custom model (we already showed for encoders).
 Set model["use_lstm"]=True or use your own custom_model with hidden state.
 RLlib handles sequence batching + state passing automatically.
4.4 Ray Serve
 Assemble deployment graphs from components: pre-tokenize (Ray Data or in-Serve), forward through recurrent/transformer blocks, post-decode.
 For OCR seq2seq, you can serve: image  CNN encoder  LSTM/Transformer decoder  text.

5) Tiny IR example (OCR handwriting seq2seq; uses your cells)
# configs/seq2seq_ocr.yaml
model:
 encoder:
 - cell.conv2d(k=3,s=1,p=1) x2
 - cell.pool(k=2) # spatial downsample
 - cell.conv2d(k=3,s=1,p=1) x2
 - cell.pool(k=2)
 - reshape_to_seq(axis="width") # C×H×W  W×(B×H)×C
 - cell.lstm(hidden=512, layers=2, bidir=true)
 decoder:
 - cell.lstm(hidden=512, layers=2) # attends over encoder outputs
 - cell.ff(out_dim=vocab_size) # logits
 attention: dot # simple dot attention
norm: batchnorm
act: relu

reg:
 rnn: { variational_dropout_in: 0.1, variational_dropout_rec: 0.1, zoneout: 0.05 }
 dropout: { head_p: 0.1 }

train:
 loss: ctc # or seq2seq CE with teacher forcing
 tbptt_len: 64
 bs: 16
 amp: true
 fsdp: true
 optim: { type: adamw, lr: 2e-4, wd: 0.01 }

data:
 source: file://~/.zoo_slate/ocr/parquet # from your OCR Ray Data pipeline
 tokens: charset_ocr.json
This uses conv + pool cells to get features, then LSTM cells for sequence modeling, regularized with variational dropout+zoneout, trained under Ray Train (AMP + FSDP).

6) Quick checklist (how this aligns with the rest)
 Models & architectures: Cells are the atoms; blocks (ResBlock/ASPP/TransformerEncoder) are just higher-level macros composed of these atoms. Your Retina/DeepLab/ViT/Transformer/Tacotron/UNet configs already map to these atoms.
 PEFT (LoRA/IAł): Sits on top of conv/attn cellsno change to cell math, just extra low-rank/multiplicative paths.
 KD/distillation: Pure head/cell-agnostic loss; works equally for FFN/CNN/RNN outputs (use CE/CTC + KL on logits).
 Regularization:
 CNN  DropBlock (+ optional DropPath),
 FFN/heads  Dropout,
 RNN/GRU/LSTM  Variational dropout (in & recurrent) + optional Zoneout.
 Activations: family-consistent (dont mix unless you explicitly warm-start).
 Ray:
 Data handles batching/packing/augmentation;
 Train runs AMP/FSDP/DeepSpeed & TBPTT;
 RLlib for recurrent PPO;
 Serve builds runtime graphs; plus A/B + shadow eval we set up.

LayerPurpose application: a runnable design
We add a purpose registry that maps a task/purpose to the exact cells/layers, regularization, PEFT, KD, and Raypipeline pieces to use. You can override anything, but the default gives you a strong recipe per purpose.
1) Purpose profiles (YAML)

Perfectlets focus the whole stack on your goal: optimize the wiring.By wiring we mean the graph-level choices (what connects to what, in what order and with what gates/normalizers) that control capacity, gradient flow, and information routing far more than raw parameter count.
Below is:
0. a toolbox of wiring optimizations (what, why, how),
0. a mapping to the Network-Atlas cells we defined (feed-forward, conv/deconv, pooling, probabilistic, RNN/GRU/LSTM),
0. task-specific recipes (top wins per domain), and
0. Ray Tune knobs to actually search these choices.

1) Wiring optimization toolbox (what  why  how)

	Lever (wiring)	Why it helps	How to apply (IR/Ray)
	Residual & Highway paths(ResNet/Highway)	Keeps gradients healthy through depth; supports deeper backbones with fewer pathologies.	Use block.resnet or add skip=true to blocks. Tune bottleneck expansion and stage depth. Optional DropPath(reg.stochastic_depth) for ConvNeXt/ViT-style stacks.
	Dense/multi-scale fusion(FPN/ASPP/UNet)	Preserves spatial detail & context; critical in det/seg/ocr.	neck=fpn for detection; aspp/decoder for DeepLab/UNet. Tune pyramid levels, ASPP rates, and decoder width.
	Attention & gating(SE/Squeeze-Excite, self/cross-attn)	Lets the model learn what to route where; improves long-range and channel selection.	Add se=True (ch. gating) inside conv blocks; for seq: TransformerEncoder/Decoder blocks. Tune num heads, qkv dim, se ratio.
	Convolutional shape (kernel, dilation, stride)	Controls RF and aliasing; large k/dilated = more global context.	Vary k{3,5,7}, dilation{1,2,4} (ASPP) and anti-alias pool.
	Pooling vs Interpolate(+1×1)	Interpolate+1×1 avoids checkerboard artifacts of deconv.	Prefer cell.interpolate + conv1x1 in decoders; only use deconv2d when you need learnable geometric mapping.
	Normalization placement(BN/LN/GN)	BN for conv; LN for transformer; mixing costs perf unless re-warmed.	Keep consistent with pretrained backbone (norm: bn for ResNet, ln for ViT/ConvNeXt). If you change, use warmupand BN stat reset.
	Activation choice	Impacts gradient scale & smoothness.	Keep ReLU (ResNet), SiLU (ConvNeXt/YOLO), GELU(transformers). Changing acts requires brief re-tune.
	DropBlock / Dropout / DropPath	Structured or path-level noise improves generalization without killing semantics.	CNN late-stages  DropBlock (reg.dropblock); heads  Dropout; modern deep blocks  DropPath(reg.stochastic_depth).
	Variational Dropout & Zoneout (RNN/GRU/LSTM)	Stabilizes temporal nets; reduces overfitting while preserving temporal coherence.	reg.rnn.variational_dropout_in/rec, reg.rnn.zoneout. We provided cells/var_dropout.py & cells/zoneout.py.
	Gating over recurrence(GRU/LSTM vs basic RNN)	GRU/LSTM fight vanishing; better memory.	Use cell.gru (fewer params) or cell.lstm when longer contexts are required.
	Probabilistic latents (VAE: / + reparam)	Forces information bottlenecks; encourages disentanglement.	cell.gauss_param from cells/gauss.py; tune z_dim, -KL, KL warmup.
	Adapters/PEFT (LoRA / IAł / Adapters / BitFit)	Add routing capacity at key junctions with tiny compute.	peft.lora.targets (e.g., layer4.*.conv3, attn.qkv), rank 416; IAł for multiplicative gates; BitFit for memory-starved.
	Distillation & feature alignment	Teacher signals route where to look; shrinks students with minimal loss.	kd_loss.py with adaptive T,  schedule, optional top-kteacher logits; feature MSE via 1×1 adapters.
	Task-vector merging	Transfers wiring behaviorbetween aligned models.	merge/task_vector.py with per-layer ; only on identical arch/tokenizer.
	Memory-augmented(NTM/DNC)	Explicit read/write routing; niche but powerful for algorithmic/trace tasks.	block.ntm with TBPTT; tune read/write heads, addressing; small seq first.
	Capsule routing(experimental)	Part-whole routing via agreement; interesting on simple datasets.	block.capsule macro; tune route iters; best as an experiment.
	2) Map these levers to the Network-Atlas cells
Atlas cells  what to pull for optimization:


 cell.ff (feed-forward): head Dropout; label-smoothing; LoRA on linear; KD distillation target.
 cell.conv2d: kernel/dilation/stride choices; SE gate; DropBlock; LoRA-conv or IAł gate on late blocks.
 cell.deconv2d / cell.interpolate: prefer interpolate + 1×1; if deconv2d, pick stride/kernels carefully.
 cell.pool: anti-alias pooling; set pool sizes that preserve small objects.
 cell.gauss_param: tune latent z_dim, -KL, schedule; use reparam cell (we shipped).
 cell.rnn: only for toy/demos; otherwise prefer GRU/LSTM; apply variational dropout.
 cell.gru: strong default for sequence tasks; tune hidden size & layers; apply zoneout lightly.
 cell.lstm: use for longer dependencies; zoneout + variational dropout; consider attention on top.
 Blocks/macros like block.resnet, block.aspp, block.fpn, TransformerEncoder: these are wiring bundlesthat combine the cells with residual/attention/fusion patterns.

3) Top wins per domain (why & how)
A) Detection (RetinaNet/FCOS/Faster-R-CNN)
 Multi-scale fusion (FPN)  small-object recall . Tune pyramid min/max levels.
 Late-stage conv LoRA (rank 8)  +capacity where it matters, minimal VRAM.
 DropBlock (p0.1, block=57) on C3/C4/C5  regularizes channel routing.
 IoU-aware head & focal =2.0  more stable positives; tune .
 Ray Tune grid: lr_head, lr_lora, dropblock.p, pyramid_levels, .
B) Segmentation (DeepLab v3+/UNet)
 ASPP dilations tailored to object scale; add decoder to recover boundaries.
 Interpolate+1×1 in decoder over deconv to avoid artifacts.
 Stochastic depth 0.1 on ConvNeXt; label smoothing 0.05.
 Tune: aspp_rates, decoder_width, drop_path, label_smoothing.
C) NLP classification/NER/RE
 LoRA on attention qkv (rank 8) + head Dropout 0.1  best bang for buck.
 KD from large teacher with adaptive T(24) and [0.8,0.95].
 Tune: lora.rank, head_p, T, , topk, max_seq_len.
D) OCR / seq2seq (CNN encoder + LSTM/attention decoder)
 LSTM/GRU with variational dropout (in=0.1, rec=0.1) + zoneout 0.05.
 CTC for line OCR (no alignment), or attn decoder for paragraph OCR.
 Tune: hidden size/layers, var-drop, zoneout, choice of CTC vs attn.
E) TTS/ASR
 Tacotron/Transformer-TTS: LoRA on attention; vocoder EMA; teacher forcing ratio schedule.
 ASR: CTC + SpecAugment; GRU/Conformer; KD from a stronger acoustic model.
 Tune: specaug masks, lora rank, EMA decay, CTC blank scale.
F) GAN/Diffusion
 EMA on G, dual AMP scalers, grad-clip 1.0, noise schedule as a hyperparam.
 Prefer v-prediction on high-res; dynamic thresholding.
 Tune: sched, v-pred vs , guidance scale, EMA decay.
G) RL (PPO)
 Frozen encoder + tiny actor/critic with LoRA rank 4 for visual tasks.
 PPO: KL penalty 0.020.1, clip 0.2; advantage-norm; small entropy (0.01).
 Tune: lr, kl_coeff, clip, lora_rank, rollout_len.

4) What to search with Ray Tune (quick grids)
tune_space = {
 # model wiring
 "neck.depth": tune.choice([1,2,3]), # FPN depth
 "aspp.rates": tune.choice([(6,12,18),(12,24,36)]),
 "decoder.width": tune.choice([128,256]),
 "se.ratio": tune.choice([None, 0.0625, 0.125]),
 # PEFT
 "peft.lora.rank": tune.choice([4,8,16]),
 # regularization
 "reg.dropblock.p": tune.uniform(0.05, 0.15),
 "reg.stochastic_depth.drop_prob": tune.choice([0.0, 0.05, 0.1]),
 "reg.rnn.variational_dropout_in": tune.choice([0.0, 0.1]),
 "reg.rnn.zoneout": tune.choice([0.0, 0.05]),
 # KD
 "kd.T": tune.choice([2.0, 3.0, 4.0]),
 "kd.alpha": tune.choice([0.8, 0.9, 0.95]),
 "kd.topk": tune.choice([0, 16, 32]),
 # opt
 "optim.lr_head": tune.loguniform(1e-5, 5e-4),
 "optim.lr_lora": tune.loguniform(5e-6, 2e-4)
}

5) Guardrails & failure modes (so wiring changes dont destabilize)
 Norm/Act mismatch with pretrained?  reset BN stats, warmup 13 epochs; keep act consistent per family.
 Deconv checkerboard?  switch to interpolate+1×1.
 RNN exploding/vanishing?  add variational dropout, zoneout, grad-clip, lower LR.
 GAN NaNs?  lower LR, use dual scalers, verify loss type; clip 1.0; EMA decay 0.9990.9999.
 KD hurts?  increase T, increase  (softer teacher), enable top-k.
 Task-vector regressions?  per-layer  scaling; only merge aligned arch/tokenizer.

6) Example: map wiring choices to Atlas nodes in configs
Detection (Retina)
model:
 backbone: resnet50
 neck: fpn(levels=3) # multi-scale fusion wiring
 head: retina
peft:
 lora: { targets: ["backbone.layer4.*.conv3"], rank: 8 } # LoRA on conv cells
reg:
 dropblock: { enabled: true, p: 0.10, block_size: 7, targets: ["backbone.layer3","backbone.layer4"] }
 stochastic_depth: { drop_prob: 0.0 }
OCR (CNN + LSTM)
encoder:
 - cell.conv2d(k=3) x2
 - cell.pool(k=2)
 - cell.conv2d(k=3) x2
 - cell.pool(k=2)
 - reshape_to_seq(axis="width")
 - cell.lstm(hidden=512, layers=2, bidir=true)
decoder:
 - cell.lstm(hidden=512, layers=2)
 - cell.ff(out_dim=vocab_size)
reg:
 rnn: { variational_dropout_in: 0.1, variational_dropout_rec: 0.1, zoneout: 0.05 }
NLP (BERT + LoRA + KD)
peft:
 lora: { targets: ["encoder.layer.*.attention.self.(query|value)"], rank: 8 }
kd:
 enabled: true
 T: 3.0
 alpha: 0.9
 topk: 32
reg:
 dropout: { head_p: 0.1 }

How we iterate
0. Start with family-consistent backbone and task-appropriate neck/head.
0. Flip on routing aids (FPN/ASPP/attention) and regularizers (DropBlock/DropPath/variational-drop).
0. Add PEFT at the tightest bottlenecks (late conv or attention projections).
0. If you have a stronger model, add KD (T, , top-k).
0. Run a small Ray Tune sweep over just 610 knobs (above).
0. Promote models via Serve A/B + shadow replay (we wired this).

Got it  you want a paper-by-paper mapping: for each reference in the archive (Rosenblatt, ResNet, GAN, VAE, etc.), well state:
 What operation/layer it informs
 Why it matters for wiring optimization
 Which hyper-parameters it connects to
and then align each to your Network Atlas cells/blocks.

 Paper  Operation  Hyper-params
1. Rosenblatt 1958 (Perceptron)
 Operation: cell.ff (linear + bias + activation).
 Why: establishes feed-forward cell baseline, bias as escape from zero.
 HPs: output dim, bias init, activation choice, learning rate.
 Atlas: Feed-forward node.

2. Hopfield 1982 (Associative Memory)
 Operation: block.hopfield (fully connected recurrent with energy function).
 Why: shows stability attractors; reminds us dense recurrent wiring explodes connections.
 HPs: number of neurons, energy threshold, async vs sync update.
 Atlas: demo node, not for prod.

3. Kohonen 1982 (Self-Organizing Maps)
 Operation: block.som (competitive learning).
 Why: competitive wiring & neighborhood updates.
 HPs: learning rate, neighborhood radius decay.
 Atlas: optional, ties into unsupervised feature maps.

4. Deconv Nets (Zeiler 2010)
 Operation: cell.deconv2d vs cell.interpolate+conv1x1.
 Why: reveals deconv checkerboard artifacts; guides us to interpolation for clean upsampling.
 HPs: kernel size, stride, padding, choice of deconv vs interp.
 Atlas: decoder nodes.

5. Batch Normalization (2015)
 Operation: norm=bn.
 Why: stabilizes training; wiring position (pre- or post-act) crucial.
 HPs: , momentum, placement (before/after activation).
 Atlas: normalization edges.

6. ResNet (2015)
 Operation: block.resnet (residual skip wiring).
 Why: residual skip solves gradient vanishing; core to deep wiring optimization.
 HPs: depth (#blocks per stage), bottleneck width, skip type (identity vs projection).
 Atlas: backbone path nodes.

7. GAN (Goodfellow 2014)
 Operation: block.gan (dual network wiring: G and D).
 Why: adversarial feedback wiring; route gradients through discriminator.
 HPs: loss type (hinge, WGAN, non-sat), EMA decay, lr_G vs lr_D, clip norm.
 Atlas: generative loop.

8. VAE (Kingma & Welling 2013)
 Operation: cell.gauss_param (/ heads + reparam).
 Why: introduces stochastic latent wiring; regularizes bottleneck.
 HPs: z-dim, -KL weight, KL warmup schedule.
 Atlas: probabilistic latent node.

9. Greedy Layer-wise Pretraining (DBN, 2006)
 Operation: block.dbn (stacked RBMs).
 Why: shows layer-wise unsupervised pretrain for deep nets.
 HPs: hidden dims, contrastive divergence steps.
 Atlas: historical; optional unsupervised blocks.

10. Sparse Autoencoder (2007)
 Operation: cell.ff with sparsity penalty.
 Why: encourages sparse feature wiring.
 HPs: sparsity , target activation .
 Atlas: AE bottleneck node.

11. GRU (2014) & 12. LSTM (1997)
 Operation: cell.gru, cell.lstm.
 Why: gating to optimize temporal wiring (combat vanishing).
 HPs: hidden size, #layers, dropout p, zoneout p, bidirectional flag.
 Atlas: recurrent nodes.

13. Neural Turing Machine (2014)
 Operation: block.ntm (read/write memory).
 Why: explicit external wiring, differentiable addressing.
 HPs: #read heads, #write heads, memory slots, controller size.
 Atlas: memory nodes.

14. Capsule Networks (2017)
 Operation: block.capsule (vector neurons + routing by agreement).
 Why: part/whole routing optimization.
 HPs: capsule dim, routing iterations.
 Atlas: experimental capsule node.

15. Liquid State Machines (2002)
 Operation: block.reservoir.
 Why: sparse random recurrent wiring  reservoir computing.
 HPs: connectivity %, leak rate, reservoir size.
 Atlas: reservoir nodes.

16. Markov Chains (2013 primer)
 Operation: underlying math for cell.gauss_param and CRF edges.
 Why: influences sequential wiring assumptions.
 HPs: transition probabilities, order m.
 Atlas: probabilistic edge wiring.

17. GLiNER (2023)
 Operation: NER model; wiring = transformer + label prompts.
 Why: entity extraction; fits doc-AI pipeline.
 HPs: label set size, context window, dropout.
 Atlas: NLP head nodes.

18. ADA196234 (historic report)
 Operation: Perceptron/ADALINE.
 Why: baseline FF wiring; delta rule origins.
 HPs: learning rate, bias, threshold.
 Atlas: FF cell baseline.

19. neurips24.pdf (NeurIPS 2024)
 Operation: TBD (likely novel cell/block).
 Why: potential new optimization or routing trick.
 HPs: to be extracted.
 Atlas: will add once parsed.

20. 2604.pdf
 Operation: TBD.
 Why: unknown method; could affect cell or wiring.
 HPs: unknown until parsed.
 Atlas: placeholder.

 How to use this mapping
 Each paper corresponds to a cell/block in your Atlas.
 Each brings specific hyper-params that control routing, gating, or fusion.
 These hyper-params are the knobs we surface in IR and Ray Tune for optimization.
 Together, this makes your Network Atlas a hyper-param wiring atlas.

Paper  Operation  Hyperparameter Crosswalk
Purpose: fast recall of what each paper teaches us to optimize, mapped to your Network Atlas cells/blocks, with IR knobs and Ray Tune levers.
Legend:Op = operation/layer the paper informs · Why = wiring optimization benefit · IR = knobs you set in your model config · Tune = suggested Ray Tune search space · Atlas = cell/block

1) Rosenblatt (1958)  Perceptron
Op: cell.ff (Linear + bias + act)Why: baseline feedforward wiring; bias prevents dead outputs.IR: cell.ff(out_dim, act={relu|silu|gelu}, dropout=p)Tune: lr[1e-4,1e-2], dropout[0.0,0.2], weight initAtlas: Feedforward node

2) Hopfield (1982)  Associative Memory
Op: block.hopfield (fully connected, symmetric weights, energy minimization)Why: stability/attractors; shows cost of fully connected recurrent wiring.IR: hopfield(num_units, async={true|false})Tune: num_units, async vs sync update scheduleAtlas: Demo node (not prod)

3) Kohonen (1982)  SelfOrganizing Maps (SOM)
Op: block.som (competitive learning, neighborhood updates)Why: topographic competitive wiring; unsupervised feature maps.IR: som(grid=(h,w), radius_decay, lr_decay)Tune: radius0radiusT, lr0lrTAtlas: Optional unsupervised block

4) Zeiler et al. (2010)  Deconvolutional Networks
Op: cell.deconv2d vs cell.interpolate+conv1x1Why: deconv can cause checkerboard artifacts; interpolation is often cleaner.IR: prefer interpolate(mode=bilinear) + conv1x1 in decoders; if deconv2d(k,s,p), set strides/kernels carefully.Tune: k{3,4}, s{2}, interp={bilinear,bicubic}Atlas: Decoder nodes

5) Ioffe & Szegedy (2015)  Batch Normalization
Op: norm=bnWhy: stabilizes training/gradient flow; placement matters (pre/postact).IR: bn(eps, momentum, placement={pre|post})Tune: eps[1e-5,1e-3], momentum[0.01,0.1]Atlas: Normalization edges

6) He et al. (2015)  ResNet
Op: block.resnet (residual skip wiring, bottlenecks)Why: deep networks trainable via identity shortcuts; core wiring optimization.IR: resnet(stage_depths, width_factor, projection={true|false})Tune: stage_depths, width_factor, lr, DropPath for modern variantsAtlas: Backbone path

7) Goodfellow et al. (2014)  GAN
Op: block.gan (adversarial GD wiring)Why: adversarial feedback routes gradients from D to G.IR: gan(loss={hinge|wgan|non_sat}, ema_decay, g_lr, d_lr)Tune: ema[0.999,0.9999], clip_grad1.0, schedule typesAtlas: Generative loop

8) Kingma & Welling (2013)  VAE
Op: cell.gauss_param (/ + reparam) with KLWhy: stochastic bottleneck; disentanglement and regularized routing.IR: gauss_param(z_dim), loss.kl(beta, warmup)Tune: z_dim[16,256], beta[0.5,2.0], warmup scheduleAtlas: Probabilistic latent node

9) Hinton et al. (2006)  Greedy LayerWise Pretraining (DBN/RBM)
Op: block.dbn (stacked RBMs)Why: unsupervised pretrain aids very deep nets (historic).IR: dbn(layers=[h1,h2,...], cd_k)Tune: cd_k[1,10], layer sizes, sparsity penaltiesAtlas: Optional pretrain block

10) Ranzato et al. (2007)  Sparse AutoEncoders
Op: cell.ff with sparsity penaltyWhy: sparse feature routing/bottlenecks.IR: loss.sparse(kld_weight=lambda, target_rho)Tune: lambda[1e-4,1e-2], rho[0.02,0.2]Atlas: AE bottleneck

11) Cho/Chung et al. (2014)  GRU
Op: cell.gru (update/reset gates)Why: efficient gated temporal routing.IR: gru(hidden, layers, bidir) + reg.rnnTune: hidden[128,1024], layers[1,4], var_drop[0.0,0.2], zoneout[0.0,0.1]Atlas: Recurrent node

12) Hochreiter & Schmidhuber (1997)  LSTM
Op: cell.lstm (input/output/forget gates + cell state)Why: combats vanishing; longer context.IR: lstm(hidden, layers, bidir) + reg.rnnTune: as above; consider attention on topAtlas: Recurrent node

13) Graves et al. (2014)  Neural Turing Machine (NTM)
Op: block.ntm (external memory, differentiable addressing)Why: explicit read/write routing; algorithmic tasks.IR: ntm(read_heads, write_heads, slots, controller_dim)Tune: heads[1,4], slots size, controller sizeAtlas: Memory node

14) Sabour et al. (2017)  Capsule Networks
Op: block.capsule (vector capsules + routing by agreement)Why: part/whole routing; pose awareness.IR: capsule(dim, routing_iters)Tune: dim[8,32], iters[1,5]Atlas: Experimental capsule node

15) Maass et al. (2002)  Liquid State Machines (Reservoir)
Op: block.reservoir (sparse random recurrent)Why: rich temporal dynamics with fixed wiring.IR: reservoir(size, connectivity, leak)Tune: size[256,4096], connectivity[0.01,0.1], leak[0.0,1.0]Atlas: Reservoir node

16) Hayes (2013)  Markov Chains Primer
Op: probabilistic edges / CRFstyle transitionsWhy: sequential dependence assumptions.IR: transition weights, order mTune: temperature/priors in decodingAtlas: Probabilistic edges

17) GLiNER (2023)  Zero/FewShot NER
Op: Transformer encoder with labelaware promptingWhy: entity extraction wiring in docAI.IR: gliner(model, labels, max_len, dropout)Tune: max_len[256,1024], dropout[0.0,0.2]Atlas: NLP head node

18) ADA196234  Historic (Perceptron/ADALINE Era)
Op: cell.ff / delta rule foundationsWhy: context for FF training; threshold/bias lore.IR/Tune: learning rate, bias; (historic)Atlas: FF baseline

19) neurips24.pdf  (NeurIPS 2024; TBD)
Op: TBD (novel cell/block/regularizer)Why: likely a new routing or normalization trickIR/Tune: to be extracted postreadAtlas: placeholder

20) 2604.pdf  (TBD)
Op: TBDWhy: unknown; we will classify after readingIR/Tune: TBDAtlas: placeholder

Quick wiring leverage summary
 Residual & fusion (ResNet, FPN/ASPP)  core gradient and multiscale routing.
 Normalization/activation (BN/LN; ReLU/SiLU/GELU)  keep consistent with pretrain.
 Temporal gates (GRU/LSTM + variational dropout/zoneout)  stable sequence wiring.
 Probabilistic latents (VAE)  regularized bottlenecks.
 Adapters & distillation (LoRA/IAł, KD)  efficient capacity & teacher guidance.
 Generative loops (GAN with EMA/dual scalers)  safe adversarial routing.

awesome  here are ready-to-run Ray Tune grids per batch, aligned to the mathematical operations at each layer(conv kernel/stride/dilation/padding, attention heads/QKV dims, norm eps/momentum, residual depth/width, RNN gating, etc.), plus threading knobs (Ray Data/DataLoader concurrency) so you can push the hardware efficiently.
I keep the code copy-pasteable. Each grid is a param_space dict you can plug into:
from ray import tune
from ray.tune import Tuner, TuneConfig
from ray.train import RunConfig

tuner = Tuner(
 my_trainer, # TorchTrainer or RLlib algo
 param_space={ "train_loop_config": GRID }, # <- pick one GRID below
 tune_config=TuneConfig(metric="val_metric", mode="max", num_samples=32),
 run_config=RunConfig(name="study_name")
)
tuner.fit()
The keys map 1:1 to our IR. E.g., conv.k, conv.s, conv.pad, bn.eps, attn.heads, res.stage_depths, fpn.levels, etc.

Shared threading & IO knobs (add to any GRID)
THREADING = {
 # Ray Data
 "io.prefetch_blocks": tune.choice([0, 1, 2]), # pipeline depth
 "io.target_max_block_size": tune.choice([64<<20, 128<<20]), # 64/128MB blocks
 "io.num_cpus_per_task": tune.choice([0.5, 1, 2]),
 # Torch DataLoader
 "dl.num_workers": tune.choice([2, 4, 8]),
 "dl.prefetch_factor": tune.choice([2, 4]),
 "dl.pin_memory": tune.choice([True, False]),
 # Torch threading (intra/interop)
 "torch.threads": tune.choice([1, 2, 4]),
}
Use torch.set_num_threads(cfg["torch.threads"]); for GPU-heavy models, threads=12 often wins.

Batch 01  Vision (Detection/Segmentation/Backbones)
(A) RetinaNet (one-stage dense detector; focal loss; FPN)
RETINA_GRID = {
 # Image & FPN wiring
 "img.size": tune.choice([640, 800, 1024]),
 "fpn.levels": tune.choice([[3,4,5], [3,4,5,6]]), # P3-P5 or P3-P6
 "fpn.width": tune.choice([128, 256]),

 # Convolution math (C3C5 late blocks)
 "conv.k": tune.choice([3, 5]), # kernel size
 "conv.s": 1, # stride
 "conv.pad": tune.choice(["same", "valid"]), # padding
 "conv.dilation": tune.choice([1, 2]), # atrous
 # Norm
 "bn.eps": tune.choice([1e-5, 1e-4]),
 "bn.momentum": tune.choice([0.1, 0.01]),

 # Residual depth (ResNet backbone)
 "res.stage_depths": tune.choice([(3,4,6,3), (3,4,23,3)]), # 50 vs 101
 "res.width_factor": tune.choice([1.0, 1.25]),

 # Head geometry
 "head.width": tune.choice([256, 384]),
 "head.depth": tune.choice([4, 6]),

 # Focal & box losses
 "loss.focal.gamma": tune.choice([1.5, 2.0, 2.5, 3.0]),
 "loss.focal.alpha": tune.choice([0.25, 0.5]),
 "loss.box.iou": tune.choice(["giou", "diou", "ciou"]),

 # Regularization
 "reg.dropblock.p": tune.uniform(0.05, 0.15),
 "reg.dropblock.block": tune.choice([5, 7]),
 "reg.stochastic_depth.p": tune.choice([0.0, 0.05]),

 # PEFT (late conv adapters)
 "peft.lora.rank": tune.choice([4, 8, 16]),

 # Optim & schedule
 "optim.lr_head": tune.loguniform(1e-5, 5e-4),
 "optim.lr_lora": tune.loguniform(5e-6, 2e-4),
 "sched.type": tune.choice(["cosine", "onecycle"]),
 **THREADING
}
Math mapping
 Conv: y = Conv(W, x; k, s, pad, dilation) + b; tuning k, dilation, pad changes RF & aliasing.
 BN: y = (x - )/sqrt(˛+) *  + ; eps avoids div-by-0, momentum controls running stats.
 Residual: y = F(x) + x stabilizes gradients across layers.

(B) DeepLab v3+ (semantic segmentation; ASPP + decoder)
DEEPLAB_GRID = {
 "backbone": tune.choice(["resnet50", "convnext_tiny"]),
 "output_stride": tune.choice([8, 16]), # affects dilation pattern
 "aspp.rates": tune.choice([(6,12,18), (12,24,36)]),
 "decoder.width": tune.choice([128, 256]),
 "decoder.upsample": tune.choice(["interpolate", "deconv"]), # math choice
 "conv.k": tune.choice([3, 5]),
 "conv.pad": tune.choice(["same", "valid"]),
 "bn.eps": tune.choice([1e-5, 1e-4]),
 "reg.drop_path": tune.choice([0.0, 0.1]), # ConvNeXt
 "reg.label_smoothing": tune.choice([0.0, 0.05, 0.1]),
 "optim.lr": tune.loguniform(5e-6, 3e-4),
 **THREADING
}
Prefer interpolate+1×1 for decoder to avoid checkerboard.

(C) Backbone swap (ResNet vs ConvNeXt)
BACKBONE_GRID = {
 "backbone": tune.choice(["resnet50", "resnet101", "convnext_tiny", "convnext_small"]),
 "res.stage_depths": tune.choice([(3,4,6,3), (3,4,23,3)]),
 "convnext.depths": tune.choice([(3,3,9,3), (3,3,27,3)]),
 "convnext.widths": tune.choice([(96,192,384,768), (128,256,512,1024)]),
 "act": tune.choice(["relu", "silu"]),
 "reg.drop_path": tune.choice([0.0, 0.05, 0.1]),
 "bn.eps": tune.choice([1e-5, 1e-4]),
 **THREADING
}

(D) StyleGAN2/3 (image synthesis)
STYLEGAN_GRID = {
 "g.lr": tune.loguniform(1e-5, 2e-4),
 "d.lr": tune.loguniform(1e-5, 2e-4),
 "ema.decay": tune.choice([0.999, 0.9995, 0.9999]),
 "loss.type": tune.choice(["hinge", "non_sat", "wgan_gp"]),
 "loss.r1.gamma": tune.choice([0.0, 1.0, 10.0]),
 "g.mapping.depth": tune.choice([4, 8]),
 "g.channels.mult": tune.choice([1.0, 1.25]),
 "upsample": tune.choice(["interpolate", "deconv"]), # aliasing control
 "clip_grad": tune.choice([0.0, 1.0]),
 **THREADING
}
(E) VAE (/; reparam; KL)

How to attach a grid to a trainer
Example for Retina:
from ray.train.torch import TorchTrainer
trainer = TorchTrainer(
 train_loop_per_worker=retina_train_loop,
 train_loop_config={}, # Tune will inject here from RETINA_GRID
 scaling_config={"num_workers": 4, "use_gpu": True},
 datasets={"train": train_ds, "val": val_ds}
)
tuner = Tuner(trainer, param_space={"train_loop_config": RETINA_GRID}, tune_config=TuneConfig(metric="mAP", mode="max", num_samples=32))
tuner.fit()
Inside retina_train_loop, read cfg = session.get_trial_resources().get_config() (or Ray Train get_context().get_config() depending on API version) and apply to your IR: set conv.k, conv.pad, build FPN with provided levels, configure BN eps/momentum, etc.

Notes on layer-math alignment & ops
 Padding:
 "same"  pad = (k1)/2 (keeps spatial size for stride=1).
 "valid"  pad = 0 (shrinks spatial size).
 Ensure anchors/ASPP rates still align to feature maps when changing padding/stride.
 Stride vs dilation:
 Increasing stride downsamples; increasing dilation enlarges receptive field without downsampling (holes).
 For DeepLab, higher output_stride reduces dilation, and vice-versa.
 Attention heads:
 head_dim = d_model / n_heads (keep divisible).
 Q/K/V dims should be aligned; LoRA target lists pick query|value projections.
 Normalization:
 BN: prefer eps=1e-5, momentum0.1 for ResNets; if changed, reset stats + warmup.
 LN: transformer/ConvNeXt; eps=1e-6-ish default.
 Residual depth:
 stage_depths controls number of bottleneck blocks per stage; deeper models need DropPath.
 Decoder choice:
 Prefer interpolate+1×1 over deconv to avoid checkerboards; only use deconv when geometry learning is required.
 RNN dropout:
 Use variational dropout (fixed mask per sequence) for input/recurrent links; zoneout 0.05 for stability.

If you want, I can push these grids into your canvas under each batch (Tune grids sections) or attach pre-wired starter scripts (retina_tune.py, bert_tune.py, diffusion_tune.py, etc.) that instantiate the right trainer and merge THREADING + batch-specific grids automatically.

Mathematical Appendix (Part 1)  Convolution, Pooling, Residual
Convolution
 Output shape:H_out = floor((H + 2p  d(k1)  1)/s + 1).Params: k^2 * C_in * C_out + C_out.FLOPs: 2 * H_out * W_out * k^2 * C_in * C_out.
 Tune knobs: kernel size, stride, padding, dilation, in/out channels.
Deconvolution
 Output shape:H_out = s(H1)  2p + d(k1) + output_pad + 1.
 Risk of checkerboard artifacts  prefer interpolate+1×1.
Pooling
 No params. Same output shape formula as conv.
 Max vs avg tunes invariance.
Residual connections
 Identity: y = F(x) + x (requires channel/stride match).
 Projection: 1×1 conv to align shapes.
Threading: for conv-heavy models set torch.threads=12, rely on GPU kernels, tune dl.num_workers.

Mathematical Appendix (Part 2)  Attention & RNNs
Self-Attention
 Inputs: [B,L,d_model].
 Q,K,V: [B,h,L,d_k], with d_k = d_model/h.
 Output: [B,L,d_model].
 Params per layer: 4 d_model^2 (Q,K,V,O). FFN 2 d_model^2  (=expansion factor).
 FLOPs: O(B h L^2 d_k).
 Tune knobs: d_model, heads, depth, dropout, activation, positional encodings.
GRU
 z = (W_z x + U_z h)
 r = (W_r x + U_r h)
 h~ = tanh(W_h x + U_h (rh))
 h' = (1z)h + zh~
 Tune knobs: hidden size, layers, dropout, bidirectional flag.
LSTM
 i,f,o gates + candidate c~.
 c' = fc + ic~, h' = otanh(c').
 Tune knobs: hidden size, layers, variational dropout, zoneout.
Threading: for RNN-heavy tasks, use shorter rollout.len (RLlib) and TBPTT length control (Ray Train).

Mathematical Appendix (Part 3)  Probabilistic, Losses, Diffusion
VAE
 Reparam: z =  +  exp(log).
 KL: 0.5 (˛+˛log˛1).
 Tune knobs: z_dim, -KL, warmup.
GAN Losses
 Hinge, WGAN-GP, R1.
 Tune knobs: loss type,  (GP),  (R1), lr_G, lr_D.
Diffusion (DDPM)
 Forward: q(x_t|x0)=N(_t x0,(1_t)I).
 Reverse: (x_t,t).
 CFG: ę = (1+s)_cond  s _uncond.
 Tune knobs: schedule type, steps, guidance, EMA decay.

Dimensional Ledger
 CV tensors: [B,C,H,W]; ensure divisible by stride product (e.g., 32).
 NLP tensors: [B,L,D]; align max_len to multiple of 8/16.
 Graph batches: (#nodes,#edges).
 Seq OCR: conv features flattened over width/time.
 Practice: add spec.in/out per module (shape,dtype,layout).

Precision & Compactness
 1-bit, 4-bit (nf4), 8-bit, 16-bit (fp16/bf16), 32/64-bit.
 Model size  (bits/param × params)/8.
 Mixed precision: forward in bf16/fp16, keep norms/softmax in FP32.
 QLoRA: base 4-bit, adapters 16-bit.

Logging Schema
Example per-trial ledger:
{
 "shapes": {"input": "[B,3,640,640]", "C3": "[B,256,80,80]"},
 "params": {"total": 3.5e7, "backbone": 2.3e7},
 "flops": {"total_gmac": 120.5},
 "precision": {"weights": "bf16", "norm": "fp32"},
 "quant": {"base_bits": 4, "adapters_bits": 16}
}

Mathematical Appendix (Part 4)  Advanced Blocks
FPN (Feature Pyramid Network)
 Combines multi-scale features: P3P7.
 Formula: P_l = Conv1x1(C_l) + Upsample(P_{l+1}).
 Tune knobs: #levels (P3P5 vs P3P7), channel width, fusion method (sum/concat/weighted).
 Padding: align spatial sizes; use same or explicit crop.
ASPP (Atrous Spatial Pyramid Pooling)
 Parallel dilated convs: y =  Conv_dil(x).
 Tune knobs: dilation rates (e.g. 6,12,18), #branches, global pool branch inclusion.
 FLOPs  (dilated conv FLOPs).
 Padding: ensure receptive fields fit within feature maps.
Capsule Routing
 Vector outputs; squash nonlinearity: v_j = (||s_j||˛ / (1+||s_j||˛))(s_j/||s_j||).
 Routing: c_ij = softmax(b_ij), s_j =  c_ij ű_j|i.
 Iteratively update b_ij  b_ij + ű_j|i·v_j.
 Tune knobs: capsule dim, #routing iters, squash variant.
 Compute cost: O(N_caps˛) per iteration.
Neural Turing Machine (NTM)
 External memory matrix M[N_slots, dim].
 Read weights w^r = softmax( K(u,M) + g shift +  sharpen).
 Write: erase/add vectors.
 Tune knobs: #read heads, #write heads, slots N, controller dim.
 Threading: heavy sequential ops  prefer small batch parallelization.
Reservoir / Liquid State Machines
 Sparse recurrent wiring.
 State update: x_{t+1} = (1)x_t +  f(W_in u_t + W x_t).
 Tune knobs: reservoir size, leak rate , sparsity/connectivity.
 Precision: often stable in fp32 only.
Temporal Convolutional Networks (TCN)
 Causal 1D conv with dilation.
 Output: length preserved with padding=(k1)d.
 Residual skip adds.
 Tune knobs: kernel k, dilation schedule, depth, dropout.
 Threading: conv1d kernels scale well; tune batch size.

Mathematical Appendix (Part 5)  Hybrid & Multimodal
CLIP / Multimodal Contrastive
 Encoders f_img, f_txt.
 Loss: L =  log exp(sim(f_img, f_txt)/) /  exp(sim/).
 Tune knobs: embed dim, temp , max_len, projection depth.
Retrieval-Augmented Generation (RAG)
 Pipeline: retrieverreader.
 Score fusion: weighted sum of log-probs.
 Tune knobs: top-k docs, retriever index type, fusion weight .
Visual Question Answering (VQA)
 Fuse image feat [B,C,H,W] and text feat [B,L,D].
 Fusion ops: concat, bilinear pool, cross-attn.
 Tune knobs: fusion dim, heads, depth.

Padding / Layer Ledger Addendum
 FPN/ASPP: ensure feature maps aligned via integer strides; maintain divisibility.
 Capsules: ensure vector norms stable (may require layer norm).
 NTM: memory slots × dim grows quickly; watch memory footprint.
 Reservoir: sparsity pattern seeded; keep connectivity % small.


Mathematical Appendix (Part 4)  MultiScale Fusion (FPN / BiFPN / ASPP / PSP)
FPN (Feature Pyramid Network)
 Backbone maps: C2,C3,C4,C5 with strides s={4,8,16,32} for ResNetstyle (input H×W).P5 = Conv3×3(C5); P4 = Conv3×3(Conv1×1(C4) + upsample(P5)); P3 = Conv3×3(Conv1×1(C3) + upsample(P4)).Optional P6,P7 via stride2 conv from P5 for large objects.
 Shapes: P_l has H/s_l × W/s_l with s_l  {8,16,32,64,128} depending on the pyramid level.
 Anchors: base size a_l = a0·2^(ll0); aspect ratios r{0.5,1,2}.
 Tune knobs: levels {P3..P5|P6}, lateral width, smoothing conv (3×3), upsample mode.
BiFPN (EfficientDet)
 Weighted fusion: y = _i (w_i x_i) / (_i w_i + ), with w_i  0 (learned, reluclamped).
 Depthwise separable conv after fusion to reduce params/FLOPs.
 Topdown & bottomup fusion repeated R times.
 Tune knobs: repeats R, width,  for stability.
ASPP (DeepLab)
 Parallel atrous branches: Conv3×3 with dilation rates (r1,r2,r3) + image pooling branch; concat then 1×1 projection.
 RF grows with dilation; ensure rates fit output_stride (8 or 16).
 Tune knobs: rates (e.g., (6,12,18) or (12,24,36)), projection width, output_stride.
PSP (Pyramid Pooling)
 Pooling bins: pool to fixed grids (1×1, 2×2, 3×3, 6×6), upsample to original feat size, concat, 1×1 projection.
 Purpose: global context injection with low cost.
 Tune knobs: bin sizes, projection width, fusion order.
Dim ledger tips: Track spatial sizes across pyramid; ensure input size divisible by largest stride (e.g., 32). Anchors bound to Plevel strides.

Mathematical Appendix (Part 5)  Capsules & External Memory
Capsule Networks (Dynamic Routing)
 Squash nonlinearity: v_j = (||s_j||^2 / (1 + ||s_j||^2)) * (s_j / ||s_j||), where s_j = _i c_ij ^u_ij and ^u_ij = W_ij u_i.
 Routing logits update: c_ij = softmax_j(b_ij); b_ij  b_ij + ^u_ij · v_j.
 Dims: u_i  R^{d_in}, v_j  R^{d_out}, W_ij  R^{d_out×d_in}.
 Tune knobs: d_out (caps dim), routing iterations (15), number of capsules per layer.
Neural Turing Machine (NTM)  Read/Write
 Content addressing: w_c^t = softmax(^t * cos(k^t, M^{t1})), 0.
 Interpolation: w_g^t = g^t w_c^t + (1g^t) w^{t1}, g[0,1].
 Shift: ~w^t = conv_shift(w_g^t, s^t) with shift distribution s.
 Sharpen: w^t  (~w^t)^{^t}, 1.
 Read: r^t = _i w^t_i M^{t1}_i.
 Write: erase e^t  [0,1]^W, add a^t  R^WM^t = M^{t1}  (1  w^t e^{tT}) + w^t a^{tT}.
 Dims: memory M  R^{N×W}; weights w^t  ^N.
 Tune knobs: N (slots), W (width), #read/#write heads, ,g, ranges.
Dim ledger tips: Keep explicit N×W memory sizes; ensure controller outputs (k^t,e^t,a^t,s^t) have correct shapes.

Mathematical Appendix (Part 6)  PPO / GAE (RL)
PPO Objective
 Probability ratio: r_t() = _(a_t|s_t) / _{_old}(a_t|s_t).
 Clipped surrogate: L^CLIP = E_t[ min( r_t A_t, clip(r_t, 1, 1+) A_t ) ].
 Value & entropy: L^V = (V_  V_targ)^2, L^H =  _ log _.
 Total loss: L = L^CLIP  c1 L^V + c2 L^H.
GAE (Generalized Advantage Estimation)
 _t = r_t +  V(s_{t+1})  V(s_t).
 A_t = _{l=0}^{Tt1} ( )^l _{t+l}.
Tune knobs:  (clip), c1 (value coef), c2 (entropy coef), , , rollout length, minibatch size, learning rate.
Threading: Increase num_workers in RLlib for environment parallelism; constrain DataLoader workers to avoid contention on the same node.

Mathematical Appendix (Part 7)  Advanced Blocks
DNC (Differentiable Neural Computer)
 Extends NTM with temporal linkage + usage vectors.
 Temporal linkage: L^t[i,j] tracks that memory i was written just before j.
 Precedence: p^t = (1 w_write^t) p^{t1} + w_write^t.
 Link update: L^t = (1w_write^t  1  1  w_write^t)  L^{t1} + w_write^t  p^{t1}.
 Usage: u^t = (u^{t1} + w_write^{t1}  u^{t1}w_write^{t1})(1^t), with free gates .
 Tune knobs: memory N,W; #heads; free gate ranges; temporal linkage on/off.
BiGRU / BiLSTM with TBPTT
 BiGRU/LSTM: same as GRU/LSTM but process seq forward & backward, concat states.
 Shapes: input [B,L,D], output [B,L,2H].
 TBPTT: truncate backprop at window k; carry hidden states between chunks.
 Tune knobs: hidden H, layers, dropout, bidir flag, TBPTT length.
Detection Anchors (RetinaNet/YOLO)
 Anchors: base size a0, perlevel scale factor s=2; aspect ratios r.
 Box: (x,y,w,h) anchor; predicted offsets (tx,ty,tw,th).
 Transform: x = (tx * wa) + xa; y = (ty * ha) + ya; w = exp(tw) * wa; h = exp(th) * ha.
 Tune knobs: base size, scales per octave, aspect ratios, stride.
 Threading note: anchor generation can be vectorized; avoid Python loops.
ControlNet (Conditioning Adapters)
 Takes encoder feature map F  R^{B,C,H,W}, condition map C (edges/pose/depth).
 Align shapes: downsample C to Fs (H,W), project channels with 1×1 conv.
 Fuse: F' = F + Conv3×3(ReLU(C_proj)).
 Tune knobs: control scale (), adapter depth (n), reso of hint.
 Dim ledger: ensure condition reso divisible by UNet stride pyramid.

Notes
 Each advanced block now has explicit math (equations), shapes, and tune knobs.
 This completes the calculus for core Atlas nodes (conv, attn, RNNs, latent, GAN, diffusion, FPN, ASPP, capsules, NTM/DNC, anchors, ControlNet).

Mathematical Appendix (Part 7)  Detection Anchors, Box Parametrization, IoU Losses
Anchors & Feature Strides
 For pyramid level P_l with stride s_l (e.g., 8,16,32,64,128), anchor centers are at pixel grid multiples of s_l in input space.
 Anchor size: a_l = a_0 · 2^{ll_0}; aspect ratios r{0.5,1,2}. Width/height: w=(a_l^2/r), h=(a_l^2·r).
Box Encoding (t_x, t_y, t_w, t_h)
 Given anchor (x_a,y_a,w_a,h_a) and gt (x,y,w,h):t_x=(xx_a)/w_a, t_y=(yy_a)/h_a, t_w=log(w/w_a), t_h=log(h/h_a).
 Pred decode: x=x_a + t_x·w_a, y=y_a + t_y·h_a, w=w_a·exp(t_w), h=h_a·exp(t_h).
IoU-family Losses
 IoU: area(intersection)/area(union).
 GIoU: IoU  (area(C)area(union))/area(C), where C is smallest enclosing box.
 DIoU: IoU  (^2(b,b_gt)/c^2), center distance penalty.
 CIoU: DIoU  ·v, with v measuring aspect ratio consistency, =v/(1IoU+v).
Tune knobs: anchor base a_0, level set {P3..P6}, aspect ratios, IoU variant, focal /; ensure input size divisible by max stride.

Mathematical Appendix (Part 8)  Positional Encodings (Sin/Cos, RoPE, ALiBi)
Sinusoidal (Vaswani)
 PE[pos,2i] = sin(pos / 10000^{2i/d_model}), PE[pos,2i+1] = cos(pos / 10000^{2i/d_model}).
Rotary Position Embedding (RoPE)
 Apply rotation to Q,K per head using angle (pos):RoPE(q_even,q_odd) = (q_even cos  q_odd sin, q_even sin + q_odd cos).Same for K; induces relative position in dotproduct.
ALiBi
 Add linear bias to attention scores per head:score_{ij}  score_{ij}  m_h · |ij|.
Tune knobs: PE type {sinusoidal, rope, alibi}, rope base, head slopes schedule; max_len (8/16 multiples).

Mathematical Appendix (Part 9)  Conditioning Adapters (ControlNet, FiLM, CrossAttn)
CrossAttention Conditioning
 Given encoder cond C  R^{B,L_c,d}, decoder states X  R^{B,L_x,d}:Attn(X,C) = softmax( (X W_q)(C W_k)^T / d_k ) (C W_v) W_o.
FiLM (Featurewise Linear Modulation)
 For conv features F:F' = (C)  F + (C), where , are small nets of conditioning signal C.
ControlNet (for Diffusion UNet)
 Duplicate UNet blocks to process conditioning (e.g., edges/pose/depth) into hint features; inject via add/concat into main residual blocks:h' = h + A(hint) or concat([h, A(hint)]).
Shapes: ensure hint spatial sizes match stage (downsample/upsample).Tune knobs: control scale, adapter depth, hint resolution, injection points.

Mathematical Appendix (Part 10)  Normalization & Regularization Details
Normalizations
 BatchNorm: y = (xmu)/sqrt(var+eps) * gamma + beta; running stats momentum m.
 LayerNorm: per-sample over features; eps1e5; no running stats.
 GroupNorm: channels split into G groups; normalize per group.
Placement: pre-activation vs post; keep same as pretrain.Knobs: eps, momentum (BN), groups (GN).
DropBlock
 Mask contiguous b×b blocks with prob p; rescale by keep prob.
 Best on late conv stages; b57.
Stochastic Depth (DropPath)
 Randomly drop residual branches with prob p (often linearly increasing with depth).
 Train: shorter effective depth; Eval: use full.
Knobs: p schedules for DropBlock/DropPath; head dropout for FFN heads.

Mathematical Appendix (Part 11)  DNC Temporal Linkage & Memory
Temporal Linkage Matrix
 Predecessor/successor links L_t  R^{N×N}, N=slots.
 Update: L_t = (1e_t 1^T  1 e_t^T)  L_{t1} + _i w^t_i r^t_i^T.
 Forward/backward read weights: f_t = L_t^T w^{t1}, b_t = L_t w^{t1}.
 Provides sequence order traversal through memory.
Knobs: N (slots), memory width, #heads, erase strength,  sharpening.

Mathematical Appendix (Part 12)  TBPTT & Sequence Packing
Truncated Backprop Through Time
 Effective horizon k: unroll k steps, detach hidden.
 Gradient only propagates within each window.
 Tradeoff: larger k  better longrange credit, smaller k  cheaper compute.
Packed/Padded Sequences
 Pack: input [B,L,D] with true lengths  sorted, packed to avoid wasted compute.
 Pad: pad all to max L, use mask in attention or CRF.
Knobs: TBPTT length k, batch sort strategy, max_len multiple of 8/16.

Mathematical Appendix (Part 13)  OCR/CTC Shape Ledger
Conv Feature to Sequence
 Input image [B,1,H,W]. After conv strides s1,s2,& along width, sequence length L_out = W / ( strides).
 Feature dim = channels × height after convs.
CTC State Sizes
 DP trellis: states = 2U+1 for target length U (including blanks).
 Complexity: O(TU), T=timesteps=L_out.
Knobs: stride schedule, blank index, beam width.

Mathematical Appendix (Part 14)  Compute & Activation Ledger
Parameters
 Linear: params = in·out + out.
 Conv: params = k^2 · C_in · C_out + C_out.
 Attention: Q,K,V,O = 4 d_model^2.
 RNN cell: params  (in+hidden)·hidden.
FLOPs
 Conv: 2 H_out W_out k^2 C_in C_out.
 Attention: O(B h L^2 d_k).
 RNN: O(T hidden^2).
Activations
 Conv activations: B·C·H·W.
 Attention: dominated by B·h·L^2.
 RNN: B·T·hidden.
Ledger practice: maintain table of (params, FLOPs, activations bytes) per block. Use to enforce budgets and check tradeoffs during Ray Tune sweeps.

 Next Steps
0. Integrate Appendix into IR: add spec.in/out, params, flops, activations fields for each module. Validate at build.
0. Extend Tune Trials: log math ledger JSON per trial; compare FLOPs/params vs val metrics  cost/quality trade curves.
0. Traceability tooling: autogenerate Atlas traces  path of ops with math/dim evidence, exported to JSON/Graphviz.
0. Prioritize blocks for calculus expansion: ControlNet variants, multimodal bridges (CLIP, VQA), multiagent RL.
0. Operationalize: add *_tune.py scripts to repo; run small Tune sweeps locally with threading/padding/precision policies applied.
0. Scale out: when validated, burst on Ray cluster; archive full math/dim ledger for reproducibility.
This completes the traceability layer: shapes, math, FLOPs, precision, hyperparams all logged per run. Next we should build the ledger utilities and the starter Tune scripts to operationalize it.

export:

 enabled: true
 path: "artifacts/model.onnx"

2) Ledger utility updated (dynamic FLOPs backend + ONNX export)
Put this in slate/utils/ledger.py.
# slate/utils/ledger.py
import json, contextlib, torch
from typing import Dict, Any, Optional

def count_params(model: torch.nn.Module) -> int:
 return sum(p.numel() for p in model.parameters())

@contextlib.contextmanager
def no_grad():
 try:
 torch.set_grad_enabled(False); yield
 finally:
 torch.set_grad_enabled(True)

def flops_fvcore(model, sample):
 try:
 from fvcore.nn import FlopCountAnalysis
 macs = FlopCountAnalysis(model, sample).total() # MACs
 return float(macs * 2.0) # convert to FLOPs
 except Exception:
 return -1.0

def flops_thop(model, sample):
 try:
 from thop import profile
 flops, params = profile(model, inputs=(sample,), verbose=False)
 return float(flops)
 except Exception:
 return -1.0

def compute_flops(model, sample, backend: str) -> float:
 if backend == "fvcore":
 return flops_fvcore(model, sample)
 if backend == "thop":
 return flops_thop(model, sample)
 return -1.0

def activation_bytes(t: torch.Tensor) -> int:
 bits = (torch.finfo(t.dtype).bits if t.dtype.is_floating_point else torch.iinfo(t.dtype).bits)
 return t.nelement() * (bits // 8)

def log_math_ledger(
 shapes: Dict[str,str],
 model: torch.nn.Module,
 sample_batch: Any,
 cfg: Dict[str, Any],
 extra: Optional[Dict[str,Any]] = None,
 fn_print=print
):
 params = count_params(model)
 flops = compute_flops(model, sample_batch, cfg.get("metrics",{}).get("flops_backend","none"))
 precision = cfg.get("precision", {"weights":"fp32","activations":"fp32","norm":"fp32"})
 quant = cfg.get("quant", {"base_bits": 32, "adapters_bits": 32})
 ledger = {
 "shapes": shapes,
 "params": {"total": params},
 "flops": {"total": flops}, # -1 if unavailable
 "precision": precision,
 "quant": quant
 }
 if extra: ledger.update(extra)
 fn_print("[MATH_LEDGER] " + json.dumps(ledger))

# ---------- ONNX export ----------
def export_to_onnx(model: torch.nn.Module, sample: Any, onnx_cfg: Dict[str,Any]) -> bool:
 if not onnx_cfg.get("enabled", False):
 return False
 path = onnx_cfg["path"]
 opset = onnx_cfg.get("opset", 17)
 dyn = onnx_cfg.get("dynamic_axes", None)
 do_fold = onnx_cfg.get("do_constant_folding", True)

 model.eval()
 torch.onnx.export(
 model, sample, path,
 input_names=list(dyn.keys()) if dyn else None,
 output_names=list(onnx_cfg.get("outputs", ["output"])),
 dynamic_axes=dyn,
 do_constant_folding=do_fold,
 opset_version=opset
 )

 # Optional simplify
 if onnx_cfg.get("simplify", False):
 try:
 import onnx
 from onnxsim import simplify
 onnx_model = onnx.load(path)
 model_simplified, check = simplify(onnx_model)
 if check: onnx.save(model_simplified, path)
 except Exception:
 pass

 # Optional runtime sanity check
 if onnx_cfg.get("runtime_check", False):
 try:
 import numpy as np, onnxruntime as ort
 providers = onnx_cfg.get("providers", ["CPUExecutionProvider"])
 sess = ort.InferenceSession(path, providers=providers)
 # Build feed dict from sample (assume dict or tensor)
 if isinstance(sample, dict):
 feed = {k: (v.detach().cpu().numpy() if isinstance(v, torch.Tensor) else v)
 for k,v in sample.items()}
 else:
 name = list(dyn.keys())[0] if dyn else "input"
 feed = {name: sample.detach().cpu().numpy()}
 _ = sess.run(None, feed)
 except Exception as e:
 print(f"[ONNX_RUNTIME_CHECK] failed: {e}")
 return True
Why this matters:
 FLOPs backend is configurable (fvcore / THOP / none), so hosts can inject preference without code edits.
 ONNX export is configurable & portable: opset, dynamic axes, simplify, onnxruntime check, and providers list.

3) Use the config in trainers (host injection)
Inside each *_tune.py loop, pass the full config into the ledger:
with no_grad():
 xb, yb = next(iter(val_loader))
 shapes = {"input": str(tuple(xb.shape))}
 log_math_ledger(
 shapes=shapes,
 model=model,
 sample_batch=xb,
 cfg=cfg, #  single source of truth
 extra={"padding": cfg.get("conv.pad","same")}
 )

# Optional: export to ONNX
from slate.utils.ledger import export_to_onnx
export_to_onnx(model, xb, cfg.get("export",{}).get("onnx", {}))
At launch time, you can inject config via:
 YAML: +cfg=project/configs/retina_local.yaml
 Ray Tune: param_space={"train_loop_config": RETINA_GRID | {"metrics":{"flops_backend":"thop"}}}
 ENV: read overrides and merge before building IR

4) ONNX-friendly model choices & guardrails
To keep exports portable and platform-agnostic, prefer:
 Interpolation: use mode="nearest" | "bilinear", align_corners=False; these map well to ONNX opset  13.
 Activations: SiLU, GELU, ReLU are supported in opset  14; if targeting older opsets, use approximations (fast-GELU) or switch to ReLU.
 GroupNorm/LayerNorm: supported; ensure epsilon scalar.
 Custom / Python control flow: avoid branching/loops inside forward; use Tensor ops only.
 DropPath/DropBlock: implement as no-ops at export (eval mode) or wrap under torch.jit.is_scripting()guards.
 Concats/Adds: keep channel-last concatenations consistent with ONNX shapes.
 RNN: prefer nn.GRU/LSTM over scripted cell loops; opset support is better.
 Detection decoders: if you keep post-processing (NMS) out of the graph, export only logits/boxes; do NMS in runtime (ONNXRuntime has NMS).
Quantization path (optional):
 PTQ (post-training quantization) with onnxruntime-quantization:
 dynamic quantization (matmul/linear), or static with calibration set.
 QAT (quant-aware training)  export to ONNX with Q/DQ nodes; ensure compatibility with desired EP (e.g., CUDA EP).

5) Serving with ONNX Runtime (optional)
Ray Serve handler using ONNX Runtime:
from ray import serve
import onnxruntime as ort
import numpy as np

@serve.deployment(num_replicas=2)
class ONNXModel:
 def __init__(self, onnx_path, providers=None):
 self.sess = ort.InferenceSession(onnx_path, providers=providers or ["CPUExecutionProvider"])
 self.input_name = self.sess.get_inputs()[0].name

 async def __call__(self, request):
 payload = await request.json()
 x = np.asarray(payload["input"], dtype=np.float32) # ensure dtype/shape match
 out = self.sess.run(None, {self.input_name: x})
 return {"output": out[0].tolist()}

6) Extras to consider (for traceability & portability)
 Auto-export per trial: add export.onnx.enabled=true only for the best N trials (e.g., top 3 mAP).
 Determinism: set torch/cudnn deterministic flags if you care about exact reproducibility.
 Budget gating: reject configs that violate FLOPs/params ceilings (from math ledger).
 Model cards: attach the math ledger + ONNX metadata (opset, dynamic axes, providers) to the artifact.
 Simple plugin system: if you want to extend beyond fvcore/THOP, define METRIC_BACKENDS = {"fvcore": flops_fvcore, "thop": flops_thop, "none": lambda m,x: -1} so adding a new backend is 1 line.

Got it  lets wrap everything as an OS-level service so end-users dont have to think about Ray, Tune, ONNX, FLOP counters, or math ledgers. Theyll talk to a single API/RPC/SDK that works identically on a laptop, on a LAN, or across VPCs.
Below is a concrete blueprint you can implement now:

1) OS-Layer Service Blueprint
Process model
 A single daemon (container or systemd service) exposing:
 gRPC (primary, versioned) + HTTP/JSON via grpc-gateway.
 Unix domain socket locally (/var/run/atlas.sock) and mTLS TCP for remote.
 Pluggable backends (Ray, ONNX Runtime, fvcore/THOP) selected by host-injected config.
 Runs Tune jobs & trainers locally or submits to a Ray cluster transparently.
Deploy modes
 Local (single machine): systemd service (atlasd.service) + Unix socket; GPU/Tensor cores detected.
 Edge/volunteer: same container, joins central Ray head via Ray Client/Jobs API.
 Kubernetes: Operator/Deployment; per-node DaemonSet optional for data proximity.
Artifacts & config
 Artifacts in ~/.zoo_slate/ locally or S3/MinIO remotely (configurable).
 Config via YAML/env; all knobs injectable by host (no hard-coded choices).

2) API Surface (gRPC first; HTTP mirrored)
2.1 Protobuf (core services)
syntax = "proto3";
package atlas.v1;
option go_package = "atlas/v1;atlas";

message IRSpec { string yaml = 1; } // full IR as YAML
message TuneGrid { string json = 1; } // Tune param space (JSON)
message DatasetSpec { string uri = 1; map<string,string> opts = 2; }
message OnnxExportSpec {
 bool enabled = 1; string path = 2; uint32 opset = 3;
 map<string,Axis> dynamic_axes = 4; bool simplify = 5; bool runtime_check = 6;
 repeated string providers = 7; message Axis { map<int32,string> dims = 1; }
}
message LedgerSpec { string flops_backend = 1; bool log_activations = 2; } // fvcore|thop|none
message PrecisionSpec { string weights = 1; string activations = 2; string norm = 3; }
message QuantSpec { uint32 base_bits = 1; uint32 adapters_bits = 2; }

message SubmitTuneRequest {
 IRSpec ir = 1;
 TuneGrid grid = 2;
 DatasetSpec train = 3;
 DatasetSpec val = 4;
 OnnxExportSpec onnx = 5;
 LedgerSpec ledger = 6;
 PrecisionSpec precision = 7;
 QuantSpec quant = 8;
 uint32 num_samples = 9;
 string metric = 10;
 string mode = 11; // "max" | "min"
}
message JobId { string id = 1; }
message Status { string state = 1; map<string,string> info = 2; }
message Artifact {
 string id = 1; string uri = 2; string task = 3;
 string family = 4; string dataset = 5; map<string,double> metrics = 6;
 string onnx_uri = 7; string ledger_uri = 8;
}
message ListArtifactsRequest { map<string,string> filters = 1; }
message Ledger { string json = 1; } // math/dim ledger per run

service OrchestratorService {
 rpc SubmitTuneStudy(SubmitTuneRequest) returns (JobId);
 rpc SubmitTrainJob(SubmitTuneRequest) returns (JobId); // grid can be empty -> single config
 rpc CancelJob(JobId) returns (Status);
 rpc GetJobStatus(JobId) returns (Status);
}

service RegistryService {
 rpc ListArtifacts(ListArtifactsRequest) returns (stream Artifact);
 rpc GetLedger(JobId) returns (Ledger);
 rpc PromoteArtifact(JobId) returns (Artifact);
}

service InferenceService {
 // For framework-native inference
 rpc Run(stream bytes) returns (stream bytes);
}
The same endpoints are available via HTTP/JSON using grpc-gateway (OpenAPI generated).
2.2 Example HTTP (grpc-gateway)
POST /v1/tune { ir.yaml: "...", grid.json: "...", train.uri: "s3://...", ... }
GET /v1/jobs/{id}/status
GET /v1/artifacts?task=det&family=retina
GET /v1/jobs/{id}/ledger

3) Client SDK Shape (stable across environments)
 Python (primary), Go, TypeScript via generated stubs.
 Every SDK takes the same SubmitTuneRequest/SubmitTrainJob struct and marshals it to gRPC/HTTP automatically.
 All host decisions (FLOPs backend, ONNX export, dynamic axes, precision policy, quant bits) are in config delivered with the request or set as daemon defaults.
Python SDK example
from atlas_sdk import Atlas

atlas = Atlas(endpoint="unix:///var/run/atlas.sock") # or "https://atlas.company:8443"
req = {
 "ir": {"yaml": open("configs/retina.yaml").read()},
 "grid": {"json": open("grids/retina.json").read()},
 "train": {"uri": "s3://bucket/coco/train.parquet"},
 "val": {"uri": "s3://bucket/coco/val.parquet"},
 "onnx": {"enabled": True, "path": "s3://artifacts/retina.onnx", "opset": 17,
 "dynamic_axes": {"input": {"0":"batch","2":"H","3":"W"}},
 "simplify": True, "runtime_check": True, "providers": ["CUDAExecutionProvider"]},
 "ledger": {"flops_backend": "fvcore"},
 "precision": {"weights":"bf16","activations":"bf16","norm":"fp32"},
 "quant": {"base_bits":16,"adapters_bits":16},
 "num_samples": 32, "metric": "mAP50", "mode": "max"
}
job = atlas.orch.submit_tune(req)
print(atlas.orch.status(job["id"]))
for art in atlas.registry.list_artifacts({"task":"det","family":"retina"}):
 print(art)

4) Network Boundaries (local  external)
 Local: default endpoint unix:///var/run/atlas.sock; mTLS disabled; file permissions enforce local access.
 Remote: https://atlas.example.com:8443 with mTLS (client cert), OAuth2/JWT for human clients; RBACper project/workspace.
 Zero-trust: all internal calls to Ray head/worker use mTLS; KMS/secret manager for credentials.

5) ONNX-portable Inference
Two options:
0. Serve framework-native (Ray Serve): rich Python graphs, A/B & shadow, but framework-dependent.
0. Serve ONNX: vendor-neutral; ONNX Runtime across CPU/CUDA; easy to edge-deploy.
We recommend both:
 training/tuning with full framework graphs;
 on success, auto-export to ONNX and register the artifact; the same SDK can request either native or onnx inference endpoints.

6) Observability, Traceability, and Policy
 OpenTelemetry tracing for every job; add trial IDs & ledger URIs as spans.
 Math Ledger (the JSON we defined) saved per trial & attached to artifacts; contains shapes, FLOPs, params, precision & quantization state.
 Model cards include ledger, dataset lineage, license, and ONNX metadata (opset/providers/dynamic axes).
 Budget gating: enforce FLOPs/params ceilings at the daemon; reject configs violating policy before scheduling.

OS Level Services and Service Spec
(Network Atlas  Wiring Optimization & Cell Playbook, Part 2)
This spec defines an OS-level service (daemon atlasd) that exposes a stable API/RPC/SDK for training, tuning, exporting, and serving models with full traceability (math/dim ledger), portability (ONNX), and policy control(throttling & scheduling). It runs identically on a laptop, on edge nodes, or in Kubernetes.

1) Service Overview
 Process: single daemon (systemd service or container) exposing gRPC + HTTP/JSON via grpc-gateway; local Unix socket /var/run/atlas.sock; remote mTLS TCP.
 Backends: Ray Data/Train/Tune/Serve; ONNX Runtime for portable inference; FLOPs backends (fvcore/THOP) are config-injected, not hard-coded.
 Artifacts: model/onnx/ledger stored in filesystem or object store (S3/MinIO/GCS); registry tracks metadata, metrics, lineage.

2) API Surface (gRPC; HTTP mirrored)
OrchestratorService: SubmitTuneStudy, SubmitTrainJob, CancelJob, GetJobStatusRegistryService: ListArtifacts, GetLedger, PromoteArtifactInferenceService: Run (native) and RunOnnx (portable)
Policy APIs:PolicyService: SetThrottlePolicy, SetSchedulingPolicy, GetPolicy, ListPolicies
OpenAPI generated for REST; versioned as atlas.v1.

3) Configuration Schema (host-injected)
metrics:
 flops_backend: fvcore # fvcore | thop | none
 log_activations: false

export:
 onnx:
 enabled: true
 path: artifacts/model.onnx
 opset: 17
 dynamic_axes:
 input: {0: batch, 2: H, 3: W}
 output: {0: batch}
 simplify: true
 runtime_check: true
 providers: [CPUExecutionProvider] # or CUDAExecutionProvider

precision: {weights: bf16, activations: bf16, norm: fp32}
quant: {base_bits: 4, adapters_bits: 16}

# NEW: Throttling & Scheduling
throttle:
 endpoints:
 tune.submit: {rps: 2, burst: 4, concurrent: 2}
 train.submit: {rps: 4, burst: 8, concurrent: 4}
 resources:
 cpu_cores: {max_total: 32, max_per_job: 8}
 gpu_devices: {max_total: 4, max_per_job: 1}
 mem_bytes: {max_total: 128Gi, max_per_job: 16Gi}
 io_mb_s: {max_total: 500, max_per_job: 150}
 net_mb_s: {max_total: 1000, max_per_job: 300}
 hyperparams:
 lr: {rate_limit: per_minute: 100} # prevent floods of tiny LR scans
 batch_size: {min: 4, max: 1024, step: 4}
 img.size: {allowed: [512,640,800,1024]}

scheduler:
 job:
 max_concurrent: 4
 queue_capacity: 64
 priority_classes:
 - {name: emergency, weight: 100}
 - {name: high, weight: 10}
 - {name: normal, weight: 1}
 fairness: drf # weighted fair share | DRF | strict-priority
 trial:
 algorithm: asha # asha | pbt | hyperband | random
 asha: {grace_epochs: 2, reduction_factor: 3}
 budget:
 walltime_minutes: 240
 gpu_hours: 20
 flops_max: 2.0e15
 params_max: 1.0e8
 resource_placement:
 pack: true # prefer bin-packing vs spread
 affinities: {require_gpu: true}
 topology:
 numa_aware: true
 node_labels: {accelerator: nvidia}

4) Throttling (Admission & Flow Control)
 Endpoint rate-limits: token-bucket (RPS/burst) per endpoint+tenant; reject or queue beyond limits.
 Concurrency gates: cap in-flight jobs/trials; backpressure to clients with 429 and Retry-After.
 Resource quotas: enforce max CPU/GPU/mem/IO/network per job and global totals; map to cgroups (local) or K8s requests/limits (cluster).
 Hyperparam guards: validate grid values (min/max/allowed sets, step) and change rates (e.g., lr sweep density), refuse pathological sweeps.
 Fairness: WFQ/DRF across tenants; priority classes with preemption.
Admission Controller (pseudocode)
def admit(job):
 check_endpoint_rate(job.user, job.endpoint)
 check_concurrency(job.user)
 enforce_quotas(job.resources)
 validate_grid(job.grid, policy.hyperparams)
 enqueue(job, priority=job.priority)

5) Scheduling (Job / Trial / Resource)
 Job-level: priority queue; DRF (Dominant Resource Fairness) sharing across CPU/GPU/mem.
 Trial-level: ASHA/Hyperband early-stop poor configs; optional PBT (mutate/promote).
 Resource-level: Ray PlacementGroups with accelerators; GPU MIG partitions if available; NUMA pinning; disk/IO shaping.
 Budgets: per-study budget (wall-clock, GPU-hours, FLOPs, params); terminate/exclude out-of-budget trials.
 Preemption & checkpointing: periodic AIR checkpoints; resume on available nodes.
ASHA + DRF schedule loop
while queue:
 job = pick_by_priority_drf(queue)
 if resources_available(job):
 start_trials(job, algo=ASHA(job.conf))
 else:
 evict_or_wait()

6) Inference Scheduling & Throttling
 Dynamic batching: per-endpoint batch window (e.g., 5ms) + max batch size.
 Micro-batching: split large batches across streams; control GPU streams.
 Rate-limit: tenant/endpoint RPS; queue depth; SLO timeouts.
 ONNX providers: schedule across CPU/CUDA/MIG; fallbacks if EP unsupported.
Serve config example
serve:
 deployments:
 detector:
 num_replicas: 4
 autoscaling: {min: 2, max: 16, target_qps: 50}
 batching: {max_batch_size: 16, batch_wait_ms: 5}
 rate_limit: {rps: 200, burst: 400}

7) Protobuf Extensions (Policy APIs)
message ThrottlePolicy { /* mirrors throttle.* schema */ }
message SchedulingPolicy { /* mirrors scheduler.* schema */ }
service PolicyService {
 rpc SetThrottlePolicy(ThrottlePolicy) returns (Status);
 rpc SetSchedulingPolicy(SchedulingPolicy) returns (Status);
 rpc GetPolicy(google.protobuf.Empty) returns (PolicyBundle);
}

8) Implementation Notes (Ray & OS Integration)
 Ray: PlacementGroups for GPU affinity; RuntimeEnv per job; Ray Serve autoscaling for inference.
 OS: cgroups v2 (CPU/mem/IO); cpuset & numactl for locality; NVIDIA MIG profiles; ulimits (nofile).
 Security: mTLS for all remote APIs; per-tenant auth (JWT/OIDC); request/response audit logs.
 Reproducibility: record seeds, env, package hashes; attach to math ledger.

9) Example Policy Bundle (YAML)
policy:
 throttle:
 endpoints:

 Math Ledger Collector (Tune callback)
Use this to capture [MATH_LEDGER] {...} lines printed by train loops and persist them per trial:
File: atlas/logs/ledger_callback.py
import os, json, re
from ray.tune import Callback

LEDGER_RE = re.compile(r"^\[MATH_LEDGER\]\s+(\{.*\})$")

class MathLedgerCallback(Callback):
 def __init__(self, out_root: str, job_id: str):
 self.root = os.path.join(out_root, job_id)
 os.makedirs(self.root, exist_ok=True)
 self.ledgers = []
 def on_trial_log(self, iteration, trials, trial, output):
 m = LEDGER_RE.search(output)
 if m:
 try:
 self.ledgers.append(json.loads(m.group(1)))
 except Exception:
 pass
 def on_trial_complete(self, iteration, trials, trial, **info):
 path = os.path.join(self.root, f"{trial.trial_id}_ledger.json")
 with open(path, "w") as f:
 json.dump(self.ledgers[-1] if self.ledgers else {}, f, indent=2)
Wire it in ray_runner.launch_trials:
from atlas.logs.ledger_callback import MathLedgerCallback
cb = MathLedgerCallback(out_root=os.environ.get("ATLAS_ARTIFACTS","artifacts"), job_id=job_id)

tuner = tune.Tuner(
 trainer,
 param_space=...,
 tune_config=...,
 run_config=ray.train.RunConfig(name=job_id, placement_group=pg)
)
result = tuner.fit(callbacks=[cb])

1) Cosine-sim ONNX round-trip helper (in slate/utils/ledger.py)
Use this after export to ensure the ONNX graph is numerically sane vs. the PyTorch graph.
# slate/utils/ledger.py (append)
import numpy as np

def cosine_sim(a: np.ndarray, b: np.ndarray, eps: float = 1e-9) -> float:
 a = a.reshape(-1).astype(np.float64); b = b.reshape(-1).astype(np.float64)
 denom = (np.linalg.norm(a) * np.linalg.norm(b)) + eps
 return float(np.dot(a, b) / denom)

def onnx_roundtrip_check(model, sample, onnx_path: str, threshold: float = 0.995, provider="CPUExecutionProvider"):
 """Compare PyTorch vs ONNX runtime outputs (cosine similarity)."""
 import onnxruntime as ort
 model.eval()
 with torch.no_grad():
 torch_out = model(**sample) if isinstance(sample, dict) else model(sample)
 # convert to numpy
 if isinstance(torch_out, (tuple, list)):
 torch_out_np = [t.detach().cpu().numpy() if hasattr(t, "detach") else np.array(t) for t in torch_out]
 torch_out_np = np.concatenate([t.reshape(-1) for t in torch_out_np], axis=0)
 else:
 torch_out_np = torch_out.detach().cpu().numpy() if hasattr(torch_out, "detach") else np.array(torch_out)

 sess = ort.InferenceSession(onnx_path, providers=[provider])
 if isinstance(sample, dict):
 feed = {inp.name: sample.get(inp.name, None) for inp in sess.get_inputs()}
 # fall back to the first key if names don't match
 for k, v in list(feed.items()):
 if v is None:
 # choose a likely key (first in dict)
 v = sample[list(sample.keys())[0]]
 feed[k] = v
 feed = {k: (v.detach().cpu().numpy() if isinstance(v, torch.Tensor) else np.asarray(v)) for k, v in feed.items()}
 else:
 name = sess.get_inputs()[0].name
 feed = {name: sample.detach().cpu().numpy() if isinstance(sample, torch.Tensor) else np.asarray(sample)}
 ort_out = sess.run(None, feed)
 if isinstance(ort_out, (tuple, list)):
 ort_out_np = np.concatenate([o.reshape(-1) for o in ort_out], axis=0)
 else:
 ort_out_np = ort_out.reshape(-1)
 sim = cosine_sim(torch_out_np, ort_out_np)
 return sim >= threshold, sim
How to enable (per job config):
export:
 onnx:
 enabled: true
 path: "artifacts/model.onnx"
 opset: 17
 dynamic_axes: { input: {0: batch}, output: {0: batch} }
 simplify: true
 runtime_check: true
 cos_sim_threshold: 0.995
After export_to_onnx(), call:
ok, sim = onnx_roundtrip_check(model, sample, cfg["export"]["onnx"]["path"],
 threshold=cfg["export"]["onnx"].get("cos_sim_threshold", 0.995))
print("[ONNX_CHECK]", {"ok": ok, "cos_sim": sim})
This will appear in the model card.

What else are the major things we still need?
Heres a concise, prioritized list:
A) Hardening & correctness
 Strict shape contracts: enforce spec.in/out on every module; block build if shapes dont match.
 Determinism & seeds: unify seeding across torch/cuda/python/numpy; log seed in math ledger.
 Error budget & retries: propagate failure reasons in TRIT; auto-retry transient Ray/IO errors with backoff.
B) Scheduling & quotas
 DRF fairness: implement real Dominant Resource Fairness across CPU/GPU/mem for multi-tenant queues.
 FLOPs/params ceilings: reject configs before scheduling if they exceed budgets (compute from IR).
 Data locality: prefer nodes with cached datasets (Ray locality hints) to reduce IO.
C) Security & tenancy
 mTLS & RBAC: per-tenant certs; project-level access controls; rate-limits per tenant.
 Audit logging: admission/schedule/serve events with tenant IDs; immutable logs for policy compliance.
D) Reproducibility
 Manifest hashing: record git SHA, pip freeze, CUDA/cuDNN versions; tie to model card.
 Dataset versioning: compute dataset fingerprint/hash; store with model card.
E) Serve & monitoring
 ONNX Runtime EPs: support selection of CUDA/MIG/CPU providers per deployment; expose via config.
 A/B + shadow: already specd; add latency/throughput/err metrics; automated rollback if candidate underperforms.
 Observability: Prometheus metrics for queue depth, schedule latency, GPU utilization, success/failure rates.
F) Developer ergonomics
 atlasctl CLI: wrap the SDK to submit/list/status/promote/serve; support YAML submit files and --set k=voverrides.
 Starter templates: cookiecutter project with all studies, daemon, configs, and CI pipeline.
G) Performance
 Dataset caching: Ray Data persistent blocks, S3 + local SSD; reduce transform overhead.
 Kernel fusion: optional Triton/Inductor for hotspots; falls back on portable ops.
 Quantization: export QAT/PTQ ONNX models when target runtime benefits (edge devices).

2) DRF deallocation on job completion
Subtract tenants provisional shares when trials finish
Update atlas/scheduler/drf.py:
class DRFBroker:
 ...
 def release(self, tenant: str, req: dict):
 a = self.alloc[tenant]
 a["CPU"] = max(0.0, a["CPU"] - req.get("resources",{}).get("CPU",0))
 a["GPU"] = max(0.0, a["GPU"] - req.get("resources",{}).get("GPU",0))
 a["MEM"] = max(0.0, a["MEM"] - req.get("resources",{}).get("MEM",0))
In atlasd loop (or in RayRunner.launch_trials finally:):

3) Placement constraints (MIG / node labels)
Add custom resources to bundles & optional node affinity
Update atlas/ray_runner.py placement groups:
def _mk_pg(self, res: dict):
 mig = res.get("node_resources", {}) # e.g., {"accelerator:nvidia/a100-40gb-mig": 1}
 # head bundle
 head = {"CPU": res.get("head_cpus", 1)}
 head.update({k: v for k, v in mig.items()}) # head constraints if desired
 # worker bundles
 bundles = [head] + [
 {"CPU": res.get("cpus_per_worker", 2), "GPU": res.get("gpus_per_worker", 0), **mig}
 for _ in range(res.get("num_workers", 1))
 ]
 return placement_group(bundles=bundles, strategy=res.get("strategy","PACK").lower())
Optional Node affinity for Ray tasks (if you want to pin to a labeled node):

Ray uses custom resources for node selection; if your cluster labels nodes with custom resources (e.g., {"node_label:edge":1}), include those keys in node_resources.

def export_trace(ir_yaml: str, outdir: str, job_id: str, trial_id: str):
 import yaml, json, os
 from graphviz import Digraph
 ir = yaml.safe_load(ir_yaml)
 # Build a simple node/edge list from IR (pseudo)
 nodes = ir.get("model",{})
 edges = [] # from your IR builder, capture connections
 trace = {"nodes": nodes, "edges": edges}
 os.makedirs(outdir, exist_ok=True)
 with open(os.path.join(outdir, f"{trial_id}_trace.json"), "w") as f:
 json.dump(trace, f, indent=2)
 # dot
 dot = Digraph(comment=f"Atlas Trace {trial_id}")
 for n in nodes: dot.node(n)
 for (u,v) in edges: dot.edge(u,v)
 dot.render(os.path.join(outdir, f"{trial_id}_trace"), format="svg", cleanup=True)
Call after best result chosen:

Brilliant  Ive added the requested pieces and kept everything small and drop-in:

 Node affinity scheduling_strategy (labeled nodes / MIG)
If you choose to run the trainer as a Ray task (instead of using RunConfigs placement group), you can pin it to a specific labeled node or MIG slice via NodeAffinitySchedulingStrategy:
# atlas/ray_runner.py (alternative submit path as a Ray task)
from ray.util.scheduling_strategies import NodeAffinitySchedulingStrategy

@ray.remote
def run_trainer_on_node(trainer, param_space, tune_cfg):
 from ray import tune
 tuner = tune.Tuner(trainer, param_space=param_space, tune_config=tune_cfg)
 return tuner.fit()

def launch_trials(self, job_id: str, req: Dict):
 # Create trainer as before
 trainer = self._build_trainer(req, pg=None)

 # Node affinity (optional); choose by label or resource
 node_id = req.get("resources", {}).get("node_id") # e.g., "node:abc123"
 strategy = None
 if node_id:
 strategy = NodeAffinitySchedulingStrategy(node_id=node_id, soft=False)

 metric, mode = req.get("metric","val_acc"), req.get("mode","max")
 asha = ASHAScheduler(grace_period=2, reduction_factor=3, metric=metric, mode=mode)
 tune_cfg = tune.TuneConfig(metric=metric, mode=mode, num_samples=req.get("num_samples",16), scheduler=asha)
 param_space = {"train_loop_config": json.loads(req["grid"]["json"]) if req.get("grid") else {}}

 # Submit as a Ray task pinned to node
 result = ray.get(run_trainer_on_node.options(scheduling_strategy=strategy).remote(trainer, param_space, tune_cfg))
 self._collect_ledgers(job_id, result)
 return result
Host config examples:
resources:
 node_id: "3b1a2c5d..." # specific Ray node id
 node_resources:
 accelerator:nvidia/a100-40gb-mig: 1 # MIG constraint via custom resource
You can combine PlacementGroups (for per-worker bundles) with node affinity if you need both guaranteed bundles and hard pinning to a labeled node.

 CLI commands (atlasctl) to exercise features
Package layout
atlasctl/
 __init__.py
 cli.py
 pyproject.toml
atlasctl/cli.py
import json, click
from atlas_sdk import Atlas # REST client from the SDK we added

@click.group()
@click.option("--endpoint", default="http://127.0.0.1:8080", help="Atlas service endpoint")
@click.pass_context
def cli(ctx, endpoint):
 ctx.ensure_object(dict); ctx.obj["atlas"] = Atlas(endpoint)

@cli.command("promote")
@click.argument("job_id")
@click.pass_context
def promote(ctx, job_id):
 # calls REST GET /v1/artifacts/{id}/promote (we exposed POST)
 r = ctx.obj["atlas"].registry.list_artifacts({"job_id": job_id})
 if not r:
 click.echo("No artifacts found for job."); return
 # naive: just print first; in real impl call the promote endpoint
 click.echo(json.dumps(r[0], indent=2))

@cli.command("policy:set")
@click.option("--throttle", type=click.Path(), help="YAML throttle policy file")
@click.option("--scheduler", type=click.Path(), help="YAML scheduler policy file")
@click.pass_context
def policy_set(ctx, throttle, scheduler):
 import requests, yaml
 ep = ctx.obj["atlas"].ep
 if throttle:
 data = {"yaml": open(throttle).read()}
 print(requests.post(f"{ep}/v1/policy/throttle", json=data).json())
 if scheduler:
 data = {"yaml": open(scheduler).read()}
 print(requests.post(f"{ep}/v1/policy/scheduler", json=data).json())

@cli.command("serve")
@click.option("--model-card", type=click.Path(), required=True, help="Path to model_card.json")
@click.pass_context
def serve(ctx, model_card):
 card = json.load(open(model_card))
 onnx_path = card["onnx"]["path"]
 # Launch a small ONNX Runtime server (example)
 click.echo(f"Serving ONNX model at: {onnx_path}")
 click.echo("(In production, call the daemons Serve API to deploy Ray Serve / ORT.)")

if __name__ == "__main__":
 cli(obj={})

 Tiny unit tests (DRF broker & ONNX checker)
tests/test_drf.py
from atlas.scheduler.drf import DRFBroker, TenantWeights

def test_drf_pick_and_release():
 broker = DRFBroker()
 broker.set_weights("tenantA", TenantWeights(cpu=1,gpu=1,mem=1))
 broker.set_weights("tenantB", TenantWeights(cpu=1,gpu=1,mem=1))
 queue = [
 ("tenantA", "job1", {"resources":{"CPU":2,"GPU":1,"MEM":8}}),
 ("tenantB", "job2", {"resources":{"CPU":2,"GPU":1,"MEM":8}})
 ]
 total = {"CPU":16,"GPU":4,"MEM":64}
 picked = broker.pick_next(queue, total)
 assert picked[0] in ("tenantA","tenantB")
 # release should not go negative
 broker.release(picked[0], picked[2]["resources"])
 assert broker.alloc[picked[0]]["CPU"] >= 0
tests/test_onnx_check.py
import torch, numpy as np, tempfile, os
from slate.utils.ledger import onnx_roundtrip_check, export_to_onnx

class Tiny(torch.nn.Module):
 def __init__(self): super().__init__(); self.lin = torch.nn.Linear(8,4)
 def forward(self, x): return self.lin(x)

def test_onnx_roundtrip_basic():
 m = Tiny().eval()
 x = torch.randn(2,8)
 tmp = tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix=".onnx", delete=False); tmp.close()
 export_to_onnx(m, x, {"enabled": True, "path": tmp.name, "opset": 17,
 "dynamic_axes": {"input": {0:"batch"}, "output":{0:"batch"}}, "runtime_check": False})
 ok, sim = onnx_roundtrip_check(m, x, tmp.name, threshold=0.90)
 os.unlink(tmp.name)
 assert ok and sim > 0.90
These unit tests check the DRF brokers pick/release behavior and ONNX round-trip sanity.
