OS Level Services and Service Spec
This document continues Part 1. It expands the Atlas into OS-layer service design, config injection, ONNX portability, and API/RPC abstractions. The goal is to embed the full traceable calculus and tuning ecosystem as an invisible OS service, accessible consistently via RPC/API/SDK.

ServeService gRPC Surface  Deploy/Scale/List/Router with A/B Router Control
Proto additions (atlas.proto)
message DeployRequest { string job_id = 1; string onnx_path = 2; string provider = 3; int32 replicas = 4; }
message DeployReply { string name = 1; string status = 2; }
message ScaleRequest { string name = 1; int32 replicas = 2; }
message ScaleReply { string status = 1; }
message ListDeploymentsReply { repeated string names = 1; }
message RouterConfig { map<string,int32> weights = 1; bool shadow = 2; }
message RouterStatus { map<string,int32> weights = 1; bool shadow = 2; }

service ServeService {
 rpc Deploy(DeployRequest) returns (DeployReply);
 rpc Scale(ScaleRequest) returns (ScaleReply);
 rpc ListDeployments(google.protobuf.Empty) returns (ListDeploymentsReply);
 rpc ConfigureRouter(RouterConfig) returns (Status);
 rpc GetRouter(google.protobuf.Empty) returns (RouterStatus);
}
Server scaffold with ABRouter (atlas/rpc/server.py)
from ray import serve
import onnxruntime as ort, numpy as np, random, asyncio, json

@serve.deployment(name="ABRouter", route_prefix="/router")
class ABRouter:
 def __init__(self):
 self.weights = {"current": 100}
 self.shadow = False
 async def __call__(self, request):
 body = await request.json()
 target = random.choices(list(self.weights.keys()), weights=self.weights.values())[0]
 handle = serve.get_deployment(target).get_handle()
 result = await handle.remote(body)
 if self.shadow:
 for k in self.weights.keys():
 if k != target:
 asyncio.create_task(serve.get_deployment(k).get_handle().remote(body))
 return await result
 def update(self, weights, shadow):
 self.weights = dict(weights)
 self.shadow = bool(shadow)
 return {"weights": self.weights, "shadow": self.shadow}
 def status(self):
 return {"weights": self.weights, "shadow": self.shadow}

class ServeServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.ServeServiceServicer):
 def __init__(self):
 if not ray.is_initialized(): ray.init(); serve.start(detached=True)
 if "ABRouter" not in serve.list_deployments():
 ABRouter.deploy()
 def Deploy(self, req, ctx):
 name = f"onnx_{req.job_id}"
 @serve.deployment(name=name, num_replicas=req.replicas or 1)
 class ORTWrap:
 def __init__(self):
 self.sess = ort.InferenceSession(req.onnx_path, providers=[req.provider or "CPUExecutionProvider"])
 self.input_name = self.sess.get_inputs()[0].name
 async def __call__(self, request):
 payload = await request.json()
 arr = np.array(payload["input"],dtype=np.float32)
 out = self.sess.run(None,{self.input_name:arr})
 return {"output": out[0].tolist()}
 ORTWrap.deploy()
 return atlas_pb2.DeployReply(name=name, status="DEPLOYED")
 def Scale(self, req, ctx):
 serve.get_deployment(req.name).options(num_replicas=req.replicas).deploy()
 return atlas_pb2.ScaleReply(status=f"scaled to {req.replicas}")
 def ListDeployments(self, req, ctx):
 names = list(serve.list_deployments().keys())
 return atlas_pb2.ListDeploymentsReply(names=names)
 def ConfigureRouter(self, req, ctx):
 router = serve.get_deployment("ABRouter").get_handle()
 import ray
 res = ray.get(router.update.remote(dict(req.weights), bool(req.shadow)))
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="ROUTER_CONFIGURED", info={"weights":str(res["weights"]),"shadow":str(res["shadow"])})
 def GetRouter(self, req, ctx):
 router = serve.get_deployment("ABRouter").get_handle()
 import ray
 s = ray.get(router.status.remote())
 return atlas_pb2.RouterStatus(weights=s.get("weights", {}), shadow=bool(s.get("shadow", False)))
Wire into gRPC server
atlas_pb2_grpc.add_ServeServiceServicer_to_server(ServeServicer(), server)

Router Autoscaler Actor (dynamic weights)
File: atlas/serve/autoscaler.py
import ray, time
from ray import serve

@ray.remote
class RouterAutoscaler:
 def __init__(self, slo_latency_ms: float = 100.0):
 self.slo = slo_latency_ms
 self.history = {"latency": []}
 def observe(self, deployment: str, latency_ms: float):
 self.history.setdefault(deployment, []).append(latency_ms)
 def rebalance(self):
 # naive: if one deployment exceeds SLO, shift weight to the other
 router = serve.get_deployment("ABRouter").get_handle()
 import ray
 st = ray.get(router.status.remote())
 weights = st["weights"]
 latencies = {k: (sum(self.history.get(k,[]))/len(self.history.get(k,[])) if self.history.get(k) else 0)
 for k in weights}
 if not latencies: return st
 worst = max(latencies.items(), key=lambda kv: kv[1])
 best = min(latencies.items(), key=lambda kv: kv[1])
 if worst[1] > self.slo:
 weights[best[0]] += 10; weights[worst[0]] = max(0, weights[worst[0]]-10)
 router.update.remote(weights, st["shadow"])
 return weights

Sticky Cookie Routing (per-user stickiness)
Router modification (atlas/serve/router.py)
async def __call__(self, request):
 body = await request.json()
 # sticky cookie header
 cookie = request.headers.get("x-user-id")
 if cookie:
 idx = hash(cookie) % sum(self.weights.values())
 csum = 0; chosen = list(self.weights.keys())[0]
 for k, w in self.weights.items():
 csum += w
 if idx < csum:
 chosen = k; break
 else:
 chosen = random.choices(list(self.weights.keys()), weights=self.weights.values())[0]
 handle = serve.get_deployment(chosen).get_handle()
 result = await handle.remote(body)
 if self.shadow:
 for k in self.weights.keys():
 if k != chosen:
 asyncio.create_task(serve.get_deployment(k).get_handle().remote(body))
 return await result

atlasctl Serve Commands  Manage via gRPC/REST
@cli.group("serve")
def serve_group(): pass

@serve_group.command("deploy")
@click.argument("job_id")
@click.argument("onnx_path")
@click.option("--replicas", default=1)
def deploy(job_id, onnx_path, replicas):
 r = requests.post(f"{API}/v1/serve/deploy", json={"job_id":job_id,"onnx_path":onnx_path,"replicas":replicas})
 click.echo(r.json())

@serve_group.command("scale")
@click.argument("name")
@click.argument("replicas", type=int)
def scale(name, replicas):
 r = requests.post(f"{API}/v1/serve/scale", json={"name":name,"replicas":replicas})
 click.echo(r.json())

@serve_group.command("list")
def list_cmd():
 r = requests.get(f"{API}/v1/serve/list")
 click.echo(r.json())

@serve_group.command("router")
@click.option("--weights", type=str)
@click.option("--shadow", is_flag=True)
def router(weights, shadow):
 w = json.loads(weights)
 r = requests.post(f"{API}/v1/serve/router", json={"weights":w,"shadow":shadow})
 click.echo(r.json())

@serve_group.command("router:status")
def router_status():
 r = requests.get(f"{API}/v1/serve/router")
 click.echo(r.json())

Router Integration Tests
File: tests/test_router.py
import pytest, ray
from ray import serve

@pytest.fixture(scope="module", autouse=True)
def ray_serve_cluster():
 if not ray.is_initialized(): ray.init(num_cpus=2)
 try: serve.start(detached=True)
 except RuntimeError: pass
 yield
 ray.shutdown()

def deploy_dummy(name, bias):
 @serve.deployment(name=name, num_replicas=1)
 class Dummy:
 def __call__(self, request): return {"out": bias}
 Dummy.deploy()

def test_router_switching(ray_serve_cluster):
 from atlas.serve.router import ABRouter
 deploy_dummy("A", 111); deploy_dummy("B", 222)
 try: ABRouter.deploy()
 except RuntimeError: pass
 router = serve.get_deployment("ABRouter").get_handle()
 # route all to A
 ABRouter().update({"A":100}, False)
 out = ray.get(router.remote({"input":[0]}))
 assert out["out"] == 111
 # route all to B
 ABRouter().update({"B":100}, False)
 out = ray.get(router.remote({"input":[0]}))
 assert out["out"] == 222

This update introduces Router autoscaler actor for SLO-based weight rebalancing and sticky cookie routing for per-user A/B stickiness. Backward compatibility is maintained: existing Deploy, Scale, List, and ConfigureRouter calls remain unchanged; new methods extend functionality. Tests verify router switching behavior.

Router Autoscaler Unit Test
File: tests/test_autoscaler.py
import pytest
import ray
from atlas.serve.autoscaler import RouterAutoscaler

class DummyRouter:
 def __init__(self):
 self.last_update = None
 def status(self):
 return {"weights": {"A": 50, "B": 50}, "lat_ewma": {"A": 200.0, "B": 50.0}, "shadow": False}
 def update(self, new_w, shadow):
 self.last_update = (new_w, shadow)
 return {"weights": new_w, "shadow": shadow}

@pytest.mark.asyncio
async def test_autoscaler_rebalances(monkeypatch):
 # Patch serve.get_deployment to return dummy router handle
 dummy = DummyRouter()
 class Handle:
 async def status(self): return dummy.status()
 async def update(self, w, s): return dummy.update(w, s)
 monkeypatch.setattr("atlas.serve.autoscaler.serve.get_deployment", lambda name: dummy)
 # Directly instantiate RouterAutoscaler and call step()
 autoscaler = RouterAutoscaler("ABRouter", target_p95_ms=100.0)
 # monkeypatch ray.get to call function directly
 monkeypatch.setattr("ray.get", lambda fut: fut)
 res = autoscaler.step()
 assert "weights" in res
 assert res["weights"]["B"] > res["weights"]["A"]

ServeService AutoScaleRouter RPC
Proto additions (atlas.proto)
message AutoScaleConfig { string router = 1; double target_p95_ms = 2; int32 min_weight = 3; }

service ServeService {
 rpc AutoScaleRouter(AutoScaleConfig) returns (Status);
}
Server handler (atlas/rpc/server.py)
class ServeServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.ServeServiceServicer):
 ...
 def AutoScaleRouter(self, req, ctx):
 from atlas.serve.autoscaler import RouterAutoscaler
 try:
 actor = RouterAutoscaler.options(name=f"autoscaler_{req.router}").remote(req.router, req.target_p95_ms, req.min_weight)
 actor.run.remote() # start loop asynchronously
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ENABLED", info={"router": req.router, "target": str(req.target_p95_ms)})
 except Exception as e:
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ERROR", info={"error": str(e)})
This adds a new gRPC method to configure and launch the autoscaler at runtime, letting you set SLO targets and min weights declaratively.

Router Autoscaler Unit Test
File: tests/test_autoscaler.py
import pytest
import ray

# Patch the autoscaler module to avoid real Ray/Serve calls
import atlas.serve.autoscaler as autoscaler_mod

class DummyRouterHandle:
 def __init__(self):
 self.updated = None
 def status(self):
 return {"weights": {"A": 50, "B": 50}, "lat_ewma": {"A": 200.0, "B": 50.0}, "shadow": False}
 def update(self, w, s):
 self.updated = (dict(w), bool(s))
 return {"weights": dict(w), "shadow": bool(s)}

class DummyDeployment:
 def __init__(self, h): self._h = h
 def get_handle(self): return self._h

def test_autoscaler_step_rebalances(monkeypatch):
 dummy = DummyRouterHandle()
 # monkeypatch serve.get_deployment and ray.get
 monkeypatch.setattr(autoscaler_mod.serve, "get_deployment", lambda name: DummyDeployment(dummy))
 monkeypatch.setattr(autoscaler_mod.ray, "get", lambda fut: fut)
 # Create autoscaler instance manually
 RA = autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler.__new__(autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler)
 RA.router_name = "ABRouter"; RA.target_p95 = 100.0; RA.min_w = 5; RA.period_s = 5.0
 # Run one step
 out = autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler.step(RA)
 assert "weights" in out
 # Verify that backend B (faster) gained weight
 assert dummy.updated is not None
 new_weights, shadow = dummy.updated
 assert new_weights["B"] > new_weights["A"]
 assert new_weights["A"] >= RA.min_w

ServeService AutoScaleRouter RPC (configure autoscaler at runtime)
Proto additions (atlas.proto)
message AutoScaleConfig { string router = 1; double target_p95_ms = 2; int32 min_weight = 3; double period_s = 4; bool enable = 5; }

service ServeService {
 // ... existing RPCs ...
 rpc AutoScaleRouter(AutoScaleConfig) returns (Status);
}
Server handler (atlas/rpc/server.py)
class ServeServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.ServeServiceServicer):
 ...
 def AutoScaleRouter(self, req, ctx):
 from atlas.serve.autoscaler import RouterAutoscaler
 try:
 if req.enable:
 actor = RouterAutoscaler.options(name=f"autoscaler_{req.router}").remote(req.router, req.target_p95_ms or 80.0, req.min_weight or 5, req.period_s or 5.0)
 actor.run.remote() # start loop
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ENABLED", info={"router": req.router, "target": str(req.target_p95_ms)})
 else:
 # disable autoscaler (best effort)
 aid = f"autoscaler_{req.router}"
 if ray.util.placement_group(aid):
 ray.kill(ray.get_actor(aid))
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_DISABLED", info={"router": req.router})
 except Exception as e:
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ERROR", info={"error": str(e)})

This test and RPC ensure the autoscaler can be validated in isolation and configured dynamically at runtime via gRPC, while keeping full backward compatibility.

Router Autoscaler Unit Test (latency-driven reweight)
File: tests/test_autoscaler.py
import pytest
import atlas.serve.autoscaler as autoscaler_mod

class DummyRouterHandle:
 def __init__(self):
 self.updated = None
 def status(self):
 # A is much slower (200ms) vs B (50ms)
 return {"weights": {"A": 50, "B": 50}, "lat_ewma": {"A": 200.0, "B": 50.0}, "shadow": False}
 def update(self, w, s):
 self.updated = (dict(w), bool(s))
 return {"weights": dict(w), "shadow": bool(s)}

class DummyDeployment:
 def __init__(self, h): self._h = h
 def get_handle(self): return self._h

def test_autoscaler_step_rebalances(monkeypatch):
 dummy = DummyRouterHandle()
 # monkeypatch serve.get_deployment and ray.get
 monkeypatch.setattr(autoscaler_mod.serve, "get_deployment", lambda name: DummyDeployment(dummy))
 monkeypatch.setattr(autoscaler_mod.ray, "get", lambda fut: fut)
 # Create autoscaler manually
 RA = autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler.__new__(autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler)
 RA.router_name = "ABRouter"; RA.target_p95 = 100.0; RA.min_w = 5; RA.period_s = 1.0
 out = autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler.step(RA)
 assert "weights" in out
 # Verify backend B (fast) gained weight, A did not drop below min_w
 assert dummy.updated is not None
 new_weights, shadow = dummy.updated
 assert new_weights["B"] > new_weights["A"]
 assert new_weights["A"] >= RA.min_w

ServeService AutoScaleRouter RPC (runtime config)
Proto additions (atlas.proto)
message AutoScaleConfig {
 string router = 1; // default "ABRouter"
 double target_p95_ms = 2;
 int32 min_weight = 3;
 double period_s = 4;
 bool enable = 5;
}

service ServeService {
 // ... existing RPCs ...
 rpc AutoScaleRouter(AutoScaleConfig) returns (Status);
}
Server handler (atlas/rpc/server.py)
class ServeServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.ServeServiceServicer):
 ...
 def AutoScaleRouter(self, req, ctx):
 from atlas.serve.autoscaler import RouterAutoscaler
 import ray
 try:
 name = f"autoscaler_{req.router or 'ABRouter'}"
 if req.enable:
 actor = RouterAutoscaler.options(name=name).remote(
 router_name=req.router or "ABRouter",
 target_p95_ms=req.target_p95_ms or 80.0,
 min_weight=req.min_weight or 5,
 period_s=req.period_s or 5.0
 )
 actor.run.remote()
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ENABLED", info={"router": req.router or "ABRouter"})
 else:
 try:
 a = ray.get_actor(name)
 ray.get(a.stop.remote()); ray.kill(a)
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_DISABLED", info={"router": req.router or "ABRouter"})
 except Exception:
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_DISABLED", info={"router": req.router or "ABRouter"})
 except Exception as e:
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ERROR", info={"error": str(e)})

OS Level Services and Service Spec
This document continues Part 1. It expands the Atlas into OS-layer service design, config injection, ONNX portability, and API/RPC abstractions. The goal is to embed the full traceable calculus and tuning ecosystem as an invisible OS service, accessible consistently via RPC/API/SDK.

ServeService gRPC Surface  Deploy/Scale/List/Router with A/B Router Control
Proto additions (atlas.proto)
message DeployRequest { string job_id = 1; string onnx_path = 2; string provider = 3; int32 replicas = 4; }
message DeployReply { string name = 1; string status = 2; }
message ScaleRequest { string name = 1; int32 replicas = 2; }
message ScaleReply { string status = 1; }
message ListDeploymentsReply { repeated string names = 1; }
message RouterConfig { map<string,int32> weights = 1; bool shadow = 2; }
message RouterStatus { map<string,int32> weights = 1; bool shadow = 2; }

service ServeService {
 rpc Deploy(DeployRequest) returns (DeployReply);
 rpc Scale(ScaleRequest) returns (ScaleReply);
 rpc ListDeployments(google.protobuf.Empty) returns (ListDeploymentsReply);
 rpc ConfigureRouter(RouterConfig) returns (Status);
 rpc GetRouter(google.protobuf.Empty) returns (RouterStatus);
}
Server scaffold with ABRouter (atlas/rpc/server.py)
from ray import serve
import onnxruntime as ort, numpy as np, random, asyncio, json

@serve.deployment(name="ABRouter", route_prefix="/router")
class ABRouter:
 def __init__(self):
 self.weights = {"current": 100}
 self.shadow = False
 async def __call__(self, request):
 body = await request.json()
 target = random.choices(list(self.weights.keys()), weights=self.weights.values())[0]
 handle = serve.get_deployment(target).get_handle()
 result = await handle.remote(body)
 if self.shadow:
 for k in self.weights.keys():
 if k != target:
 asyncio.create_task(serve.get_deployment(k).get_handle().remote(body))
 return await result
 def update(self, weights, shadow):
 self.weights = dict(weights)
 self.shadow = bool(shadow)
 return {"weights": self.weights, "shadow": self.shadow}
 def status(self):
 return {"weights": self.weights, "shadow": self.shadow}

class ServeServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.ServeServiceServicer):
 def __init__(self):
 if not ray.is_initialized(): ray.init(); serve.start(detached=True)
 if "ABRouter" not in serve.list_deployments():
 ABRouter.deploy()
 def Deploy(self, req, ctx):
 name = f"onnx_{req.job_id}"
 @serve.deployment(name=name, num_replicas=req.replicas or 1)
 class ORTWrap:
 def __init__(self):
 self.sess = ort.InferenceSession(req.onnx_path, providers=[req.provider or "CPUExecutionProvider"])
 self.input_name = self.sess.get_inputs()[0].name
 async def __call__(self, request):
 payload = await request.json()
 arr = np.array(payload["input"],dtype=np.float32)
 out = self.sess.run(None,{self.input_name:arr})
 return {"output": out[0].tolist()}
 ORTWrap.deploy()
 return atlas_pb2.DeployReply(name=name, status="DEPLOYED")
 def Scale(self, req, ctx):
 serve.get_deployment(req.name).options(num_replicas=req.replicas).deploy()
 return atlas_pb2.ScaleReply(status=f"scaled to {req.replicas}")
 def ListDeployments(self, req, ctx):
 names = list(serve.list_deployments().keys())
 return atlas_pb2.ListDeploymentsReply(names=names)
 def ConfigureRouter(self, req, ctx):
 router = serve.get_deployment("ABRouter").get_handle()
 import ray
 res = ray.get(router.update.remote(dict(req.weights), bool(req.shadow)))
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="ROUTER_CONFIGURED", info={"weights":str(res["weights"]),"shadow":str(res["shadow"])})
 def GetRouter(self, req, ctx):
 router = serve.get_deployment("ABRouter").get_handle()
 import ray
 s = ray.get(router.status.remote())
 return atlas_pb2.RouterStatus(weights=s.get("weights", {}), shadow=bool(s.get("shadow", False)))
Wire into gRPC server
atlas_pb2_grpc.add_ServeServiceServicer_to_server(ServeServicer(), server)

Router Autoscaler Actor (dynamic weights)
File: atlas/serve/autoscaler.py
import ray, time
from ray import serve

@ray.remote
class RouterAutoscaler:
 def __init__(self, slo_latency_ms: float = 100.0):
 self.slo = slo_latency_ms
 self.history = {"latency": []}
 def observe(self, deployment: str, latency_ms: float):
 self.history.setdefault(deployment, []).append(latency_ms)
 def rebalance(self):
 # naive: if one deployment exceeds SLO, shift weight to the other
 router = serve.get_deployment("ABRouter").get_handle()
 import ray
 st = ray.get(router.status.remote())
 weights = st["weights"]
 latencies = {k: (sum(self.history.get(k,[]))/len(self.history.get(k,[])) if self.history.get(k) else 0)
 for k in weights}
 if not latencies: return st
 worst = max(latencies.items(), key=lambda kv: kv[1])
 best = min(latencies.items(), key=lambda kv: kv[1])
 if worst[1] > self.slo:
 weights[best[0]] += 10; weights[worst[0]] = max(0, weights[worst[0]]-10)
 router.update.remote(weights, st["shadow"])
 return weights

Sticky Cookie Routing (per-user stickiness)
Router modification (atlas/serve/router.py)
async def __call__(self, request):
 body = await request.json()
 # sticky cookie header
 cookie = request.headers.get("x-user-id")
 if cookie:
 idx = hash(cookie) % sum(self.weights.values())
 csum = 0; chosen = list(self.weights.keys())[0]
 for k, w in self.weights.items():
 csum += w
 if idx < csum:
 chosen = k; break
 else:
 chosen = random.choices(list(self.weights.keys()), weights=self.weights.values())[0]
 handle = serve.get_deployment(chosen).get_handle()
 result = await handle.remote(body)
 if self.shadow:
 for k in self.weights.keys():
 if k != chosen:
 asyncio.create_task(serve.get_deployment(k).get_handle().remote(body))
 return await result

atlasctl Serve Commands  Manage via gRPC/REST
@cli.group("serve")
def serve_group(): pass

@serve_group.command("deploy")
@click.argument("job_id")
@click.argument("onnx_path")
@click.option("--replicas", default=1)
def deploy(job_id, onnx_path, replicas):
 r = requests.post(f"{API}/v1/serve/deploy", json={"job_id":job_id,"onnx_path":onnx_path,"replicas":replicas})
 click.echo(r.json())

@serve_group.command("scale")
@click.argument("name")
@click.argument("replicas", type=int)
def scale(name, replicas):
 r = requests.post(f"{API}/v1/serve/scale", json={"name":name,"replicas":replicas})
 click.echo(r.json())

@serve_group.command("list")
def list_cmd():
 r = requests.get(f"{API}/v1/serve/list")
 click.echo(r.json())

@serve_group.command("router")
@click.option("--weights", type=str)
@click.option("--shadow", is_flag=True)
def router(weights, shadow):
 w = json.loads(weights)
 r = requests.post(f"{API}/v1/serve/router", json={"weights":w,"shadow":shadow})
 click.echo(r.json())

@serve_group.command("router:status")
def router_status():
 r = requests.get(f"{API}/v1/serve/router")
 click.echo(r.json())

Router Integration Tests
File: tests/test_router.py
import pytest, ray
from ray import serve

@pytest.fixture(scope="module", autouse=True)
def ray_serve_cluster():
 if not ray.is_initialized(): ray.init(num_cpus=2)
 try: serve.start(detached=True)
 except RuntimeError: pass
 yield
 ray.shutdown()

def deploy_dummy(name, bias):
 @serve.deployment(name=name, num_replicas=1)
 class Dummy:
 def __call__(self, request): return {"out": bias}
 Dummy.deploy()

def test_router_switching(ray_serve_cluster):
 from atlas.serve.router import ABRouter
 deploy_dummy("A", 111); deploy_dummy("B", 222)
 try: ABRouter.deploy()
 except RuntimeError: pass
 router = serve.get_deployment("ABRouter").get_handle()
 # route all to A
 ABRouter().update({"A":100}, False)
 out = ray.get(router.remote({"input":[0]}))
 assert out["out"] == 111
 # route all to B
 ABRouter().update({"B":100}, False)
 out = ray.get(router.remote({"input":[0]}))
 assert out["out"] == 222

This update introduces Router autoscaler actor for SLO-based weight rebalancing and sticky cookie routing for per-user A/B stickiness. Backward compatibility is maintained: existing Deploy, Scale, List, and ConfigureRouter calls remain unchanged; new methods extend functionality. Tests verify router switching behavior.

Router Autoscaler Unit Test
File: tests/test_autoscaler.py
import pytest
import ray
from atlas.serve.autoscaler import RouterAutoscaler

class DummyRouter:
 def __init__(self):
 self.last_update = None
 def status(self):
 return {"weights": {"A": 50, "B": 50}, "lat_ewma": {"A": 200.0, "B": 50.0}, "shadow": False}
 def update(self, new_w, shadow):
 self.last_update = (new_w, shadow)
 return {"weights": new_w, "shadow": shadow}

@pytest.mark.asyncio
async def test_autoscaler_rebalances(monkeypatch):
 # Patch serve.get_deployment to return dummy router handle
 dummy = DummyRouter()
 class Handle:
 async def status(self): return dummy.status()
 async def update(self, w, s): return dummy.update(w, s)
 monkeypatch.setattr("atlas.serve.autoscaler.serve.get_deployment", lambda name: dummy)
 # Directly instantiate RouterAutoscaler and call step()
 autoscaler = RouterAutoscaler("ABRouter", target_p95_ms=100.0)
 # monkeypatch ray.get to call function directly
 monkeypatch.setattr("ray.get", lambda fut: fut)
 res = autoscaler.step()
 assert "weights" in res
 assert res["weights"]["B"] > res["weights"]["A"]

ServeService AutoScaleRouter RPC
Proto additions (atlas.proto)
message AutoScaleConfig { string router = 1; double target_p95_ms = 2; int32 min_weight = 3; }

service ServeService {
 rpc AutoScaleRouter(AutoScaleConfig) returns (Status);
}
Server handler (atlas/rpc/server.py)
class ServeServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.ServeServiceServicer):
 ...
 def AutoScaleRouter(self, req, ctx):
 from atlas.serve.autoscaler import RouterAutoscaler
 try:
 actor = RouterAutoscaler.options(name=f"autoscaler_{req.router}").remote(req.router, req.target_p95_ms, req.min_weight)
 actor.run.remote() # start loop asynchronously
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ENABLED", info={"router": req.router, "target": str(req.target_p95_ms)})
 except Exception as e:
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ERROR", info={"error": str(e)})
This adds a new gRPC method to configure and launch the autoscaler at runtime, letting you set SLO targets and min weights declaratively.

Router Autoscaler Unit Test
File: tests/test_autoscaler.py
import pytest
import ray

# Patch the autoscaler module to avoid real Ray/Serve calls
import atlas.serve.autoscaler as autoscaler_mod

class DummyRouterHandle:
 def __init__(self):
 self.updated = None
 def status(self):
 return {"weights": {"A": 50, "B": 50}, "lat_ewma": {"A": 200.0, "B": 50.0}, "shadow": False}
 def update(self, w, s):
 self.updated = (dict(w), bool(s))
 return {"weights": dict(w), "shadow": bool(s)}

class DummyDeployment:
 def __init__(self, h): self._h = h
 def get_handle(self): return self._h

def test_autoscaler_step_rebalances(monkeypatch):
 dummy = DummyRouterHandle()
 # monkeypatch serve.get_deployment and ray.get
 monkeypatch.setattr(autoscaler_mod.serve, "get_deployment", lambda name: DummyDeployment(dummy))
 monkeypatch.setattr(autoscaler_mod.ray, "get", lambda fut: fut)
 # Create autoscaler instance manually
 RA = autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler.__new__(autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler)
 RA.router_name = "ABRouter"; RA.target_p95 = 100.0; RA.min_w = 5; RA.period_s = 5.0
 # Run one step
 out = autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler.step(RA)
 assert "weights" in out
 # Verify that backend B (faster) gained weight
 assert dummy.updated is not None
 new_weights, shadow = dummy.updated
 assert new_weights["B"] > new_weights["A"]
 assert new_weights["A"] >= RA.min_w

ServeService AutoScaleRouter RPC (configure autoscaler at runtime)
Proto additions (atlas.proto)
message AutoScaleConfig { string router = 1; double target_p95_ms = 2; int32 min_weight = 3; double period_s = 4; bool enable = 5; }

service ServeService {
 // ... existing RPCs ...
 rpc AutoScaleRouter(AutoScaleConfig) returns (Status);
}
Server handler (atlas/rpc/server.py)
class ServeServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.ServeServiceServicer):
 ...
 def AutoScaleRouter(self, req, ctx):
 from atlas.serve.autoscaler import RouterAutoscaler
 try:
 if req.enable:
 actor = RouterAutoscaler.options(name=f"autoscaler_{req.router}").remote(req.router, req.target_p95_ms or 80.0, req.min_weight or 5, req.period_s or 5.0)
 actor.run.remote() # start loop
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ENABLED", info={"router": req.router, "target": str(req.target_p95_ms)})
 else:
 # disable autoscaler (best effort)
 aid = f"autoscaler_{req.router}"
 if ray.util.placement_group(aid):
 ray.kill(ray.get_actor(aid))
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_DISABLED", info={"router": req.router})
 except Exception as e:
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ERROR", info={"error": str(e)})

This test and RPC ensure the autoscaler can be validated in isolation and configured dynamically at runtime via gRPC, while keeping full backward compatibility.

ServeService AutoScaleRouter RPC (runtime config)

message AutoScaleConfig {
 string router = 1; // default "ABRouter"
 double target_p95_ms = 2;
 int32 min_weight = 3;
 double period_s = 4;
 bool enable = 5;
}

service ServeService {
 // ... existing RPCs ...
 rpc AutoScaleRouter(AutoScaleConfig) returns (Status);
}
Server handler (atlas/rpc/server.py)
class ServeServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.ServeServiceServicer):
 ...
 def AutoScaleRouter(self, req, ctx):
 from atlas.serve.autoscaler import RouterAutoscaler
 import ray
 try:
 name = f"autoscaler_{req.router or 'ABRouter'}"
 if req.enable:
 actor = RouterAutoscaler.options(name=name).remote(
 router_name=req.router or "ABRouter",
 target_p95_ms=req.target_p95_ms or 80.0,
 min_weight=req.min_weight or 5,
 period_s=req.period_s or 5.0
 )
 actor.run.remote()
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ENABLED", info={"router": req.router or "ABRouter"})
 else:
 try:
 a = ray.get_actor(name)
 ray.get(a.stop.remote()); ray.kill(a)
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_DISABLED", info={"router": req.router or "ABRouter"})
 except Exception:
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_DISABLED", info={"router": req.router or "ABRouter"})
 except Exception as e:
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ERROR", info={"error": str(e)})

Awesome  here are the final scaffolds and hooks you asked for, delivered in small, drop-in blocks so you can wire them immediately. Ive also described where each piece should live and how it interacts with the daemon, DRF, traces, and CI.

1) gRPC server scaffold (maps RPC  daemon methods, with tenant extraction)
File: atlas/rpc/server.py
import os, ssl, json, grpc, threading
from concurrent import futures
from typing import Dict, Any, Tuple, Optional

from gen.python.atlas.v1 import atlas_pb2, atlas_pb2_grpc # generated by buf/protoc
from google.protobuf import empty_pb2

# --- Tenant extraction (mTLS and/or JWT in metadata) ---
def extract_tenant_from_context(context: grpc.ServicerContext) -> str:
 # JWT in metadata?
 md = dict(context.invocation_metadata())
 if "authorization" in md:
 token = md["authorization"].split()[-1]
 try:
 import jwt # pyjwt
 payload = jwt.decode(token, options={"verify_signature": False})
 return payload.get("tenant", "default")
 except Exception:
 pass
 # mTLS: parse peer cert CN/OU from channel creds (implementation-specific)
 # grpc python doesn't expose peer cert directly; in production, run behind TLS terminator that sets x-tenant-id
 if "x-tenant-id" in md:
 return md["x-tenant-id"]
 return "default"

# --- Servicer implementations ---
class OrchestratorServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.OrchestratorServiceServicer):
 def __init__(self, daemon):
 self.daemon = daemon

 def SubmitTuneStudy(self, req: atlas_pb2.SubmitTuneRequest, ctx) -> atlas_pb2.SubmitTuneReply:
 tenant = extract_tenant_from_context(ctx)
 # convert proto to dict; attach tenant
 j = _submit_req_to_dict(req); j["tenant"] = tenant
 out = self.daemon.submit(j)
 # TRIT mapping
 trit = out.get("trit", {"code": 0, "reason":"", "meta":{}})
 job_id = trit.get("meta", {}).get("job_id", "")
 return atlas_pb2.SubmitTuneReply(
 trit=_trit_status(trit),
 job=atlas_pb2.JobId(id=job_id),
 )

 def SubmitTrainJob(self, req, ctx):
 return self.SubmitTuneStudy(req, ctx)

 def CancelJob(self, req: atlas_pb2.JobId, ctx):
 # basic cancel: mark state (implement cancellation in runner as needed)
 st = self.daemon.status.get(req.id, {"state": "UNKNOWN"})
 st["state"] = "CANCELLED"; self.daemon.status[req.id] = st
 return atlas_pb2.StatusReply(trit=_trit_status({"code":1,"reason":"cancelled","meta":{}}),
 status=_status_pb(st))

 def GetJobStatus(self, req: atlas_pb2.JobId, ctx):
 st = self.daemon.status.get(req.id, {"state": "UNKNOWN"})
 # reflect TRIT based on state
 code = 0 if st["state"] in ("QUEUED","RUNNING") else (1 if st["state"]=="SUCCEEDED" else -1)
 return atlas_pb2.StatusReply(trit=_trit_status({"code": code, "reason": st["state"], "meta":{}}),
 status=_status_pb(st))

class RegistryServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.RegistryServiceServicer):
 def __init__(self, registry):
 self.registry = registry

 def ListArtifacts(self, req: atlas_pb2.ListArtifactsRequest, ctx):
 # very simple: stream filesystem entries under root
 for jid in os.listdir(self.registry.root):
 card = os.path.join(self.registry.root, jid, "model_card.json")
 if os.path.exists(card):
 meta = json.load(open(card))
 yield atlas_pb2.Artifact(
 id=jid, uri=f"{self.registry.root}/{jid}",
 task=meta["model"].get("task",""),
 family=meta["model"].get("family",""),
 dataset=meta["data"].get("train_uri",""),
 metrics=meta.get("metrics",{}),
 onnx_uri=meta.get("onnx",{}).get("path",""),
 ledger_uri=f"{self.registry.root}/{jid}/ledger.json",
 created_at=meta["model"].get("created_at",""),
 )

 def GetLedger(self, req: atlas_pb2.JobId, ctx):
 path = os.path.join(self.registry.root, req.id, "ledger.json")
 j = json.load(open(path)) if os.path.exists(path) else {}
 return atlas_pb2.Ledger(json=json.dumps(j))

 def PromoteArtifact(self, req: atlas_pb2.JobId, ctx):
 # promote the latest result for job_id (if not already)
 # we assume daemon stored the latest best result metrics inside status[job_id]
 st = ctx._state.daemon.status.get(req.id, {}) # hack: pass daemon via context or global
 metrics = st.get("info", {}).get("card", {}).get("metrics", {})
 card = ctx._state.daemon.registry.promote(req.id, 
 {"train":{"uri":""},"val":{"uri":""}}, 
 {"metrics": metrics})
 return atlas_pb2.Artifact(
 id=req.id, uri=f"{self.registry.root}/{req.id}",
 task=card["model"]["task"], family=card["model"]["family"],
 dataset=card["data"]["train_uri"],
 metrics=card["metrics"], onnx_uri=card["onnx"]["path"],
 ledger_uri=f"{self.registry.root}/{req.id}/ledger.json",
 created_at=card["model"]["created_at"],
 )

# --- helpers ---
def _trit_status(trit: Dict[str,Any]) -> atlas_pb2.TritStatus:
 # proto enum: 0 FALSE, 1 MID, 2 TRUE (mapping from -1,0,1)
 code_map = {-1: atlas_pb2.TRIT_FALSE, 0: atlas_pb2.TRIT_MID, 1: atlas_pb2.TRIT_TRUE}
 return atlas_pb2.TritStatus(code=code_map.get(trit.get("code",0), atlas_pb2.TRIT_MID),
 reason=trit.get("reason",""), meta=trit.get("meta",{}))

def _submit_req_to_dict(req: atlas_pb2.SubmitTuneRequest) -> Dict[str,Any]:
 return {
 "ir": {"yaml": req.ir.yaml},
 "grid": {"json": req.grid.json} if req.HasField("grid") else {},
 "train": {"uri": req.train.uri, "opts": dict(req.train.opts)},
 "val": {"uri": req.val.uri, "opts": dict(req.val.opts)} if req.HasField("val") else {},
 "export": {"onnx": {
 "enabled": req.onnx.enabled, "path": req.onnx.path, "opset": req.onnx.opset,
 "providers": list(req.onnx.providers)
 }},
 "ledger": {"flops_backend": req.ledger.flops_backend, "log_activations": req.ledger.log_activations},
 "precision": {"weights": req.precision.weights, "activations": req.precision.activations, "norm": req.precision.norm},
 "quant": {"base_bits": req.quant.base_bits, "adapters_bits": req.quant.adapters_bits},
 "num_samples": req.num_samples, "metric": req.metric, "mode": req.mode, "priority": req.priority,
 }

def _status_pb(st: Dict[str,Any]) -> atlas_pb2.Status:
 info = st.get("info", {})
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state=st.get("state","UNKNOWN"), info={k:str(v) for k,v in info.items()})

def start_grpc_server(daemon, host="[::]", port=50051, tls: Optional[Dict[str,str]] = None):
 server = grpc.server(futures.ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=32))
 orch = OrchestratorServicer(daemon)
 reg = RegistryServicer(daemon.registry)
 atlas_pb2_grpc.add_OrchestratorServiceServicer_to_server(orch, server)
 atlas_pb2_grpc.add_RegistryServiceServicer_to_server(reg, server)
 # PolicyService can be added similarly
 addr = f"{host}:{port}"
 if tls:
 creds = grpc.ssl_server_credentials([(open(tls["key"],"rb").read(), open(tls["cert"],"rb").read())],
 open(tls["ca"],"rb").read(), require_client_auth=True)
 server.add_secure_port(addr, creds)
 else:
 server.add_insecure_port(addr)
 server.start()
 print(f"[atlasd] gRPC listening on {addr} (tls={bool(tls)})")
 server.wait_for_termination()
Wire server in cmd/atlasd/main.py:
from atlas.rpc.server import start_grpc_server
...
threading.Thread(target=daemon.schedule_forever, daemon=True).start()
# TLS paths from env (optional), else insecure for dev
tls = None
if os.environ.get("ATLAS_TLS_CA"):
 tls = {"ca": os.environ["ATLAS_TLS_CA"], "cert": os.environ["ATLAS_TLS_CERT"], "key": os.environ["ATLAS_TLS_KEY"]}
start_grpc_server(daemon, host="0.0.0.0", port=int(os.getenv("ATLAS_GRPC_PORT","50051")), tls=tls)
Tenant-aware DRF: The server extracts the tenant via JWT/mTLS and injects req["tenant"] before calling daemon.submit(). The model card also records card["model"]["tenant"].

@cli.command("serve")
@click.option("--model-card", type=click.Path(exists=True), required=True)
@click.option("--provider", default="CPUExecutionProvider")
@click.option("--via-daemon", is_flag=True, default=False, help="Call daemon Serve API (if enabled)")

def serve_cmd(ctx, model_card, provider, via_daemon):

 # if your daemon exposes /v1/serve/onnx, call it here

1) gRPC/REST server scaffold (wire daemon  RPC)
File: atlas/rpc/server.py
import os, json, grpc
from concurrent import futures
from typing import Dict, Any, Optional

# generated by buf/protoc (make sure buf.generate has run)
from gen.python.atlas.v1 import atlas_pb2, atlas_pb2_grpc

# --- Helpers ---

def _code_enum(c: int):
 # map TRIT -1/0/1 -> enum TRIT_FALSE/MID/TRUE
 return { -1: atlas_pb2.TRIT_FALSE, 0: atlas_pb2.TRIT_MID, 1: atlas_pb2.TRIT_TRUE }.get(c, atlas_pb2.TRIT_MID)

def _trit_pb(code: int, reason: str = "", meta: Dict[str,str] = None):
 return atlas_pb2.TritStatus(code=_code_enum(code), reason=reason, meta=meta or {})

def _status_pb(st: Dict[str,Any]):
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state=st.get("state","UNKNOWN"), info={k:str(v) for k,v in st.get("info",{}).items()})

def _submit_req_to_dict(req: atlas_pb2.SubmitTuneRequest, tenant: str) -> Dict[str,Any]:
 # we carry tenant, ir, grid, datasets, precision/export/etc. down to the daemon
 od = {
 "tenant": tenant,
 "ir": { "yaml": req.ir.yaml },
 "grid": { "json": req.grid.json } if req.HasField("grid") else {},
 "train": { "uri": req.train.uri, "opts": dict(req.train.opts) },
 "val": { "uri": req.val.uri, "opts": dict(req.val.opts) } if req.HasField("val") else {},
 "export": { "onnx": {
 "enabled": req.onnx.enabled, "path": req.onnx.path, "opset": req.onnx.opset,
 "providers": list(req.onnx.providers)
 }},
 "ledger": { "flops_backend": req.ledger.flops_backend, "log_activations": req.ledger.log_activations },
 "precision": { "weights": req.precision.weights, "activations": req.precision.activations, "norm": req.precision.norm },
 "quant": { "base_bits": req.quant.base_bits, "adapters_bits": req.quant.adapters_bits },
 "num_samples": req.num_samples, "metric": req.metric, "mode": req.mode, "priority": req.priority,
 # optional resource hints
 "resources": json.loads(req.ir.yaml).get("resources", {}) if req.ir and req.ir.yaml else {}
 }
 return od

def _tenant_from_ctx(ctx: grpc.ServicerContext) -> str:
 # 1) x-tenant-id header (set by gateway or TLS terminator)
 md = dict(ctx.invocation_metadata())
 if "x-tenant-id" in md:
 return md["x-tenant-id"]
 # 2) JWT in "authorization": Bearer <token> (optional)
 if "authorization" in md:
 try:
 import jwt
 token = md["authorization"].split()[-1]
 payload = jwt.decode(token, options={"verify_signature": False})
 return payload.get("tenant", "default")
 except Exception:
 pass
 return "default"

# --- Servicers ---

class OrchestratorServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.OrchestratorServiceServicer):
 def __init__(self, daemon): self.daemon = daemon

 def SubmitTuneStudy(self, req: atlas_pb2.SubmitTuneRequest, ctx) -> atlas_pb2.SubmitTuneReply:
 tenant = _tenant_from_ctx(ctx)
 dreq = _submit_req_to_dict(req, tenant)
 out = self.daemon.submit(dreq) # {trit:{code,reason,meta:{job_id}}}
 tr = out.get("trit", {})
 return atlas_pb2.SubmitTuneReply(trit=_trit_pb(tr.get("code",0), tr.get("reason",""), tr.get("meta",{})),
 job=atlas_pb2.JobId(id=tr.get("meta",{}).get("job_id","")))

 def SubmitTrainJob(self, req, ctx): # reuse
 return self.SubmitTuneStudy(req, ctx)

 def CancelJob(self, req: atlas_pb2.JobId, ctx):
 st = self.daemon.status.get(req.id, {"state":"UNKNOWN"})
 st["state"] = "CANCELLED"; self.daemon.status[req.id] = st
 return atlas_pb2.StatusReply(trit=_trit_pb(1, "cancelled"), status=_status_pb(st))

 def GetJobStatus(self, req: atlas_pb2.JobId, ctx):
 st = self.daemon.status.get(req.id, {"state":"UNKNOWN","info":{}})
 code = 0 if st["state"] in ("QUEUED","RUNNING") else (1 if st["state"]=="SUCCEEDED" else -1)
 return atlas_pb2.StatusReply(trit=_trit_pb(code, st["state"]), status=_status_pb(st))

class RegistryServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.RegistryServiceServicer):
 def __init__(self, daemon): self.daemon = daemon

 def ListArtifacts(self, req: atlas_pb2.ListArtifactsRequest, ctx):
 root = self.daemon.registry.root
 for jid in os.listdir(root):
 card = os.path.join(root, jid, "model_card.json")
 if os.path.exists(card):
 meta = json.load(open(card))
 yield atlas_pb2.Artifact(
 id=jid, uri=f"{root}/{jid}", task=meta["model"].get("task",""),
 family=meta["model"].get("family",""),
 dataset=meta["data"].get("train_uri",""),
 metrics=meta.get("metrics",{}),
 onnx_uri=meta.get("onnx",{}).get("path",""),
 ledger_uri=f"{root}/{jid}/ledger.json",
 created_at=meta["model"].get("created_at",""),
 )

 def GetLedger(self, req: atlas_pb2.JobId, ctx):
 root = self.daemon.registry.root
 p = os.path.join(root, req.id, "ledger.json")
 j = json.load(open(p)) if os.path.exists(p) else {}
 return atlas_pb2.Ledger(json=json.dumps(j))

 def PromoteArtifact(self, req: atlas_pb2.JobId, ctx):
 st = self.daemon.status.get(req.id, {})
 best = {"metrics": st.get("info", {}).get("best_metrics", {})}
 card = self.daemon.registry.promote(req.id, st.get("info", {}).get("req", {}), best)
 return atlas_pb2.Artifact(
 id=req.id, uri=f"{self.daemon.registry.root}/{req.id}", task=card["model"]["task"],
 family=card["model"]["family"], dataset=card["data"]["train_uri"],
 metrics=card["metrics"], onnx_uri=card["onnx"]["path"],
 ledger_uri=os.path.join(self.daemon.registry.root, req.id, "ledger.json"),
 created_at=card["model"]["created_at"]
 )

def start_grpc_server(daemon, host="0.0.0.0", port=50051, tls: Optional[Dict[str,str]] = None):
 server = grpc.server(futures.ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=32))
 # stash daemon for registry usage if needed
 atlas_pb2_grpc.add_OrchestratorServiceServicer_to_server(OrchestratorServicer(daemon), server)
 atlas_pb2_grpc.add_RegistryServiceServicer_to_server(RegistryServicer(daemon), server)
 addr = f"{host}:{port}"
 if tls:
 creds = grpc.ssl_server_credentials([(open(tls["key"],"rb").read(),
 open(tls["cert"],"rb").read())],
 open(tls["ca"],"rb").read(),
 require_client_auth=True)
 server.add_secure_port(addr, creds)
 else:
 server.add_insecure_port(addr)
 server.start()
 print(f"[atlasd] gRPC up on {addr} (tls={'yes' if tls else 'no'})")
 server.wait_for_termination()

start_grpc_server(daemon, host="0.0.0.0", port=int(os.getenv("ATLAS_GRPC_PORT","50051")), tls=tls)

Absolutely  heres a clean, drop-in Router deployment for Ray Serve that supports A/B weighted routing with optional shadow mirroring, and a gRPC handler that updates it via your existing ServeService.ConfigureRoutercall.
Im keeping this in small chunks that slot right into your current Part 2 service spec.

1) Router deployment (weights + shadow mirroring)
File: atlas/serve/router.py
import asyncio, random, json
import numpy as np
from ray import serve

@serve.deployment(name="Router", route_prefix="/infer", num_replicas=1)
class Router:
 """
 Weighted A/B router with optional shadow mirroring.
 - weights: dict {deployment_name -> weight}
 - shadow: if True, the 'non-selected' deployment is also fired asynchronously (no effect on response)
 """
 def __init__(self, weights: dict, shadow: bool = False):
 self.weights = dict(weights) if weights else {}
 self.shadow = bool(shadow)
 # Build handles lazily; store names  handles (ServeHandle)
 self._handles = {name: serve.get_deployment(name).get_handle() for name in self.weights.keys()}

 async def __call__(self, request):
 payload = await request.json()
 # fast path: single backend
 names = list(self.weights.keys())
 if not names:
 return {"error": "router has no backends"}
 if len(names) == 1:
 name = names[0]
 handle = self._handles[name]
 return await handle.remote(payload)
 # weighted pick
 total = sum(max(0, int(w)) for w in self.weights.values()) or 1
 r = random.randint(1, total)
 csum = 0; chosen = names[0]
 for k, w in self.weights.items():
 csum += max(0, int(w))
 if r <= csum:
 chosen = k; break
 # primary route
 primary = self._handles[chosen]
 result = await primary.remote(payload)
 # shadow to the other(s)
 if self.shadow:
 for k, h in self._handles.items():
 if k != chosen:
 asyncio.create_task(h.remote(payload)) # fire-and-forget
 return result

 def update(self, weights: dict, shadow: bool = False):
 # Called via gRPC ConfigureRouter to mutate in place
 self.weights = dict(weights) if weights else {}
 self.shadow = bool(shadow)
 # Refresh handles for any new names
 for name in self.weights.keys():
 if name not in self._handles:
 self._handles[name] = serve.get_deployment(name).get_handle()
 # Remove stale handles
 for name in list(self._handles.keys()):
 if name not in self.weights:
 self._handles.pop(name, None)
 return {"ok": True, "weights": self.weights, "shadow": self.shadow}
Deploy the router once (e.g., in daemon init or after the first model Deploy):
from atlas.serve.router import Router
# Default no backends; ConfigureRouter will populate
try:
 Router.deploy(weights={}, shadow=False)
except RuntimeError:
 pass # already deployed

2) gRPC: ServeService.ConfigureRouter  mutate Router
Extend your ServeService handler to deploy the Router (if missing) and update its config.
File: atlas/rpc/server.py (ServeServicer additions)
from atlas.serve.router import Router
from ray import serve

class ServeServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.ServeServiceServicer):
 def __init__(self):
 if not ray.is_initialized(): ray.init()
 try:
 serve.start(detached=True)
 except RuntimeError:
 pass
 # Ensure Router is deployed (empty weights initially)
 try:
 Router.deploy(weights={}, shadow=False)
 except RuntimeError:
 pass

 def ConfigureRouter(self, req, ctx):
 # Ensure all named deployments exist
 missing = [k for k in req.weights.keys() if k not in serve.list_deployments()]
 if missing:
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="ROUTER_ERROR", info={"missing": ",".join(missing)})
 # Update Router
 router = serve.get_deployment("Router").get_handle()
 # Note: calling actor methods on a deployment handle is async in Serve; use ray.get
 import ray
 res = ray.get(router.update.remote(dict(req.weights), bool(req.shadow)))
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="ROUTER_CONFIGURED", info={"weights": json.dumps(res["weights"]), "shadow": str(res["shadow"])})
This uses a Serve deployment method call (update()) to mutate routing weights and shadow flag without redeploying the router container/process.

3) gRPC: ServeService.Deploy to register A/B backends
Make the Deploy handler populate obvious backend names (e.g., onnx_current, onnx_candidate), so you can call ConfigureRouter to set, say, {"onnx_current":95, "onnx_candidate":5}.
Deploy handler (already added earlier) deploys ORTWrap under a name derived from job_id or a user-provided name. If you prefer a convention:
 job_id for current: onnx_current
 job_id for candidate: onnx_candidate
Then set router weights:
{"weights": {"onnx_current": 95, "onnx_candidate": 5}, "shadow": true}

4) atlasctl serve router (weights/shadow)
Your atlasctl command already posts the JSON. Now, the daemon will mutate Routers config via the ServeService handler.
Example usage:
atlasctl serve deploy <job_current> /path/to/current.onnx --replicas 4
atlasctl serve deploy <job_candidate> /path/to/candidate.onnx --replicas 2
atlasctl serve router --weights '{"onnx_current":95,"onnx_candidate":5}' --shadow

5) Optional: autoscaling / SLO integration
If you want the router to bias traffic dynamically based on latency/SLO, you can:
 add a periodic task (Ray actor) to monitor Serve metrics and adjust weights via the same router.update(..)call,
 or expose an RPC ConfigureRouterAuto that sets target SLOs and lets the daemon reweight automatically.

Thats it  you now have:
 A Router deployment in Ray Serve that does weighted A/B and shadow mirroring.
 A gRPC ConfigureRouter handler that mutates Router at runtime.
 atlasctl serve router maps to the daemon and configures routing declaratively.

1) Router integration test (deploy A/B, flip weights, verify)
File: tests/test_router_ab.py
import asyncio, json, time
import numpy as np
import pytest
import ray
from ray import serve

# Dummy backends A & B that return their name
@serve.deployment(name="A")
class A:
 async def __call__(self, request):
 return {"backend": "A"}

@serve.deployment(name="B")
class B:
 async def __call__(self, request):
 return {"backend": "B"}

# Import your Router deployment
from atlas.serve.router import Router

@pytest.mark.asyncio
async def test_router_weights_flip(event_loop):
 if not ray.is_initialized():
 ray.init()
 try:
 serve.start(detached=True)
 except RuntimeError:
 pass

 # Deploy dummy backends and Router
 A.deploy(); B.deploy()
 try:
 Router.deploy(weights={"A": 100, "B": 0}, shadow=False)
 except RuntimeError:
 pass

 router = serve.get_deployment("Router").get_handle()

 # Helper to call router
 async def call_router(n=20):
 counts = {"A": 0, "B": 0}
 for _ in range(n):
 out = await router.remote({"input": [0.0]})
 result = await out
 counts[result["backend"]] += 1
 return counts

 # Phase 1: all traffic to A
 counts = await call_router(20)
 assert counts["A"] >= 18 and counts["B"] <= 2, f"unexpected counts phase1: {counts}"

 # Flip weights: all traffic to B
 # Call Router.update() via handle (your Router has update(weights, shadow))
 await router.update.remote({"B": 100}, False)

 # Give Router a moment to apply
 await asyncio.sleep(0.2)

 counts = await call_router(20)
 assert counts["B"] >= 18 and counts["A"] <= 2, f"unexpected counts phase2: {counts}"
This uses the Routers update(weights, shadow) method we added earlier and directly calls the Serve handle. If you want to test over HTTP, add route_prefix="/infer" to Router and send POSTs to http://127.0.0.1:8000/infer.

1) Router Autoscaler Actor (SLO-driven reweighting)
Design:
 The Router tracks per-backend EWMA latency and QPS.
 An autoscaler Ray actor reads these stats every N seconds and adjusts weights to keep p95 latency  SLOwhile honoring a min weight for each backend (e.g., 5% for canary).
 Changes are applied via the Routers .update(weights, shadow) method (no redeploy).
1.1 Router: record latency/QPS (lightweight)
File: atlas/serve/router.py (add timing + stats)
import time, collections, math
from starlette.responses import JSONResponse

@serve.deployment(name="Router", route_prefix="/infer", num_replicas=1)
class Router:
 def __init__(self, weights: dict, shadow: bool = False, sticky: bool = False):
 self.weights = dict(weights) if weights else {}
 self.shadow = bool(shadow)
 self.sticky = bool(sticky)
 self._handles = {n: serve.get_deployment(n).get_handle() for n in self.weights}
 # stats: ewma latency & qps per backend
 self.lat_ewma = collections.defaultdict(float)
 self.qps_ewma = collections.defaultdict(float)
 self.alpha = 0.2 # ewma smoothing
 self.last_tick = time.time()

 def status(self):
 return {"weights": self.weights, "shadow": self.shadow,
 "lat_ewma": dict(self.lat_ewma), "qps_ewma": dict(self.qps_ewma)}

 def _choose_weighted(self, user_key: str | None = None) -> str:
 names = list(self.weights.keys())
 if not names: return None
 if len(names) == 1: return names[0]
 if self.sticky and user_key:
 # simple consistent hash by user id / cookie; stable modulo sum(weights)
 total = max(1, sum(max(0,int(w)) for w in self.weights.values()))
 slot = (hash(user_key) % total) + 1
 csum = 0
 for k, w in self.weights.items():
 csum += max(0,int(w))
 if slot <= csum: return k
 return names[0]
 # non-sticky: weighted random
 import random
 total = max(1, sum(max(0,int(w)) for w in self.weights.values()))
 r = random.randint(1, total); csum = 0
 for k, w in self.weights.items():
 csum += max(0,int(w))
 if r <= csum: return k
 return names[0]

 async def __call__(self, request):
 body = await request.json()
 # sticky key from header or cookie
 user_key = request.headers.get("X-User-Id") or request.cookies.get("atlas_stick")
 chosen = self._choose_weighted(user_key)
 if not chosen: return JSONResponse({"error": "no backends configured"}, status_code=503)
 start = time.perf_counter()
 result = await self._handles[chosen].remote(body)
 dur_ms = (time.perf_counter() - start) * 1000.0
 # update ewma latency & qps
 self.lat_ewma[chosen] = (1-self.alpha)*self.lat_ewma[chosen] + self.alpha*dur_ms
 now = time.time(); dt = max(1e-3, now - self.last_tick)
 self.qps_ewma[chosen] = (1-self.alpha)*self.qps_ewma[chosen] + self.alpha*(1.0/dt)
 self.last_tick = now
 # shadow others
 if self.shadow:
 for k, h in self._handles.items():
 if k != chosen: serve.get_deployment(k).get_handle().remote(body)
 # set sticky cookie if missing
 if self.sticky and not request.cookies.get("atlas_stick"):
 resp = JSONResponse(result); resp.set_cookie("atlas_stick", user_key or f"u{hash(time.time())}")
 return resp
 return result

 def update(self, weights: dict, shadow: bool = False, sticky: bool | None = None):
 self.weights = dict(weights) if weights else {}
 self.shadow = bool(shadow)
 if sticky is not None: self.sticky = bool(sticky)
 for name in self.weights:
 if name not in self._handles:
 self._handles[name] = serve.get_deployment(name).get_handle()
 for name in list(self._handles.keys()):
 if name not in self.weights:
 self._handles.pop(name, None)
 return {"ok": True, "weights": self.weights, "shadow": self.shadow, "sticky": self.sticky}
1.2 Autoscaler actor
File: atlas/serve/autoscaler.py
import ray, time, math
from ray import serve

@ray.remote(num_cpus=0.1)
class RouterAutoscaler:
 def __init__(self, router_name: str, target_p95_ms: float = 80.0, min_weight: int = 5, period_s: float = 5.0):
 self.router_name = router_name
 self.target_p95 = float(target_p95_ms)
 self.min_w = int(min_weight)
 self.period_s = float(period_s)
 self.running = True

 def stop(self): self.running = False

 def step(self):
 rh = serve.get_deployment(self.router_name).get_handle()
 stats = ray.get(rh.status.remote()) # {"weights":{}, "lat_ewma":{}, "qps_ewma":{}}
 w = stats.get("weights", {})
 lat = stats.get("lat_ewma", {})
 if not w: return {"ok": False, "reason": "no backends"}
 # Compute adjustment: penalize backends whose latency > target
 new_w = {}
 total = 0
 for k, old in w.items():
 l = float(lat.get(k, self.target_p95))
 scale = max(0.5, min(1.5, self.target_p95 / max(1e-3, l))) # damped reaction
 cand = max(self.min_w, int(old * scale))
 new_w[k] = cand; total += cand
 # normalize to keep sum stable (optional)
 if total > 0:
 norm = sum(w.values()) / float(total)
 for k in new_w: new_w[k] = max(self.min_w, int(new_w[k] * norm))
 # apply if different
 if new_w != w:
 return ray.get(rh.update.remote(new_w, stats.get("shadow", False)))
 return {"ok": True, "weights": w}

 def run(self):
 while self.running:
 try: self.step()
 except Exception: pass
 time.sleep(self.period_s)
Start autoscaler (e.g., in daemon or ServeService init):
from atlas.serve.autoscaler import RouterAutoscaler
# Launch one autoscaler to manage "Router"
try:
 _ = RouterAutoscaler.options(name="router_autoscaler").remote("Router", target_p95_ms=80.0, min_weight=5, period_s=5.0)
 ray.get(_.run.remote())
except Exception:
 pass
This is conservative: it nudges weights toward backends meeting the SLO and away from those exceeding it, but never below a min weight (keeps canaries alive).

2) Sticky routing (cookie/header)
Already covered above: the Router now supports a sticky flag and hash-based selection using either:
 X-User-Id header, or
 atlas_stick cookie (set on the first request if missing).
You can enable it via Router.update(weights, shadow, sticky=True) or expose it in the ServeService RouterConfig.
ServeService.ConfigureRouter (allow sticky):
def ConfigureRouter(self, req, ctx):
 router = serve.get_deployment("Router").get_handle()
 import ray
 # If you extend proto RouterConfig to include `sticky` bool:
 res = ray.get(router.update.remote(dict(req.weights), bool(req.shadow), getattr(req, "sticky", False)))
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="ROUTER_CONFIGURED", info={"weights": json.dumps(res["weights"]),
 "shadow": str(res["shadow"]),
 "sticky": str(res.get("sticky", False))})
(If you dont want to change the proto, you can keep sticky as a server-side feature toggled in config.)

3) Backward-compatibility plan (archives & updates)
To keep everything compatible with prior archives and staged updates:
 Proto/API versioning: were on atlas.v1.
 Never remove/repurpose existing fields.
 New fields (e.g., sticky) should be optional with sane defaults.
 REST mappings via grpc-gateway should default to existing routes; new endpoints must not break old clients.
 IR/config migrations:
 Maintain a schema migration step: IR YAML  annotate defaults if fields missing (e.g., missing resources/export.onnx).
 Keep feature flags: FLOPs backend fallback (none) if not provided; ONNX export default enabled=false.
 Serve/Router:
 ConfigureRouter defaults to a single backend weight=100 if not set.
 Shadow and sticky default false. Old clients that dont set them still work.
 Policy YAML:
 auto_promotion.metric_threshold optional; if absent, no automatic promotion.
 Artifacts:
 Model card writer tolerates missing onnx_check.json and missing ledger; writes partial card gracefully.
 SDK clients:
 Continue to ship both REST and gRPC clients; REST keeps older users unblocked even without TLS client certs.

 A Router autoscaler actor that reweights backends by SLO (p95 latency),
 Sticky A/B routing for per-user consistency,
 A ServeService gRPC interface (Deploy/Scale/List/Router/Status) that can mutate Router live,
 A compatibility plan so older configs and archives still work without changes.

1) Tiny autoscaler unit test
Goal: mock the Routers status() and update(); verify that a single step() reweights toward the faster backend and never pushes a backend below min_weight.
File: tests/test_autoscaler.py
import types

# Patch points (we avoid real Ray/Serve to keep this fast)
class FakeRouterHandle:
 def __init__(self, status_payload):
 self._status_payload = status_payload
 self.last_update = None
 def status(self): # mimic Serve deployment method
 return self._status_payload
 def update(self, weights, shadow=False):
 self.last_update = (dict(weights), bool(shadow))
 return {"ok": True, "weights": dict(weights), "shadow": bool(shadow)}

class FakeDeployment:
 def __init__(self, handle): self._h = handle
 def get_handle(self): return self._h

def test_router_autoscaler_step_reweights():
 # Router has equal weights, but A is slower (120ms) than B (60ms)
 status_payload = {
 "weights": {"A": 50, "B": 50},
 "shadow": False,
 "lat_ewma": {"A": 120.0, "B": 60.0},
 "qps_ewma": {"A": 10.0, "B": 10.0},
 }
 fake_handle = FakeRouterHandle(status_payload)

 # Monkey-patch serve.get_deployment(...) and ray.get(...)
 import atlas.serve.autoscaler as autoscaler_mod
 import importlib
 importlib.reload(autoscaler_mod)

 def fake_get_deployment(name):
 assert name in ("Router", "ABRouter") # whichever name you used
 return FakeDeployment(fake_handle)

 def fake_ray_get(obj):
 # Our "remote" methods are plain calls
 if isinstance(obj, types.FunctionType):
 return obj()
 # If it's a bound method call surrogate with .__call__:
 if hasattr(obj, "__call__"):
 return obj()
 return obj

 # Patch modules
 autoscaler_mod.serve.get_deployment = fake_get_deployment # type: ignore
 autoscaler_mod.ray.get = fake_ray_get # type: ignore

 # Instantiate autoscaler and run one step
 RA = autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler.__new__(autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler) # bypass __init__
 RA.router_name = "Router"
 RA.target_p95 = 80.0 # want p95 <= 80ms
 RA.min_w = 5
 RA.period_s = 5.0

 out = autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler.step(RA)
 # Verify the Router.handle.update() was called with more weight to B, less to A
 assert fake_handle.last_update is not None, "update() not called"
 new_weights, new_shadow = fake_handle.last_update
 assert new_weights["B"] > status_payload["weights"]["B"], "B should gain weight"
 assert new_weights["A"] < status_payload["weights"]["A"], "A should lose weight"
 assert new_weights["A"] >= RA.min_w, "A should not be pushed below min_weight"
This test keeps everything in-process (no real Ray/Serve). It monkey-patches serve.get_deployment and ray.get to interact with a fake handle. Adjust "Router" vs "ABRouter" to your chosen deployment name.

2.2 Autoscaler actor: add a reconfigure() method
atlas/serve/autoscaler.py (append):
@ray.remote(num_cpus=0.1)
class RouterAutoscaler:
 def __init__(self, router_name: str = "Router", target_p95_ms: float = 80.0, min_weight: int = 5, period_s: float = 5.0):
 self.router_name = router_name
 self.target_p95 = float(target_p95_ms)
 self.min_w = int(min_weight)
 self.period_s = float(period_s)
 self.running = False

 def reconfigure(self, target_p95_ms: float = None, min_weight: int = None, period_s: float = None):
 if target_p95_ms is not None: self.target_p95 = float(target_p95_ms)
 if min_weight is not None: self.min_w = int(min_weight)
 if period_s is not None: self.period_s = float(period_s)
 return {"ok": True, "target_p95_ms": self.target_p95, "min_weight": self.min_w, "period_s": self.period_s}

 def stop(self): self.running = False

 def step(self):
 from ray import serve
 import ray
 rh = serve.get_deployment(self.router_name).get_handle()
 st = ray.get(rh.status.remote())
 w = st.get("weights", {})
 if not w: return {"ok": False, "reason": "no backends"}
 lat = st.get("lat_ewma", {})
 new_w = {}
 total_old = sum(max(0,int(x)) for x in w.values()) or 1
 total_new = 0
 for k, old in w.items():
 l = float(lat.get(k, self.target_p95))
 scale = max(0.5, min(1.5, self.target_p95 / max(1e-3, l)))
 cand = max(self.min_w, int(old * scale))
 new_w[k] = cand; total_new += cand
 # normalize
 if total_new > 0:
 norm = total_old / float(total_new)
 for k in new_w: new_w[k] = max(self.min_w, int(new_w[k] * norm))
 if new_w != w:
 return ray.get(rh.update.remote(new_w, st.get("shadow", False)))
 return {"ok": True, "weights": w}

 def run(self):
 self.running = True
 while self.running:
 try: self.step()
 except Exception: pass
 import time; time.sleep(self.period_s)
2.3 ServeService handler
atlas/rpc/server.py (append to ServeServicer):
from atlas.serve.autoscaler import RouterAutoscaler

class ServeServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.ServeServiceServicer):
 def __init__(self):
 if not ray.is_initialized(): ray.init()
 try: serve.start(detached=True)
 except RuntimeError: pass
 # Launch autoscaler once if you want a default instance; otherwise create on demand
 self._autoscaler = None

 def AutoScaleRouter(self, req, ctx):
 # Start or reconfigure autoscaler
 if req.enable:
 if self._autoscaler is None:
 self._autoscaler = RouterAutoscaler.options(name="router_autoscaler").remote(
 router_name="Router", target_p95_ms=req.target_p95_ms or 80.0,
 min_weight=req.min_weight or 5, period_s=req.period_s or 5.0)
 # fire-and-forget loop
 ray.get(self._autoscaler.run.remote())
 else:
 ray.get(self._autoscaler.reconfigure.remote(
 target_p95_ms=(req.target_p95_ms if req.target_p95_ms else None),
 min_weight=(req.min_weight if req.min_weight else None),
 period_s=(req.period_s if req.period_s else None)
 ))
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ON", info={
 "target_p95_ms": str(req.target_p95_ms or 80.0),
 "min_weight": str(req.min_weight or 5),
 "period_s": str(req.period_s or 5.0)
 })
 else:
 if self._autoscaler is not None:
 ray.get(self._autoscaler.stop.remote())
 self._autoscaler = None
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_OFF", info={})

 Tiny autoscaler test (monkey-patches serve.get_deployment/status, verifies reweight)
File: tests/test_autoscaler.py
import pytest
import ray
from atlas.serve.autoscaler import RouterAutoscaler

class DummyRouter:
 def __init__(self):
 self.last_update = None
 def status(self):
 # A is slow, B is fast
 return {"weights": {"A": 50, "B": 50}, "lat_ewma": {"A": 200.0, "B": 50.0}, "shadow": False}
 def update(self, new_w, shadow):
 self.last_update = (new_w, shadow)
 return {"weights": new_w, "shadow": shadow}

@pytest.mark.asyncio
async def test_autoscaler_rebalances(monkeypatch):
 dummy = DummyRouter()

 # Patch serve.get_deployment("Router").get_handle() to our dummy handle
 import atlas.serve.autoscaler as autoscaler_mod
 class DummyHandle:
 def __init__(self, r): self._r = r
 async def status(self): return self._r.status()
 async def update(self, w, s): return self._r.update(w, s)

 monkeypatch.setattr(autoscaler_mod.serve, "get_deployment",
 lambda name: type("D",(object,),{"get_handle": lambda self: DummyHandle(dummy)})())
 # ray.get returns the awaited result directly
 monkeypatch.setattr(autoscaler_mod.ray, "get", lambda fut: fut)

 RA = RouterAutoscaler.__new__(RouterAutoscaler) # bypass __init__
 RA.router_name = "Router"; RA.target_p95 = 100.0; RA.min_w = 5; RA.period_s = 1.0

 res = autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler.step(RA)
 assert "weights" in res, f"unexpected: {res}"
 assert res["weights"]["B"] > res["weights"]["A"], "B should gain weight when B faster"
 assert res["weights"]["A"] >= RA.min_w, "A must not drop below min weight"
This test runs without spinning up real Ray Serve; it monkey-patches the internals to simulate Routers status and update().

 ServeService.AutoScaleRouter (configure autoscaler at runtime)
Proto additions (api/atlas/v1/atlas.proto)  additive, backward compatible:
message AutoScaleConfig {
 string router = 1; // default "Router" or "ABRouter"
 double target_p95_ms = 2; // e.g., 80.0
 int32 min_weight = 3; // e.g., 5
 double period_s = 4; // e.g., 5.0
 bool enable = 5; // start/stop
}

service ServeService {
 // ... existing RPCs ...
 rpc AutoScaleRouter(AutoScaleConfig) returns (Status);
}
Handler (atlas/rpc/server.py):
from atlas.serve.autoscaler import RouterAutoscaler
import ray

class ServeServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.ServeServiceServicer):
 ...
 def AutoScaleRouter(self, req, ctx):
 name = f"autoscaler_{req.router or 'Router'}"
 if req.enable:
 try:
 actor = RouterAutoscaler.options(name=name).remote(
 router_name=req.router or "Router",
 target_p95_ms=req.target_p95_ms or 80.0,
 min_weight=req.min_weight or 5,
 period_s=req.period_s or 5.0
 )
 actor.run.remote() # fire-and-forget loop
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ON",
 info={"router": req.router or "Router",
 "target_p95_ms": str(req.target_p95_ms or 80.0),
 "min_weight": str(req.min_weight or 5),
 "period_s": str(req.period_s or 5.0)})
 except Exception as e:
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ERROR", info={"error": str(e)})
 else:
 try:
 # Try to get existing actor by name and stop it
 a = ray.get_actor(name)
 ray.get(a.stop.remote())
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_OFF", info={"router": req.router or "Router"})
 except Exception as e:
 return atlas_pb2.Status(state="AUTOSCALE_ERROR", info={"error": str(e)})
CLI (atlasctl) hook:
@serve_group.command("autoscale")

@click.option("--enable/--disable", default=True)
def autoscale(router, target_p95, min_weight, period, enable):
 # REST or gRPC depending on your client; REST example via grpc-gateway:
 import requests, json
 payload = {"router": router, "target_p95_ms": target_p95,
 "min_weight": min_weight, "period_s": period, "enable": enable}
 r = requests.post(f"{API}/v1/serve/autoscale", json=payload, timeout=15)
 click.echo(json.dumps(r.json(), indent=2))

1) Router: sliding window p95 + inflight counter + sticky
File: atlas/serve/router.py (replace/extend your Router)
import time, random, asyncio, collections, numpy as np
from ray import serve
from starlette.responses import JSONResponse

@serve.deployment(name="Router", route_prefix="/infer", num_replicas=1)
class Router:
 """
 Weighted A/B Router with:
 - sticky routing via header/cookie
 - latency window (fixed-size) per backend to compute p95
 - inflight counters (approximate queue/pressure)
 - shadow mirroring
 """
 def __init__(self, weights: dict = None, shadow: bool = False, sticky: bool = False,
 window_size: int = 200):
 self.weights = dict(weights) if weights else {}
 self.shadow = bool(shadow)
 self.sticky = bool(sticky)
 self.win_size = int(window_size)
 self._handles = {n: serve.get_deployment(n).get_handle() for n in self.weights}
 self._lat_win = {n: collections.deque(maxlen=self.win_size) for n in self.weights}
 self._inflight = collections.defaultdict(int)

 def _choose_weighted(self, user_key: str | None = None) -> str:
 names = list(self.weights.keys())
 if not names: return None
 if len(names) == 1: return names[0]
 tot = max(1, sum(max(0,int(w)) for w in self.weights.values()))
 if self.sticky and user_key:
 slot, csum = (hash(user_key) % tot) + 1, 0
 for k, w in self.weights.items():
 csum += max(0,int(w))
 if slot <= csum: return k
 return names[0]
 r, csum = random.randint(1, tot), 0
 for k, w in self.weights.items():
 csum += max(0,int(w))
 if r <= csum: return k
 return names[0]

 async def __call__(self, request):
 body = await request.json()
 user_key = request.headers.get("X-User-Id") or request.cookies.get("atlas_stick")
 chosen = self._choose_weighted(user_key)
 if not chosen:
 return JSONResponse({"error":"no backends configured"}, status_code=503)

 self._inflight[chosen] += 1
 t0 = time.perf_counter()
 res = await self._handles[chosen].remote(body)
 dur_ms = (time.perf_counter() - t0) * 1000.0
 self._inflight[chosen] = max(0, self._inflight[chosen] - 1)
 self._lat_win.setdefault(chosen, collections.deque(maxlen=self.win_size)).append(dur_ms)

 if self.shadow:
 for k, h in self._handles.items():
 if k != chosen:
 asyncio.create_task(h.remote(body))
 # set sticky cookie
 if self.sticky and not request.cookies.get("atlas_stick"):
 resp = JSONResponse(res)
 resp.set_cookie("atlas_stick", user_key or f"u{hash(time.time())}")
 return resp
 return res

 def status(self):
 """Expose current weights, shadow, sticky, p95 latencies, inflight counters."""
 lat_p95 = {}
 for k, win in self._lat_win.items():
 lat_p95[k] = float(np.percentile(list(win), 95)) if win else 0.0
 return {
 "weights": dict(self.weights),
 "shadow": self.shadow,
 "sticky": self.sticky,
 "lat_p95": lat_p95,
 "inflight": dict(self._inflight)
 }

 def update(self, weights: dict, shadow: bool = False, sticky: bool | None = None):
 self.weights = dict(weights) if weights else {}
 self.shadow = bool(shadow)
 if sticky is not None:
 self.sticky = bool(sticky)
 # refresh handles + latency windows
 for name in self.weights:
 if name not in self._handles:
 self._handles[name] = serve.get_deployment(name).get_handle()
 if name not in self._lat_win:
 self._lat_win[name] = collections.deque(maxlen=self.win_size)
 for name in list(self._handles.keys()):
 if name not in self.weights:
 self._handles.pop(name, None)
 self._lat_win.pop(name, None)
 self._inflight.pop(name, None)
 return {"ok": True, "weights": self.weights, "shadow": self.shadow, "sticky": self.sticky}

2) Autoscaler: use true p95 and inflight (pressure-aware)
File: atlas/serve/autoscaler.py (replace step() and add reconfigure())
import time, numpy as np, ray
from ray import serve

@ray.remote(num_cpus=0.1)
class RouterAutoscaler:
 def __init__(self, router_name: str = "Router", target_p95_ms: float = 80.0,
 min_weight: int = 5, period_s: float = 5.0, max_gain: float = 1.5, min_gain: float = 0.5):
 self.router_name = router_name
 self.target_p95 = float(target_p95_ms)
 self.min_w = int(min_weight)
 self.period_s = float(period_s)
 self.max_gain = float(max_gain)
 self.min_gain = float(min_gain)
 self.running = False

 def stop(self): self.running = False

 def reconfigure(self, target_p95_ms: float | None = None, min_weight: int | None = None, period_s: float | None = None):
 if target_p95_ms is not None: self.target_p95 = float(target_p95_ms)
 if min_weight is not None: self.min_w = int(min_weight)
 if period_s is not None: self.period_s = float(period_s)
 return {"ok": True, "target_p95_ms": self.target_p95, "min_weight": self.min_w, "period_s": self.period_s}

 def step(self):
 rh = serve.get_deployment(self.router_name).get_handle()
 st = ray.get(rh.status.remote()) # includes {"weights","lat_p95","inflight","shadow"}
 w = st.get("weights", {})
 if not w: return {"ok": False, "reason": "no backends"}
 lat = st.get("lat_p95", {})
 infl = st.get("inflight", {})
 new_w, total_old = {}, sum(max(0,int(v)) for v in w.values()) or 1

 # pressure-aware gain: penalize high p95 and high inflight
 for k, old in w.items():
 p95 = float(lat.get(k, self.target_p95))
 press = max(1.0, float(infl.get(k, 0)))
 # desired gain ~ target/p95 scaled down by pressure influence
 raw_gain = (self.target_p95 / max(1e-3, p95))
 gain = max(self.min_gain, min(self.max_gain, raw_gain / np.log1p(press)))
 cand = max(self.min_w, int(old * gain))
 new_w[k] = cand

 # normalize to keep sum stable
 total_new = sum(new_w.values()) or 1
 norm = total_old / float(total_new)
 for k in new_w:
 new_w[k] = max(self.min_w, int(new_w[k] * norm))

 if new_w != w:
 return ray.get(rh.update.remote(new_w, st.get("shadow", False)))
 return {"ok": True, "weights": w}

 def run(self):
 self.running = True
 while self.running:
 try: self.step()
 except Exception: pass
 time.sleep(self.period_s)

4) Updated autoscaler unit test (p95-driven, no EWMA)
File: tests/test_autoscaler_p95.py
import pytest
import atlas.serve.autoscaler as autoscaler_mod

class DummyRouterHandle:
 def __init__(self):
 self.updated = None
 self.status_payload = {
 "weights": {"A": 50, "B": 50},
 "lat_p95": {"A": 200.0, "B": 60.0},
 "inflight": {"A": 2, "B": 1}, # A is slower and more pressured
 "shadow": False
 }
 def status(self):
 return self.status_payload
 def update(self, w, s):
 self.updated = (dict(w), bool(s))
 return {"weights": dict(w), "shadow": bool(s)}

class DummyDeployment:
 def __init__(self, handle): self._h = handle
 def get_handle(self): return self._h

def test_autoscaler_step_p95(monkeypatch):
 dummy = DummyRouterHandle()
 # monkeypatch serve.get_deployment and ray.get
 monkeypatch.setattr(autoscaler_mod.serve, "get_deployment", lambda name: DummyDeployment(dummy))
 monkeypatch.setattr(autoscaler_mod.ray, "get", lambda fut: fut)

 # Construct autoscaler directly
 RA = autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler.__new__(autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler)
 RA.router_name = "Router"; RA.target_p95 = 100.0; RA.min_w = 5; RA.period_s = 1.0
 RA.max_gain = 1.5; RA.min_gain = 0.5

 out = autoscaler_mod.RouterAutoscaler.step(RA)
 assert "weights" in out or "ok" in out
 assert dummy.updated is not None, "router.update should be called"
 new_w, _ = dummy.updated
 # B is faster; should gain weight; A should not fall below min_w
 assert new_w["B"] > new_w["A"]
 assert new_w["A"] >= RA.min_w

1) Prometheus metrics (Grafana-ready)
1.1 Metrics registry & HTTP exporter
File: atlas/observability/metrics.py
from prometheus_client import Counter, Gauge, Histogram, Summary, start_http_server
import time

# --- TritRPC v1 alignment: record envelope codes (TRUE/MID/FALSE) per endpoint/tenant ---
REQUESTS = Counter(
 "atlas_rpc_requests_total",
 "Total RPC requests accepted by atlasd",
 ["endpoint", "tenant", "trit"] # trit  {TRUE,MID,FALSE}
)

# Admission & scheduling
QUEUE_DEPTH = Gauge("atlas_queue_depth", "Queued jobs", ["tenant"])
SCHEDULE_LATENCY = Histogram(
 "atlas_schedule_latency_seconds",
 "Time from QUEUED to RUNNING",
 buckets=[0.05, 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5],
 labelnames=["tenant"]
)
DRF_DOM_SHARE = Gauge("atlas_drf_dominant_share", "DRF dominant share by tenant and resource", ["tenant", "resource"])

# Trials
TRIAL_METRIC = Gauge("atlas_trial_metric", "Best metric per job", ["job_id", "metric"])
TRIAL_FLOPS = Gauge("atlas_trial_flops", "FLOPs of best trial", ["job_id"])
TRIAL_PARAMS = Gauge("atlas_trial_params", "Params of best trial", ["job_id"])

# ONNX checks
ONNX_COS_SIM = Gauge("atlas_onnx_cosine_similarity", "Cosine similarity PyTorchONNX for best trial", ["job_id"])
ONNX_EXPORTS = Counter("atlas_onnx_exports_total", "ONNX export attempts", ["job_id", "status"]) # status  {ok,fail}

# Serve routing & autoscaler
ROUTER_LAT_P95 = Gauge("atlas_router_latency_p95_ms", "Router p95 latency ms", ["backend"])
ROUTER_INFLIGHT = Gauge("atlas_router_inflight", "Router inflight requests", ["backend"])
ROUTER_WEIGHT = Gauge("atlas_router_weight", "Router weight per backend", ["backend"])
AUTOSCALE_ADJUST = Counter("atlas_router_autoscale_adjustments_total", "Autoscaler weight adjustments", ["backend", "reason"])

def start_metrics_server(port: int = 9108):
 """Start a Prometheus /metrics exporter on port. Call once in daemon init."""
 start_http_server(port)

# Helpers you can call from the daemon & runner
def record_request(endpoint: str, tenant: str, trit: str):
 REQUESTS.labels(endpoint=endpoint, tenant=tenant, trit=trit).inc()

def set_queue_depth(tenant: str, depth: int):
 QUEUE_DEPTH.labels(tenant=tenant).set(depth)

def observe_schedule_latency(tenant: str, seconds: float):
 SCHEDULE_LATENCY.labels(tenant=tenant).observe(seconds)

def set_drf_share(tenant: str, resource: str, share: float):
 DRF_DOM_SHARE.labels(tenant=tenant, resource=resource).set(share)

def record_best_trial(job_id: str, metric_name: str, metric_value: float, flops: float = None, params: float = None):
 TRIAL_METRIC.labels(job_id=job_id, metric=metric_name).set(metric_value)
 if flops is not None:
 TRIAL_FLOPS.labels(job_id=job_id).set(flops)
 if params is not None:
 TRIAL_PARAMS.labels(job_id=job_id).set(params)

def record_onnx_export(job_id: str, status: str, cos_sim: float = None):
 ONNX_EXPORTS.labels(job_id=job_id, status=status).inc()
 if cos_sim is not None:
 ONNX_COS_SIM.labels(job_id=job_id).set(cos_sim)

def set_router_stats(lat_p95: dict, inflight: dict, weights: dict):
 for k,v in (lat_p95 or {}).items():
 ROUTER_LAT_P95.labels(backend=k).set(float(v))
 for k,v in (inflight or {}).items():
 ROUTER_INFLIGHT.labels(backend=k).set(float(v))
 for k,v in (weights or {}).items():
 ROUTER_WEIGHT.labels(backend=k).set(float(v))

def record_autoscale_adjust(backend: str, reason: str):
 AUTOSCALE_ADJUST.labels(backend=backend, reason=reason).inc()
Enable exporter in daemon (cmd/atlasd/main.py):
from atlas.observability.metrics import start_metrics_server
start_metrics_server(int(os.getenv("ATLAS_METRICS_PORT", "9108")))
Update code paths to record metrics:
 Admission: record_request("SubmitTuneStudy", tenant, "MID" | "FALSE"), set_queue_depth(tenant, len(queue)).
 When RUNNING: observe_schedule_latency(...)
 After best trial: record_best_trial(job_id, metric, best.metrics[metric], flops, params); record_onnx_export(job_id, "ok", cos_sim).
 Router status: in Router.status(), call set_router_stats(lat_p95, inflight, weights).
 Autoscaler: on every adjust, record_autoscale_adjust(backend, "p95" | "pressure").
