2) Loki (Grafana stack) stub
Structured logs (JSON) with TritRPC fields:
 Key fields: ts, service, tenant, job_id, endpoint, trit, state, message, extra.
 Emit to stdout; promtail ships to Loki.
Log helper (atlas/observability/logs.py):
import json, sys, time, os

def log_event(service: str, endpoint: str, tenant: str, trit: str, state: str, job_id: str = "", message: str = "", **extra):
 evt = {
 "ts": time.strftime('%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ'),
 "service": service,
 "endpoint": endpoint,
 "tenant": tenant,
 "trit": trit, # TRUE|MID|FALSE
 "state": state, # e.g., QUEUED|RUNNING|SUCCEEDED|FAILED
 "job_id": job_id,
 "msg": message,
 **extra
 }
 print(json.dumps(evt), file=sys.stdout, flush=True)
Promtail config (promtail-config.yml):
server:
 http_listen_port: 9080
 grpc_listen_port: 0

positions:
 filename: /tmp/positions.yaml

clients:
 - url: http://loki:3100/loki/api/v1/push

scrape_configs:
 - job_name: atlasd-logs
 static_configs:
 - targets: [localhost]
 labels:
 job: atlasd
 __path__: /var/log/atlasd/*.log # or stdout from container
Grafana Loki queries
 Errors last 15m: {job="atlasd"} |= "FAILED"
 Trit distribution: {job="atlasd"} | json | count_over_time({trit=~".*"}[5m]) by (trit,endpoint)
 Admissions by tenant: {job="atlasd"} | json | line_format "{{.tenant}} {{.endpoint}} {{.trit}}"

3) TritRPC v1 alignment (end-to-end)
 TRIT codes (TRUE/MID/FALSE) are reflected in:
 gRPC envelope (TritStatus),
 Prometheus metrics label trit,
 Loki JSON logs field trit.
 Admission/Scheduling/Execution log and metric calls are present throughout (e.g., record_request, observe_schedule_latency, log_event on transitions).
 gRPC metadata can include x-trit-code header if you want to mirror over REST.

4) Autoscaler: switch to true p95 & pressure (wired)
(Already provided in previous reply.) Router computes p95 with a sliding window; autoscaler reads lat_p95 and inflight, and adjusts weights subject to a min weight and max_gain/min_gain damping. Metrics and logs:
# in autoscaler.step()
record_autoscale_adjust(backend, "p95_adjust")
log_event("atlasd","Serve.AutoScale","system","TRUE","WEIGHT_ADJUST", message="reweight", backend=backend, new_weight=new_w[backend])

5) Sticky routing RPC (independent toggle)
(Already provided.) We add RouterSticky(sticky) to ServeService for toggling stickiness without mutating weights/shadow.

6) Append small unit test for autoscaler (p95 test)
(Already provided above as tests/test_autoscaler_p95.py.)

How to enable (one pass)
0. Launch Prometheus & Grafana; add scrape for atlasd :9108 and (optionally) Serve gateway.
0. Run promtail pointing at your container stdout or a log folder; connect to Loki.
0. In daemon:
 call start_metrics_server() in main;
 sprinkle record_request, observe_schedule_latency, record_best_trial, and record_onnx_exportin the relevant code paths (submit, queue depth changes, after best trial, etc.).
 use log_event on TRIT transitions (queuedrunning, success/failure).
0. In Router:
 compute p95 in status() and expose inflight/weights; autoscaler now uses that.
 call set_router_stats(lat_p95, inflight, weights) periodically (e.g., every time status() is called, or in a small background loop).
0. Use atlasctl serve autoscale to enable autoscaler; atlasctl serve router:status to inspect weights; atlasctl serve router to override.

This completes a Grafana-ready observability surface (Prometheus + Loki), fully TritRPC v1aligned, and integrates with your A/B router + autoscaler + sticky routing. If you want, I can also export a starter Grafana dashboard JSON with the PromQL queries above wired into panels.

Yes  Ive now folded the new materials you uploaded into the mentoring + deep learning framework view. Heres where we stand:
1. Conceptual Foundation
 Self-organization of complex, intelligent systems provides the action ontology backbone: how components self-assemble, adapt, and rewire. We mapped this into the classification/decomposition/reassembly pipeline so the AI can be mentored not only in what models exist but also how to reorganize them dynamically.
 This supports our earlier Atlas + OS services work by giving it a living systems frame  updates, rewiring, and evolution are naturalized, not bolted on.
2. Practical Inventory
 From the Deep Learning Archives and Model Zoo compendium (341 pages), we now have a taxonomy of cells, layers, and models:
 CNNs, RNNs, GRUs, LSTMs (cell-level).
 Object detection (YOLO, Faster/Mask/RetinaNet, Detectron2, MMDetection).
 Generative families (GANs, VAE, Diffusion, StyleGAN/BigGAN).
 Speech/text (Tacotron, WaveNet, DeepSpeech2, Transformer TTS).
 Reinforcement Learning (AlphaZero, PPO, A3C/A2C, SAC, TRPO, RLlib).
 Graph Neural Networks (GCN, GAT, PointNet/PointNet++, MolCLR).
 Meta/transfer/few-shot (MAML, MetaFormer, Prototypical Nets, Lottery Ticket).
 These are aligned to operations and hyperparameters (activation, dropout, block dropout, weight decay, LR schedules, batch size, optimizer types, attention heads, etc.), and annotated with where Ray Tune grid-search + DRF/ASHA applies.
3. Mentoring & Traceability Layer
 Weve reframed this as a mentoring framework for the AI itself:
 Each model = a case study in decomposition and rewiring.
 Each hyperparameter = a knob the system can learn to optimize, log, and compare.
 Each trial (via Ray Tune + TritRPC service layer) = a mentored exercise where results are automatically logged in the ledger, checked with ONNX round-trip, and visualized in Grafana.
 The Atlas trace + model cards serve as the mentoring logbook: provenance, metrics, configs, lineage.
4. Update Framework
 New models or techniques (say, new GAN variant or attention mechanism) can be onboarded by:
0. Classification  what family does it belong to? (CV/NLP/Graph/Generative/RL/etc.)
0. Decomposition  break into primitives (cells/layers, activation, optimizers).
0. Rewiring  match into existing service templates (trainer, Ray Tune study, ONNX exporter, Serve deployment).
0. Validation  ONNX round-trip, cosine-sim check, DRF resource allocation fairness, p95 autoscaling.
0. Promotion  model card generated + Grafana panels updated automatically.

 Taxonomy-aware (Model Zoo list).
 Ontology-grounded (self-organization principles).
 Implementation-ready (OS-level service, Ray + ONNX + Serve plane).
 Mentoring-enabled (each training/evaluation is a guided apprenticeship step).

Absolutely  heres how we turn everything youve built into a living mentoring + deep-learning framework and wire the rewiring capability into the system end-to-end. Ive folded in the conceptual system files you provided and mapped them concretely onto the Atlas/OS Service, Serve plane, Studies, and Dashboard so its coherent, teachable, and operational.

Mentors Guide (Part 3)  Learning by Rewiring
Purpose. Make onboarding a guided apprenticeship: every new model is classified  decomposed  rewired  mentored through reproducible studies, observed in Grafana, and promoted with provenance.
How the Guide reads. Each chapter uses context  mechanics  consequence (your writing rule) so it teaches why before what to click.
A. Cognitive frame (why rewiring works)
 Reflexive hypergraph of knowing: treat each model/layer/adapter as a fiber projected from a shared semantic space; rewiring is re-aligning fibers, not bolting parts. We borrow your Hopf fibration metaphor (Są user frame, Sł semantic total space, S˛ projected understanding) to explain why classification  decomposition  recomposition creates cognitive resonance instead of sprawl.
 Agent-first OS-native nodes: emphasize the user/agent is primary; the platform serves agents, not the other way around. Every rewiring is a small local cognitive act that a node can reason about, try, and promote.
B. Operational frame (where rewiring runs)
 Corrected execution model: rewiring runs host-first when tiny/fast, LMS K3s when it needs isolation/GPU/PII, edge for sensor-adjacent inference, and fog/cloud only when necessary; same contracts everywhere. This section teaches smallest-sufficient tier.
 Dual orchestration: canonical rewires sit in governed Airflow DAGs; opportunistic fan-out can flow to the federated mesh (WUs in containers/WASM) and reduce back under policy. Students learn when/why to send a rewire to the mesh and how verification modes (redundant/TEE/spot/ZK) establish trust.
C. Contract frame (how rewiring is recorded and moves)
 Avro  JSON-LD/SALAD  TritRPC: all rewiring requests and results are Avro-typed, semantically pinned (CONTEXT-ID), and ride the same ternary-aware envelope (B2/B3/Q3) so meaning and audit survive transport. This chapter includes briefs + code snippets for Path A (Avro-binary-in-TritRPC) and Path B (Avro-T3 ternary encoding) with canonical TritPack243 bytes and AEAD.
D. Threat-model frame (how we stay safe)
 Objectives & threats: we frame the UX and service plane around no remote code execution, policy-first CSS, deterministic manifests, and capability-scoped actions; the Guide ties every step (study  serve  UI) back to the threat model.

Integrating rewiring into the System (concrete changes)
Below is exactly how the rewiring flow becomes a first-class, auditable path across the stack.
1) Agent-first node  LMS ladder (placing rewires)
 Host (agentd) receives a RewireIntent (Avro) from the User Agent. It classifies the intent (CV/NLP/Graph/Gen/RL), validates constraints (S,L,D,P,I,C,A), and either:
 runs a local study (OS-native) if tiny/low-latency, or
 offloads to LMS Ray (K3s) with a ServeService request (our gRPC).
 Why: preserves autonomy and speed; follows your corrected model that keeps Ray off the workstation for predictable, OS-native ergonomics.
Deliverables wired
 agentd/agentctl accept RewireIntent (Avro)  calls OrchestratorService.SubmitTuneStudy with the same envelope.
 Policy compiles placement heuristics from S,L,D,P,I,C,A; logs TritRPC TRIT=MID on admission; updates queue depth metric.
2) Studies as mentoring exercises (learning by doing)
 Weve added studies/ (RetinaNet, DeepLab, BERT, T5-REBEL, Diffusion UNet, GNN, PPO) that are config-driven and:
 produce a Math Ledger (params/FLOPs/activations, precision/quant, shapes),
 export ONNX, run an onnxruntime round-trip cosine check, and write onnx_check.json,
 report the correct metric via ctx.report() for ASHA/DRF scheduling.
 Students and agents learn what wires matter by observing how tweaks (LoRA rank, DropPath, ASPP rates, FPN levels, attention heads) affect FLOPs/metrics tradeoffs.
Deliverables wired
 studies/*.py + slate/utils/ledger.py (export_to_onnx, onnx_roundtrip_check, write_onnx_check).
 Ledger callback collects per-trial [MATH_LEDGER] lines; consolidated ledger.json saved for the best trial.
3) Serve plane with A/B router + autoscaler + sticky
 Deploy: ServeService.Deploy registers ONNX models as named deployments.
 Route: Router (Serve deployment) uses sliding window p95 + inflight and can do sticky routing(cookie/header) so a user keeps a consistent experience while we test candidates.
 Autoscale/Adjust: an Autoscaler actor reweights A/B weights to meet p95 SLO, considering queue pressure; RouterSticky RPC toggles per-user stickiness independent of weights/shadow.
 Why: the mentoring loop can safely test rewired models in live traffic (small %), observe p95, and promote only on Trust + SLO.
Deliverables wired
 ServeService (Deploy/Scale/List/ConfigureRouter/GetRouter/RouterSticky/AutoScaleRouter); Router (p95 window + sticky); Autoscaler (p95+pressure aware).
 Router test and autoscaler test included.
4) Governance: Airflow  Mesh integration (rewire at scale)
 When a rewire is embarrassingly parallel (feature extraction, distillation sweeps), Airflows MeshOperator can publish Work Units (WUs) to the federated mesh (Docker/Lightning/WASM) and collect verified results back.
 The same Avro+JSON-LD+TritRPC contracts apply; proof modes (redundant, TEE, ZK) are set per WU policy.
 Why: matches your Dual-Orchestration Model; keeps semantics and contracts invariant across the governed and volunteer planes.
5) Semantic fibration  rewiring maps (how we know a rewire is valid)
 We model decomposed model parts (cells/layers/blocks/adapters) as hypergraph patterns with roles (connector/role mapping). A candidate rewire is a morphism between patterns; promotion runs SHACL on the RDF projection to ensure constraints (e.g., channel/stride divisibility, tensor compatibility) hold beforedeployment.
 This grounds the act of rewiring in your SąSłS˛ fibration picture: the projection we present (S˛) remains aligned with the coherent semantic total space (Sł), not just whatever assembly runs.
6) TritRPC + Avro SALAD as the mentoring paper trail
 Every intent, tune result, ledger, ONNX check, model card, and deployment change rides a single canonical frame (SCHEMA-ID + CONTEXT-ID + AEAD) that can cross B2 now and B3/Q3 later without re-signing (TritPack243).
 Why: from trits to trust isnt metaphor  its the assurance that our rewiring history is unforgeable, replayable, and semantically pinned everywhere it travels.
7) Observability & mentoring dashboards
 The Grafana starter dashboard shows:
 RPC volume by TRIT (TRUE/MID/FALSE) and endpoint,
 Queue depth, DRF dominant share per tenant,
 Scheduling latency p50/p95,
 Best-trial metric/FLOPs/params,
 ONNX cosine similarity (pass/fail gauge),
 Router p95 per backend, weights, inflight, and Autoscaler adjust rate,
 Loki panel for TRIT-stamped logs (QUEUED  RUNNING  SUCCEEDED/FAILED).
 Why: the mentor and the learner (human or agent) both see causeeffectpromotion transparently.

How the System Docs you uploaded slot in (explicit mapping)
 The Semantic Fibration  Mentors Guide Ch. A & §5: model-as-hypergraph; rewiring as fiber alignment; promotion gates keep projections coherent.
 Objectives & Threat Model  Mentors Guide Ch. D + Serve/LDT-UI policies (no remote JS/CSS, capability-scoped actions).
 From Trits to Trust  Contracts & Federation (§3, §6): envelope, transport-independent semantics, federation sanity.
 Agent-First Node Architecture  Placement & Agents (§1): OS-native agent kernel, on-node memory fabric, host-first reasoning.
 Corrected Execution Model (by tier)  Where rewiring runs (§1): host vs LMS vs edge vs fog; smallest-sufficient tier.
 Dual-Orchestration Model  AirflowMesh (§4): MeshOperator, WU policy/proofs; same semantics on both planes.
 TritRPC for Avro: Spec Sketch  Contracts (§3): Path A/B, TritPack243, AEAD, Kafka/SR integration, test vectors next.

What well ship in the living documentation bundle
0. Mentors Guide (Part 3)  the doc that ties taxonomy, ontology, and implementation into a single learning path; includes:
 Rewiring cookbook (CV/NLP/Graph/Gen/RL families)

Mentors Guide (Part 3)  Living Deep Learning Framework for Rewiring (TritRPC-first)
This guide ties together taxonomy, ontology, and implementation into a single learning + mentoring framework. It teaches how to onboard, decompose, rewire, and mentor new models in the Atlas/OS Service ecosystem. It builds on the conceptual base (selforganization, reflexive hypergraphs, semantic fibration) and the operational base (Atlas/OS repo, Serve plane, Studies, and Grafana dashboard).

1. Cognitive Frame  Why Rewiring Works
 Ontology: Each model, layer, or adapter is a fiber in a reflexive hypergraph; rewiring is aligning fibers, not bolting parts.
 Semantic fibration: Są (agent/user view) projects through Sł (semantic total space) to S˛ (model representation). Rewiring keeps the projection consistent with the whole.
 Agentfirst: The user/agent is primary; the OS service plane supports their reasoning and choices.
Mentoring principle: Every rewire is a small, legible act of learning; provenance and contracts ensure knowledge accumulates, not fragments.

2. Operational Frame  Where Rewiring Runs
 Corrected execution tiers:
 Host (agentd)  fast, OSnative, privacysafe rewires.
 LMS/K3s (Ray cluster)  heavier, multiGPU rewires with isolation.
 Edge/Fog/Cloud  scaling tiers; same contracts everywhere.
 Dual orchestration:
 Canonical  Airflow DAGs with promotion gates.
 Federated  Mesh fanout (WUs in Docker/WASM) under policy.
Mentoring principle: Always use the smallestsufficient tier; teach why placement matters for cost, trust, and latency.

3. Contract Frame  How Rewires Are Recorded
 TritRPC-first: All intents, trials, promotions, and serve operations use the TritRPC envelope (TRIT = TRUE/MID/FALSE) as the protocol of record. gRPC/HTTP/Kafka are transports only. The envelope travels unchanged across transports and tiers.
 Avro SALAD + JSONLD: Payloads are Avro-typed and semantically pinned via JSONLD contexts. The TritRPC envelope carries code|reason|meta and is mirrored in transport headers (e.g., Kafka x-trit-code).
 Two serialize paths:
 Path A  Avro binary in TritRPC (over HTTP/2 or HTTP/1.1)
 Path B  AvroT3 ternary encoding (TritPack243) for B3/Q3 channels
 Immutable trail: Each trial emits ledger.json, onnx_check.json, model_card.json (+ trace SVG/JSON). Promotion writes a signed, auditable card.
Mentoring principle: The protocol is TritRPC; the plumbing can vary. Consistency of the envelope is what guarantees traceability.

4. ThreatModel Frame  How We Stay Safe
 No remote JS/CSS; policyfirst UI.
 Deterministic manifests.
 Capabilityscoped actions.
 Placement rules from S,L,D,P,I,C,A (Security, Latency, Data, Policy, Integrity, Cost, Availability).
Mentoring principle: Every exercise ties back to threat objectives: show how choices protect autonomy and security.

5. Studies as Mentoring Exercises
Prewired studies (RetinaNet, DeepLab, BERT, T5REBEL, Diffusion UNet, Graph GNN, PPO) demonstrate:
 Math Ledger logging (FLOPs, params, activations, precision/quant).
 ONNX export + runtime cosine check.
 Metric reporting (mAP, mIoU, F1, tripleF1, val_loss, val_acc, reward).
Mentoring principle: Students see how small changes (LoRA rank, DropPath, ASPP rates, attention heads) affect FLOPs  metric tradeoffs.

6. Serve Plane  Live Rewire Testing (TritRPC Services)
 TritRPC Services:ServeService.Deploy|Scale|List|ConfigureRouter|GetRouter|RouterSticky|AutoScaleRouter.
 Router: p95 sliding window + inflight counters + sticky per-user routing.
 Autoscaler: adjusts A/B weights to meet p95 SLO, pressure-aware.
 Mentored deployment: Candidates shadow/live at 5%, sticky ensures user coherence, auto-promotion only if metric  threshold and SLO holds.
Mentoring principle: Teach safe experimentation in production; how to observe p95/weights and when to promote  all via TritRPC calls.

 ServeService RPCs: Deploy, Scale, List, ConfigureRouter, GetRouter, RouterSticky, AutoScaleRouter.
 Router: p95 sliding window + inflight counters + sticky peruser routing.
 Autoscaler: adjusts A/B weights to meet p95 SLO, pressureaware.
 Mentored deployment: Candidates shadow/live at 5%, sticky ensures user coherence, autopromotion only if metric  threshold and SLO holds.
Mentoring principle: Teach safe experimentation in production; how to observe p95/weights and when to promote.

7. Governance: Airflow  Mesh
 Airflow MeshOperator: Launch WUs to federated mesh for embarrassingly parallel rewires.
 Verification: redundant, TEE, ZK proofs; results converge back under TritRPC.
 Policy continuity: semantics invariant across orchestrators.
Mentoring principle: Show how global cooperation is possible without breaking local trust.

8. Observability  Mentors Dashboard (TritRPC-aware)
Grafana panels:
 RPCs by endpoint+TRIT (TRUE/MID/FALSE).
 Queue depth + DRF shares.
 Scheduling latency p95.
 Best trial metrics/FLOPs/params.
 ONNX cos_sim gauge.
 Router p95/weights/inflight.
 Autoscaler adjust rate.
 Loki log panel with TRIT transitions (QUEUED  RUNNING  SUCCEEDED/FAILED).
Mentoring principle: Students see a continuous lab notebook: rewires, metrics, promotion decisions  all TritRPC-stamped  visible in real time.

Grafana panels:
 RPCs by endpoint+TRIT.
 Queue depth + DRF shares.
 Scheduling latency p95.
 Best trial metrics/FLOPs/params.
 ONNX cos_sim gauge.
 Router p95/weights/inflight.
 Autoscaler adjust rate.
 Loki log panel with TRIT transitions (QUEUED  RUNNING  SUCCEEDED/FAILED).
Mentoring principle: Students see a continuous lab notebook: rewires, metrics, promotion decisions all visible in real time.

9. Integration Guide  Adding a New Model
0. Classify: what task/family/data/metric?
0. Decompose: break into Atlas cells/blocks.
0. Rewire: map blocks into service templates; expose knobs.
0. Validate: run study; ledger+onnx_check produced.
0. Promote: card+trace generated; auto_promotion if metric  threshold.
0. Observe: Grafana/Loki shows flow; mentor reviews.

10. Living Documentation Bundle (TritRPC-first)
This bundle includes:
 Atlas/OS Service repo (proto, daemon, TritRPC service layer for Serve, autoscaler, observability, CLI, policy).
 Studies/ folder (Retina, DeepLab, BERT, Rebel, Diffusion, GNN, PPO).
 Dashboard JSONs (starter Grafana + Loki log panels).
 Mentors Guide (Part 3) and MODEL_INTEGRATION.md.
Transport note: Use TritRPC over HTTP/2 (or HTTP/1.1 via gateway) and TritRPC headers in Kafka (no Flink). The envelope is identical across transports.

This bundle includes:
 Atlas/OS Service repo (proto, daemon, Serve plane, autoscaler, observability, CLI, policy).
 Studies/ folder (Retina, DeepLab, BERT, Rebel, Diffusion, GNN, PPO).
 Dashboard JSONs (starter Grafana + Loki log panels).

Appendix: TritRPC Transport Examples
HTTP/JSON (gateway)
POST /v1/tune HTTP/1.1
Host: atlasd:8080
Content-Type: application/json
x-trit-code: MID
x-tenant-id: tenantA
x-context-id: ctx123

{ "ir": {"yaml": "..."}, "grid": {"json": "..."}, "train": {"uri": "s3://..."}, "metric": "f1", "mode": "max" }
Response:
{"trit":{"code":"TRUE","reason":"queued","meta":{"job_id":"job-abc"}}}
gRPC mapping (TritRPC over HTTP/2)
rpc SubmitTuneStudy(SubmitTuneRequest) returns (SubmitTuneReply);
 Metadata: x-trit-code: MID, x-tenant-id: tenantA, x-context-id: ctx123
 Payload: Avro-encoded or JSON mapping of SubmitTuneRequest.
 Reply: SubmitTuneReply with TritStatus (code/reason/meta).
Kafka headers
Topic: atlas.rewire.intent
Key: intent-123
Headers:
 x-trit-code = MID
 x-tenant-id = tenantA
 x-context-id = ctx123
Value (Avro JSON):
{"intent_id":"intent-123","tenant":"tenantA","task":"DET","family":"Retina","ir_yaml":"...","metric":"f1","mode":"max","context_id":"ctx123"}

Closing principle: Rewiring is not just engineering  it is learning. Every rewire is a mentored step, traceable, observable, and promotable under trust.

Awesome  here are small, drop-in code blocks to (1) run SHACL validation on a trials RDF export before promotion, and (2) emit JSON-LD alongside model_card.json with ontology types and context.
Everything is TritRPC-first and aligns to your ontology folder (ontology/atlas.ttl, ontology/shacl/constraints.ttl, ontology/contexts/atlas.jsonld).

1) Dependencies
Add to your service requirements (where you install daemon deps):
rdflib>=6.3.2
pyshacl>=0.23.0

2) JSON-LD emitters (model_card  JSON-LD & Turtle)
File: atlas/semantics/emit_jsonld.py
import os, json
from datetime import datetime
from typing import Dict, Any

# Simple JSON-LD emitter for model cards; attach @context and @type using your ontology
def model_card_to_jsonld(card: Dict[str, Any],
 context_url: str = "/ontology/contexts/atlas.jsonld") -> Dict[str, Any]:
 """
 Given a model_card dict (as written by Registry.promote), return a JSON-LD dict
 with @context and @type mapped to the ontology.
 """
 model_id = card["model"]["id"]
 tenant = card["model"].get("tenant","default")
 created = card["model"].get("created_at", datetime.utcnow().strftime('%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ'))
 onnx = card.get("onnx", {})
 data = card.get("data", {})
 metrics = card.get("metrics", {})
 ledger = card.get("ledger", {})

 # Minimal JSON-LD framing
 node = {
 "@context": context_url,
 "@id": f"urn:atlas:model:{model_id}",
 "@type": "Model",
 "tenant": tenant,
 "createdAt": created,
 "promotesTo": { "@id": f"urn:atlas:model:{model_id}" }, # self-promote for simple framing
 "produces": { "@id": f"urn:atlas:artifact:{model_id}" },
 "governedBy": card.get("policy_ref") or "",
 "hasLedger": { "@id": f"urn:atlas:ledger:{model_id}" },
 "dataset": {
 "@type": "Dataset",
 "trainUri": data.get("train_uri",""),
 "valUri": data.get("val_uri",""),
 "datasetHash": data.get("dataset_hash","unknown")
 },
 "onnx": {
 "@type": "Artifact",
 "onnxPath": onnx.get("path",""),
 "opset": onnx.get("opset"),
 "providers": onnx.get("providers", [])
 },
 "metrics": metrics,
 "ledgerData": ledger
 }
 return node
Optional Turtle export with RDFLib (useful if you want to validate Turtle instead of JSON-LD):
File: atlas/semantics/emit_rdf.py
from rdflib import Graph, Namespace, Literal, URIRef
from rdflib.namespace import RDF, RDFS, XSD

ATLAS = Namespace("https://atlas.example.org/ont#")

def model_card_to_turtle(card: dict, ontology_ttl: str = "ontology/atlas.ttl") -> str:
 g = Graph()
 g.parse(ontology_ttl, format="turtle")

 model_id = card["model"]["id"]
 model_uri = URIRef(f"urn:atlas:model:{model_id}")
 g.add((model_uri, RDF.type, ATLAS.Model))
 g.add((model_uri, RDFS.label, Literal(f"Model {model_id}")))
 g.add((model_uri, ATLAS.tenant, Literal(card["model"].get("tenant","default"))))
 g.add((model_uri, ATLAS.createdAt, Literal(card["model"].get("created_at"), datatype=XSD.dateTime)))

 # ONNX artifact
 onnx = card.get("onnx",{})
 art_uri = URIRef(f"urn:atlas:artifact:{model_id}")
 g.add((art_uri, RDF.type, ATLAS.Artifact))
 if onnx.get("path"):
 g.add((art_uri, ATLAS.onnxPath, Literal(onnx["path"])))
 g.add((model_uri, ATLAS.produces, art_uri))

 # Ledger
 led_uri = URIRef(f"urn:atlas:ledger:{model_id}")
 g.add((led_uri, RDF.type, ATLAS.Ledger))
 g.add((model_uri, ATLAS.hasLedger, led_uri))

 return g.serialize(format="turtle")

3) SHACL validation runner
File: atlas/semantics/shacl_validate.py
import os
from typing import Tuple
from rdflib import Graph
from pyshacl import validate

def validate_trial_graph_turtle(turtle_str: str,
 shapes_path: str = "ontology/shacl/constraints.ttl",
 ontology_path: str = "ontology/atlas.ttl") -> Tuple[bool, str]:
 """
 Validate a trial/model graph (in Turtle) against SHACL shapes.
 Returns (conforms, report_text).
 """
 data_g = Graph()
 data_g.parse(data=turtle_str, format="turtle")

 # Load shapes
 shacl_g = Graph()
 shacl_g.parse(shapes_path, format="turtle")

 # Import ontology (optional)
 ont_g = Graph()
 if ontology_path and os.path.exists(ontology_path):
 ont_g.parse(ontology_path, format="turtle")

 conforms, _, report_text = validate(
 data_graph=data_g,
 shacl_graph=shacl_g,
 ont_graph=ont_g,
 inference='rdfs',
 abort_on_first=False,
 allow_warnings=True
 )
 return bool(conforms), str(report_text)

Patch: atlas/registry.py (augment promote())
# add at top
from atlas.semantics.emit_jsonld import model_card_to_jsonld

from atlas.semantics.shacl_validate import validate_trial_graph_turtle

class Registry:
 ...
 def promote(self, job_id: str, req: Dict[str,Any], best: Dict[str,Any]):
 card = {
 "model": {"id": job_id, "family": req.get("entrypoint",""), "task": req.get("task",""),
 "tenant": req.get("tenant","default"), "created_at": time.strftime('%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ')},
 "data": {"train_uri": req.get("train",{}).get("uri",""), "val_uri": req.get("val",{}).get("uri",""),
 "dataset_hash": req.get("dataset_hash","unknown")},
 "metrics": best.get("metrics", {}),
 "ledger": {}, # fill if you consolidate best trial ledger
 "onnx": {"path": req.get("export",{}).get("onnx",{}).get("path",""),
 "opset": req.get("export",{}).get("onnx",{}).get("opset"),
 "providers": req.get("export",{}).get("onnx",{}).get("providers",[])},
 "policy_ref": req.get("policy_ref")
 }

 outdir = os.path.join(self.root, job_id)
 os.makedirs(outdir, exist_ok=True)
 # Write model_card.json
 with open(os.path.join(outdir, "model_card.json"), "w") as f:
 json.dump(card, f, indent=2)

 # Emit model_card.jsonld using ontology context
 card_jsonld = model_card_to_jsonld(card, context_url="/ontology/contexts/atlas.jsonld")
 with open(os.path.join(outdir, "model_card.jsonld"), "w") as f:
 json.dump(card_jsonld, f, indent=2)

 # Optional: build a small Turtle graph for SHACL
 turtle = model_card_to_turtle(card, ontology_ttl="ontology/atlas.ttl")
 conforms, report = validate_trial_graph_turtle(turtle,
 shapes_path="ontology/shacl/constraints.ttl",
 ontology_path="ontology/atlas.ttl")
 # If invalid, you can block promotion or log a warning
 if not conforms:
 # block or record in status; here we block by raising
 raise ValueError(f"SHACL validation failed for job {job_id}:\n{report}")

 return card
Choice: You can choose to block promotion on SHACL failure (as above) or only log and continue. If you dont want to block, replace the raise with a log line.

Why this matters
 SHACL gives you a formal gate: no promotion without the required evidence (ledger, artifact, typed stats).
 JSON-LD ensures model cards and trials can be queried (SPARQL/RDF datasets), visualized, and verifiedbeyond CSV/JSON silos.
 The TritRPC envelope and context_id keep transport & semantics aligned: the same knowledge can flow via HTTP/2, Kafka, or A2A messages without losing meaning.

Great call. Heres a clean, drop-in way to add a daemon CLI switch --shacl-enforce=true|false and wire it so SHACL violations either block promotion or are logged (non-blocking), without touching the rest of your flow.

1) Parse the CLI flag in the daemon and pass it to the Registry
File: cmd/atlasd/main.py (add argparse + pass flag to Registry)
# at top
import argparse
from atlas.registry import Registry

if __name__=="__main__":
 parser = argparse.ArgumentParser()
 parser.add_argument("--shacl-enforce", default=os.getenv("ATLAS_SHACL_ENFORCE","true"),
 help="true|false: block promotion on SHACL violations (default true)")
 args = parser.parse_args()

 shacl_enforce = str(args.shacl_enforce).lower() in ("1", "true", "yes", "on")

 policy = Policy.from_file(os.environ.get("ATLAS_POLICY","/etc/atlas/policy.yaml"))
 artifacts_root = os.environ.get("ATLAS_ARTIFACTS","artifacts")

 # Registry now accepts enforce flag
 daemon = Daemon(policy, artifacts_root, shacl_enforce=shacl_enforce)
 daemon.run()
Also update your Daemon to pass the flag when constructing the Registry:
class Daemon:
 def __init__(self, policy, artifacts_root, shacl_enforce=True):
 self.policy = policy
 self.registry = Registry(artifacts_root, shacl_enforce=shacl_enforce)
 ...

2) Registry respects the flag in promote()
File: atlas/registry.py (add a constructor param + conditional logic)
# add at top if not already:
import logging
from atlas.semantics.emit_jsonld import model_card_to_jsonld
from atlas.semantics.emit_rdf import model_card_to_turtle
from atlas.semantics.shacl_validate import validate_trial_graph_turtle

class Registry:
 def __init__(self, root: str, shacl_enforce: bool = True):
 self.root = root
 self.shacl_enforce = shacl_enforce
 os.makedirs(root, exist_ok=True)

 def promote(self, job_id: str, req: Dict[str,Any], best: Dict[str,Any]):
 card = {
 "model": {"id": job_id, "family": req.get("entrypoint",""), "task": req.get("task",""),
 "tenant": req.get("tenant","default"),
 "created_at": time.strftime('%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ')},
 "data": {"train_uri": req.get("train",{}).get("uri",""),
 "val_uri": req.get("val",{}).get("uri",""),
 "dataset_hash": req.get("dataset_hash","unknown")},
 "metrics": best.get("metrics", {}),
 "ledger": {}, # populate with consolidated best trial ledger if you like
 "onnx": {"path": req.get("export",{}).get("onnx",{}).get("path",""),
 "opset": req.get("export",{}).get("onnx",{}).get("opset"),
 "providers": req.get("export",{}).get("onnx",{}).get("providers",[])},
 "policy_ref": req.get("policy_ref")
 }

 outdir = os.path.join(self.root, job_id)
 os.makedirs(outdir, exist_ok=True)

 # Write model_card.json
 with open(os.path.join(outdir, "model_card.json"), "w") as f:
 json.dump(card, f, indent=2)

 # Emit JSON-LD
 card_jsonld = model_card_to_jsonld(card, context_url="/ontology/contexts/atlas.jsonld")
 with open(os.path.join(outdir, "model_card.jsonld"), "w") as f:
 json.dump(card_jsonld, f, indent=2)

 # SHACL validation (Turtle)
 turtle = model_card_to_turtle(card, ontology_ttl="ontology/atlas.ttl")
 conforms, report = validate_trial_graph_turtle(
 turtle,
 shapes_path="ontology/shacl/constraints.ttl",
 ontology_path="ontology/atlas.ttl"
 )

 if not conforms:
 msg = f"SHACL validation failed for job {job_id}:\n{report}"
 if self.shacl_enforce:
 # hard-fail promotion
 raise ValueError(msg)
 else:
 # log and continue (non-blocking)
 logging.warning(msg)

 return card

If you prefer to control this via config instead of CLI:

4) Observability & logs
 When failing on SHACL enforcement, return a TRIT_FALSE in the promotion stage (or set job state to FAILEDwith reason SHACL_VIOLATION) so your Grafana/Loki panels reflect the failure.
 When logging only, emit a warning to stdout (promtail  Loki) and add a status="SHACL_WARN" into the model card info for traceability (optional):
if not conforms and not self.shacl_enforce:
 card.setdefault("info", {})["shacl"] = "WARNING"
 with open(os.path.join(outdir, "model_card.json"), "w") as f:
 json.dump(card, f, indent=2)

5) CLI usage examples
# Block promotions on any SHACL violation (default)
python cmd/atlasd/main.py --shacl-enforce=true

# Allow promotions but log violations
python cmd/atlasd/main.py --shacl-enforce=false

# or via env
ATLAS_SHACL_ENFORCE=false python cmd/atlasd/main.py

Why this helps
 Safety: you can start with non-blocking SHACL (observe), then flip to blocking once your shapes are stable.
 Clarity: a single CLI switch keeps deployment scripts simple, and the choice is visible in logs + metric panels.
If you want, I can also add a tiny unit test that toggles the enforcement flag and asserts promote() raises on violation vs. logs and continues.

Heres a tiny pytest that toggles the enforcement flag and verifies Registry.promote() either raises on SHACL violations or logs & continues, using a simple monkeypatch so we dont depend on the full SHACL stack during the unit test.
Drop this file in your repo as atlas_service/tests/test_shacl_enforce.py.
# atlas_service/tests/test_shacl_enforce.py
import json
import logging
import os
import time
import pytest

from types import SimpleNamespace

# Import your Registry and the function we will monkeypatch
from atlas.registry import Registry
import atlas.semantics.shacl_validate as shacl_mod

@pytest.fixture
def tmp_artifacts(tmp_path):
 # A fresh artifacts root for each test
 return str(tmp_path / "artifacts")

@pytest.fixture
def minimal_req():
 # Minimal request dict similar to what Daemon passes to Registry.promote()
 return {
 "entrypoint": "bert",
 "task": "nlp-clf",
 "tenant": "acme",
 "train": {"uri": "s3://bucket/train.parquet"},
 "val": {"uri": "s3://bucket/val.parquet"},
 "dataset_hash": "hash123",
 "export": {"onnx": {"path": "s3://bucket/model.onnx", "opset": 17, "providers": ["CPUExecutionProvider"]}},
 "policy_ref": "pol-v1"
 }

@pytest.fixture
def minimal_best():
 return {"metrics": {"f1": 0.81}}

def test_promote_blocks_on_shacl_violation(tmp_artifacts, minimal_req, minimal_best, monkeypatch, caplog):
 """
 When shacl_enforce=True, a SHACL violation should raise ValueError and prevent promotion.
 """
 # Monkeypatch the SHACL validator to force a violation (False, "report...")
 monkeypatch.setattr(shacl_mod, "validate_trial_graph_turtle",
 lambda ttl, shapes_path=None, ontology_path=None: (False, "SHACL VIOLATION REPORT"))

 reg = Registry(tmp_artifacts, shacl_enforce=True)

 with pytest.raises(ValueError) as exc:
 reg.promote(job_id="job-123", req=minimal_req, best=minimal_best)
 assert "SHACL validation failed" in str(exc.value)

 # Model card should not exist because promotion was blocked
 outdir = os.path.join(tmp_artifacts, "job-123")
 assert not os.path.exists(os.path.join(outdir, "model_card.jsonld"))

def test_promote_logs_on_shacl_violation(tmp_artifacts, minimal_req, minimal_best, monkeypatch, caplog):
 """
 When shacl_enforce=False, a SHACL violation should be logged (warning) but promotion should continue.
 """
 monkeypatch.setattr(shacl_mod, "validate_trial_graph_turtle",
 lambda ttl, shapes_path=None, ontology_path=None: (False, "SHACL VIOLATION REPORT"))

 reg = Registry(tmp_artifacts, shacl_enforce=False)

 with caplog.at_level(logging.WARNING):
 card = reg.promote(job_id="job-456", req=minimal_req, best=minimal_best)

 # Card should be written despite the violation
 outdir = os.path.join(tmp_artifacts, "job-456")
 assert os.path.exists(os.path.join(outdir, "model_card.json"))
 assert os.path.exists(os.path.join(outdir, "model_card.jsonld"))

 # Verify we logged a warning about SHACL
 assert any("SHACL validation failed for job job-456" in rec.message for rec in caplog.records if rec.levelno == logging.WARNING)

 # Optional: confirm returned card is the JSON dict we expect
 assert card["model"]["id"] == "job-456"
 assert card["metrics"]["f1"] == pytest.approx(0.81)
What this test does
 Blocks mode (shacl_enforce=True): we monkeypatch validate_trial_graph_turtle() to return (False, "&"), then assert Registry.promote() raises ValueError and does not produce model_card.jsonld.
 Logs mode (shacl_enforce=False): same violation, but promote() writes model_card.json and model_card.jsonld and emits a warning (captured via caplog).

 Add the SHACL/ontology files (from the A2A+ontology bundle) to your repo so the import paths are valid in normal (non-monkeypatched) runs.
If you want, I can also wire a second test that exercises the successful case (i.e., SHACL returns True) and asserts promotion completes silently (no warning, files written), plus a CLI integration test that spawns the daemon with --shacl-enforce=false and confirms a violation logs rather than blocks.

Absolutelylets put everything behind TritRPC and make the promotion/validation path enforceable via the TritRPC API (not imports or CLI shortcuts). Below are drop-in patches and tests so:
 Promotion happens only through the TritRPC service method;
 SHACL enforcement and failures are reported as TRIT codes in the API response (no leaking exceptions);
 You get unit tests that call the TritRPC servicer methods directly (no hidden backdoors), so the entire workflow stays protocol-first.

1) TritRPC mapping for promotion (block/log SHACL via Trit)
Patch: atlas/rpc/server.py  adjust RegistryServicer.PromoteArtifact so it never raises, and always returns a TritStatus:
# atlas/rpc/server.py (inside RegistryServicer)
class RegistryServicer(atlas_pb2_grpc.RegistryServiceServicer):
 def __init__(self, daemon): self.daemon = daemon

 def PromoteArtifact(self, req: atlas_pb2.JobId, ctx):
 # Pull state and request
 st = self.daemon.status.get(req.id, {})
 # If your daemon stores the original req under info.req and best metrics under info.best_metrics:
 original_req = st.get("info", {}).get("req", {}) or {}
 best = {"metrics": st.get("info", {}).get("best_metrics", {})}

 # Try to promote via registry, catch SHACL enforcement exceptions
 try:
 card = self.daemon.registry.promote(req.id, original_req, best)
 # Success case (TRIT TRUE). If registry logged a SHACL warn (non-enforce),
 # you can include that hint in 'info' for observability:
 info = {"model_card": f"{self.daemon.registry.root}/{req.id}/model_card.json"}
 # If you wrote a "shacl" warning flag into the card, include it:
 if card.get("info", {}).get("shacl") == "WARNING":
 info["shacl"] = "WARNING"
 return atlas_pb2.Artifact(
 id=req.id,
 uri=f"{self.daemon.registry.root}/{req.id}",
 task=card["model"].get("task",""),
 family=card["model"].get("family",""),
 dataset=card["data"].get("train_uri",""),
 metrics=card.get("metrics",{}),
 onnx_uri=card.get("onnx",{}).get("path",""),
 ledger_uri=f"{self.daemon.registry.root}/{req.id}/ledger.json",
 created_at=card["model"].get("created_at","")
 )
 except ValueError as e:
 # SHACL violation with enforce=True  TRIT FALSE
 # Reply via a minimal artifact and set TritStatus on the Status wrapper
 # (If you prefer, add a separate method that returns {trit,status,artifact} together)
 # Here: we return an error via a Status RPC, or you can adjust the proto to include a TritStatus on Artifact
 # For now, surface as a Status reply pattern:
 status = atlas_pb2.Status(state="PROMOTION_FAILED", info={"error": str(e)})
 # turn it into a gRPC error OR wrap in a new RPC; simplest: raise a gRPC error with metadata
 context = ctx
 context.set_trailing_metadata((("x-trit-code","FALSE"),("x-trit-reason","SHACL_VIOLATION"),))
 context.abort(grpc.StatusCode.FAILED_PRECONDITION, f"SHACL_VIOLATION: {e}")
If youd rather always return a structured payload with TritStatus, add a dedicated RPC that responds with StatusReply { trit, status } for promotion. The above shows how to abort with Trit metadata so clients can map it to TRIT=FALSE.
Alternative (preferred, consistent pattern)  add a Promote RPC that returns a StatusReply instead of trying to encode errors in Artifact:
// in atlas.proto
rpc Promote(JobId) returns (StatusReply) {
 option (google.api.http) = { post: "/v1/promote/{id}" };
}
And in server:
def Promote(self, req, ctx):

Whats inside this add-on
Containerization

How to use
0. Build & push images
# Replace org
export ORG=your-org
docker build -t ghcr.io/$ORG/tritfabric-server:latest -f Dockerfile.server .
docker build -t ghcr.io/$ORG/tritfabric-sse:latest -f Dockerfile.sse .
docker build -t ghcr.io/$ORG/tritfabric-ssegw:latest -f Dockerfile.ssegw .
docker build -t ghcr.io/$ORG/tritfabric-tools:latest -f Dockerfile.tools .
docker push ghcr.io/$ORG/tritfabric-*:latest
Or rely on GitHub Actions: push to main and publish.yml will build/push to GHCR automatically.
0. Deploy with Helm (optional)
helm install tritfabric-server charts/tritfabric-server \
 --set image.repository=ghcr.io/$ORG/tritfabric-server \
 --set image.tag=latest
Or use the existing Kustomize under deploy/argo/apps/tritfabric-services/.
0. ArgoCD sync
 Add your repo URL in deploy/argo/argocd/applicationset.yaml and apply the files; ArgoCD automates sync to dev/stage/prod namespaces.
0. Rollouts
 Canary release ramps based on Prom SLOs (LLM stream p95 & error ratio).
 Add the promotion gates Job (from tritfabric-tools) to the Rollouts analysis step if you want both metric & gate checks during canary.
0. Secrets
 Put AEAD key in Vault under tritfabric/aead (property base64), apply the ExternalSecret, and restart gateways to enable signature verification.
